%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Numerical continuation of the reduced flavor toy model}

We continued the reduced pre-EWSB flavor analysis at the purely numerical level,
keeping the common family-space logic
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{fam}} \cong \mathbb C^3,
\qquad
V_{\mathrm{CKM}} = U_u^\dagger U_d,
\]
and asking only the following concrete question:
\[
\text{Can the current reduced two-texture toy ansatz produce CKM-like mixing, in particular the Cabibbo angle?}
\]

Since the original exploratory scripts were not available in the present session,
we reconstructed a minimal midpoint-overlap toy model consistent with the master contents.
Let \(X_a\in\mathbb R^3\) (\(a=1,2,3\)) be the family centers, let \(\sigma\) be the Gaussian width,
and define the overlap factor
\[
S_{ab} = \exp\!\left(-\frac{|X_a-X_b|^2}{4\sigma^2}\right),
\qquad
m_{ab}:=\frac{X_a+X_b}{2}.
\]
We used the radial defect profile factor
\[
f_R(x)=\frac{4R^2}{\bigl(|x|^2+R^2\bigr)^2},
\]
and the reconstructed kernels
\begin{align}
(B_0)_{ab} &= S_{ab}\, f_R(m_{ab}),\\
(B_1)_{ab} &= \kappa_Y\, S_{ab}\, f_R(m_{ab})
\exp\!\left(-\frac{|m_{ab}-C_Y|^2}{2\ell_Y^2}\right),\\
(B_H)_{ab} &= \kappa_H\, S_{ab}\, f_R(m_{ab})
\exp\!\left(-\frac{|m_{ab}-C_H|^2}{2\ell_H^2}\right).
\end{align}
Thus
\[
H_u = B_0-\frac23 B_1,
\qquad
H_d = B_0+\frac13 B_1,
\qquad
M_u = H_u+B_H,
\qquad
M_d = H_d-B_H.
\]

We then diagonalized
\[
U_u^\dagger M_u U_u = \operatorname{diag}(m_u,m_c,m_t),
\qquad
U_d^\dagger M_d U_d = \operatorname{diag}(m_d,m_s,m_b),
\]
and read off
\[
V_{\mathrm{CKM}} = U_u^\dagger U_d.
\]

The numerical target values were taken from the 2025 PDG global-fit magnitudes:
\[
|V_{us}|=0.22501,\qquad
|V_{cb}|=0.04183,\qquad
|V_{ub}|=0.003732.
\]

A constrained random-plus-refinement search produced the best reconstructed fit
\[
|V_{\mathrm{CKM}}|_{\mathrm{toy}}
\approx
\begin{pmatrix}
0.97373 & 0.22770 & 0.00312\\
0.22762 & 0.97281 & 0.04269\\
0.00669 & 0.04228 & 0.99908
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Hence
\[
|V_{us}|_{\mathrm{toy}}=0.22770,\qquad
|V_{cb}|_{\mathrm{toy}}=0.04269,\qquad
|V_{ub}|_{\mathrm{toy}}=0.00312.
\]

This has the following immediate consequences.

First,
\[
|V_{us}|_{\mathrm{toy}}
\]
reaches the observed Cabibbo scale.
Therefore the current two-texture reduced ansatz is \emph{not}
structurally incapable of producing the Cabibbo angle.

Second, the full CKM hierarchy
\[
|V_{us}| \gg |V_{cb}| \gg |V_{ub}|
\]
is reproduced numerically in the reduced toy model.

Third, the best-fit matrices are genuinely misaligned.
For the best point,
\[
B_0 \approx
\begin{pmatrix}
0.02479 & 0.06702 & 0.12594\\
0.06702 & 0.09241 & 0.29356\\
0.12594 & 0.29356 & 0.49214
\end{pmatrix},
\]
\[
B_1 \approx
\begin{pmatrix}
1.19\times 10^{-10} & 5.41\times 10^{-6} & 5.89\times 10^{-6}\\
5.41\times 10^{-6} & 1.03\times 10^{-3} & 6.54\times 10^{-3}\\
5.89\times 10^{-6} & 6.54\times 10^{-3} & 5.20\times 10^{-3}
\end{pmatrix},
\]
\[
B_H \approx
\begin{pmatrix}
0.00513 & 0.01234 & 0.00942\\
0.01234 & 0.00026 & 0.00095\\
0.00942 & 0.00095 & 0.00055
\end{pmatrix},
\]
with
\[
\|[B_0,B_1]\|_F \approx 2.79\times 10^{-3},
\qquad
\|[M_u,M_d]\|_F \approx 2.83\times 10^{-2}.
\]
So the CKM-like mixing is produced by genuine noncommutativity, not by a numerical artifact of nearly degenerate matrices.

However, the current ansatz still has two clear limitations.

First, although \(|V_{us}|\) and \(|V_{cb}|\) can be matched well,
\(|V_{ub}|\) tends to come out slightly too small.
This indicates that the present two-texture ansatz has enough freedom to generate
the dominant \(1\text{--}2\) and \(2\text{--}3\) mixings, but likely not enough independent
control over the \(1\text{--}3\) sector.

Second, in the present reconstruction all matrices are real symmetric,
so the model can fit only CKM magnitudes, not the physical Dirac CP phase.
A genuinely complex texture is required for that.

Therefore the honest status is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the current reduced two-texture toy model is sufficient to produce Cabibbo-scale mixing and the CKM hierarchy,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{it is not yet sufficient for a full precision CKM fit with CP violation.}
}
\]

The most economical next enlargement is to keep the same family-space reduction
but replace the single \(B_H\) texture by either
\[
B_H \;\to\; B_H^{(1)} + B_H^{(2)},
\]
with two displaced Higgs-like kernels, or
\[
B_1 \;\to\; B_1^{(1)} + e^{i\phi}\,B_1^{(2)},
\]
so that the \(1\text{--}3\) sector and the physical CKM phase can be adjusted independently.

\section{Final summary}

The reduced TECT flavor problem has now passed a nontrivial numerical test.

Using a reconstructed midpoint-overlap toy realization of
\[
M_u = \left(B_0-\frac23 B_1\right)+B_H,
\qquad
M_d = \left(B_0+\frac13 B_1\right)-B_H,
\qquad
V_{\mathrm{CKM}}=U_u^\dagger U_d,
\]
we find explicit parameter points with
\[
|V_{us}| \approx 0.228,\qquad
|V_{cb}| \approx 0.0427,\qquad
|V_{ub}| \approx 0.0031,
\]
which is already close to the observed CKM hierarchy.

Therefore the present two-texture reduced ansatz is sufficient to generate:

\begin{enumerate}
\item nontrivial quark-sector misalignment,
\item Cabibbo-scale mixing,
\item the qualitative CKM hierarchy
\[
|V_{us}| \gg |V_{cb}| \gg |V_{ub}|.
\]
\end{enumerate}

So the statement
\[
\text{``the current toy ansatz cannot generate Cabibbo''}
\]
is false.

The honest remaining limitations are:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(|V_{ub}|\) tends to be slightly underestimated;
\item the present real-symmetric reconstruction does not generate a physical CKM CP phase.
\end{enumerate}

Hence the best current conclusion is
\[
\boxed{
\text{two-texture TECT flavor reduction is sufficient at the hierarchy/Cabibbo level,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{an enlarged complex texture is likely needed for full CKM precision and CP violation.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Interpretation of the current CKM refinement run}

We analyze the current best point obtained from the exploratory refinement fitter:
\[
|V_{us}|=0.208440,\qquad
|V_{cb}|=0.045425,\qquad
|V_{ub}|=0.003730,
\]
with target values
\[
|V_{us}|^{\rm tar}=0.225000,\qquad
|V_{cb}|^{\rm tar}=0.041000,\qquad
|V_{ub}|^{\rm tar}=0.003500.
\]

The deviations are
\[
\Delta |V_{us}| = -0.016560,
\qquad
\Delta |V_{cb}| = +0.004425,
\qquad
\Delta |V_{ub}| = +0.000230,
\]
or in relative form
\[
\frac{\Delta |V_{us}|}{|V_{us}|^{\rm tar}} \approx -7.36\%,
\qquad
\frac{\Delta |V_{cb}|}{|V_{cb}|^{\rm tar}} \approx +10.79\%,
\qquad
\frac{\Delta |V_{ub}|}{|V_{ub}|^{\rm tar}} \approx +6.58\%.
\]

Thus the present best point already reproduces the qualitative CKM hierarchy,
but the dominant remaining mismatch is clearly the Cabibbo entry:
\[
|V_{us}| \text{ is still too small.}
\]

The full absolute CKM matrix is
\[
|V_{\rm CKM}|
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0.978028 & 0.20844021 & 0.00373027\\
0.20806076 & 0.97706053 & 0.04542511\\
0.01311312 & 0.04365091 & 0.99896078
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
This shows that the model is far from the trivial identity limit and already
produces a realistic hierarchical mixing pattern.

The misalignment diagnostics are
\[
\|[B_0,B_1]\|_F = 2.76446644\times 10^{-2},
\qquad
\|[M_u,M_d]\|_F = 3.62498081\times 10^{-2},
\]
while the numerical unitarity error is
\[
\|V^\dagger V-\mathbf 1\| \sim 5.62\times 10^{-16}.
\]
Therefore the mixing is genuine and numerically stable:
it is produced by actual noncommutativity of the sectoral family operators,
not by diagonalization noise.

The family centers are
\[
X_1=-1.42549,\qquad
X_2=-0.28092,\qquad
X_3=2.85749,
\qquad
\sigma=1.488486.
\]
Hence the pairwise separations are
\[
d_{12}\approx 1.14457,\qquad
d_{23}\approx 3.13841,\qquad
d_{13}\approx 4.28298.
\]
Using the Gaussian overlap estimate
\[
S_{ab}\sim \exp\!\left(-\frac{d_{ab}^2}{4\sigma^2}\right),
\]
one finds approximately
\[
S_{12}\approx 0.863,\qquad
S_{23}\approx 0.329,\qquad
S_{13}\approx 0.126.
\]

This is exactly the geometric pattern expected for hierarchical flavor mixing:
\[
1\text{--}2 \text{ overlap is strong},\qquad
2\text{--}3 \text{ overlap is moderate},\qquad
1\text{--}3 \text{ overlap is suppressed}.
\]
Hence the current best point strongly supports the interpretation that
the reduced TECT flavor ansatz naturally produces CKM-like hierarchy from
family-space localization plus sectoral misalignment.

The sectoral eigenvalues are
\[
m_u^{\rm toy}\sim (0.01922,\ 0.10373,\ 0.80661),
\qquad
m_d^{\rm toy}\sim (0.01327,\ 0.06098,\ 0.85649).
\]
Although these are not yet directly meaningful as physical quark masses,
they do show that the toy model already generates a nondegenerate hierarchical spectrum.

The honest interpretation is therefore:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the current reduced ansatz successfully produces nontrivial hierarchical CKM-like mixing,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{it still does not achieve a precise simultaneous fit, mainly because } |V_{us}| \text{ remains too small.}
}
\]

A plausible structural interpretation is that the present texture family does not yet
have enough independent freedom to increase the \(1\text{--}2\) mixing angle
without simultaneously distorting the \(2\text{--}3\) sector.
However, this should be treated as a hypothesis suggested by the present point,
not yet as a theorem.

Therefore the immediate next numerical task should not be another blind global run.
Instead, one should perform a local sensitivity audit around the current best point:
\begin{enumerate}
\item freeze the family geometry \((X_a,\sigma,R)\) near the present optimum;
\item vary only the texture parameters \((\epsilon,\delta,\mathrm{amps}_H,\mathrm{phases}_H)\);
\item measure
\[
\frac{\partial |V_{us}|}{\partial p_i},
\qquad
\frac{\partial |V_{cb}|}{\partial p_i},
\qquad
\frac{\partial |V_{ub}|}{\partial p_i};
\]
\item identify whether there exists a local direction in parameter space that increases
\(|V_{us}|\) while leaving \(|V_{cb}|\) nearly fixed.
\end{enumerate}

If no such direction exists in a robust neighborhood of the present optimum,
then the correct conclusion will be that the current ansatz is too rigid and must be enlarged,
for example by adding:
\[
B_H \to B_H^{(1)}+B_H^{(2)}+B_H^{(3)},
\]
or by allowing a genuinely complex hypercharge-sensitive texture
\[
B_1 \to B_1^{(1)} + e^{i\phi} B_1^{(2)}.
\]
Such an enlargement would provide additional control over the \(1\text{--}2\) and \(2\text{--}3\)
sectors and, eventually, over the physical CKM phase as well.

\section{Final summary}

The current refinement run gives
\[
|V_{us}|=0.208440,\qquad
|V_{cb}|=0.045425,\qquad
|V_{ub}|=0.003730,
\]
with excellent numerical unitarity and clearly nonzero commutator diagnostics:
\[
\|[B_0,B_1]\|_F>0,
\qquad
\|[M_u,M_d]\|_F>0.
\]

Therefore the reduced TECT flavor model has passed the following nontrivial test:
\[
\boxed{
\text{it genuinely produces hierarchical CKM-like mixing from family-space misalignment.}
}
\]

What is not yet achieved is a precise simultaneous fit.
The dominant remaining problem is
\[
\boxed{
|V_{us}| \text{ is still too small.}
}
\]

The current best-fit geometry has strong \(1\text{--}2\) overlap,
moderate \(2\text{--}3\) overlap, and suppressed \(1\text{--}3\) overlap,
which explains why the CKM hierarchy already emerges naturally.

Hence the honest current status is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{hierarchy-level success is real,}
}
\qquad
\boxed{
\text{precision-level Cabibbo fitting remains open.}
}
\]

The immediate next task is a local sensitivity audit around the present best point.
If \(|V_{us}|\) cannot be increased locally without spoiling \(|V_{cb}|\),
then the present ansatz should be enlarged by an additional independent texture mode.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Complex-texture extension for CKM phase generation}

We now enlarge the reduced flavor toy ansatz by adding a single complex Hermitian texture mode.
The goal is to test whether the reduced TECT flavor model can generate not only CKM-like
magnitudes but also a nontrivial CP-violating phase.

We keep the previous real textures and replace
\[
B_1 \;\longrightarrow\; B_1^{(\mathrm{real})}+B_1^{(\mathrm{cx})},
\]
where the added complex mode is taken to be
\[
\boxed{
\bigl(B_1^{(\mathrm{cx})}\bigr)_{ab}
=
A_{ab}\Bigl[
\cos\!\bigl(q_{\rm cp}(x_a-x_b)\bigr)
+i\,\chi_{\rm cp}\sin\!\bigl(q_{\rm cp}(x_a-x_b)\bigr)
\Bigr].
}
\]
Here \(A_{ab}\) is a real symmetric envelope,
\[
A_{ab}
=
\epsilon_{\rm cp}\,
S_{ab}\,f_R(m_{ab})
\exp\!\left(
-\frac{(m_{ab}-c_{\rm cp})^2}{2\ell_{\rm cp}^2}
\right),
\]
with \(S_{ab}\) the Gaussian family overlap factor and \(m_{ab}\) the midpoint coordinate.
Because the cosine term is even and the sine term is odd under \(a\leftrightarrow b\),
one has
\[
\bigl(B_1^{(\mathrm{cx})}\bigr)_{ba}
=
\overline{\bigl(B_1^{(\mathrm{cx})}\bigr)_{ab}},
\]
so \(B_1^{(\mathrm{cx})}\) is exactly Hermitian.

The quark-sector matrices are still defined by
\[
M_u=\left(B_0-\frac23 B_1\right)+B_H,
\qquad
M_d=\left(B_0+\frac13 B_1\right)-B_H,
\]
and are therefore Hermitian as well.
We diagonalize them as
\[
U_u^\dagger M_u U_u = \operatorname{diag}(m_u,m_c,m_t),
\qquad
U_d^\dagger M_d U_d = \operatorname{diag}(m_d,m_s,m_b),
\]
and define
\[
V_{\rm CKM}=U_u^\dagger U_d.
\]

To quantify CP violation we use the Jarlskog invariant
\[
J=\operatorname{Im}\!\left(
V_{ud}V_{cs}V_{us}^\ast V_{cd}^\ast
\right),
\]
and reconstruct the standard-phase quantity \(\delta\) from
\[
J
=
c_{12}c_{23}c_{13}^2 s_{12}s_{23}s_{13}\sin\delta,
\]
with
\[
s_{13}=|V_{ub}|,\qquad
s_{12}=\frac{|V_{us}|}{\sqrt{1-|V_{ub}|^2}},\qquad
s_{23}=\frac{|V_{cb}|}{\sqrt{1-|V_{ub}|^2}}.
\]

The default numerical target is taken from the PDG 2025 global-fit CKM review:
\[
|V_{us}|=0.22501,\qquad
|V_{cb}|=0.04183,\qquad
|V_{ub}|=0.003732,
\]
\[
|V_{td}|=0.00858,\qquad
|V_{ts}|=0.04111,\qquad
J=3.12\times 10^{-5},\qquad
\delta=1.147\ \text{rad}.
\]

A representative best balanced run gives
\[
|V_{\rm CKM}|
\approx
\begin{pmatrix}
0.973044 & 0.230574 & 0.004563\\
0.230501 & 0.972253 & 0.039918\\
0.007379 & 0.039494 & 0.999193
\end{pmatrix},
\]
together with
\[
\delta \approx 0.912742\ \text{rad},
\qquad
J \approx 3.230584\times 10^{-5}.
\]

This result is significant for two reasons.

First, the model now enters a genuinely CP-violating regime:
\[
\boxed{
J\neq 0,\qquad \delta\neq 0.
}
\]
Hence the reduced TECT flavor model with one additional complex Hermitian texture
is capable of producing a physical CKM-phase surrogate, not merely real mixing angles.

Second, the fitted Jarlskog invariant is already close to the phenomenological target:
\[
J_{\rm toy}\approx 3.23\times 10^{-5}
\quad \text{vs.} \quad
J_{\rm target}\approx 3.12\times 10^{-5}.
\]
Thus the overall size of CP violation can already be reproduced with only one extra complex mode.

However, the same run also shows the remaining limitation of the ansatz.
Although the fit is qualitatively good, the simultaneous precision fit of
\[
(|V_{us}|,\ |V_{cb}|,\ |V_{ub}|,\ \delta)
\]
is not yet achieved.
In the current best balanced point,
\[
|V_{us}| \text{ is slightly high},\qquad
|V_{cb}| \text{ is slightly low},\qquad
|V_{ub}| \text{ is somewhat high},\qquad
\delta \text{ is somewhat low}.
\]

Moreover, another search basin was found in which
\[
\delta \approx 1.144\ \text{rad}
\]
is almost perfect, but
\[
|V_{ub}| \approx 0.0064
\]
becomes too large.
This indicates that the present ansatz has enough freedom to generate either
nearly correct phase or nearly correct magnitudes, but not yet enough freedom
to fit all observables simultaneously with high precision.

The commutator diagnostics remain clearly nonzero,
\[
\|[B_0,B_1]\|_F \approx 1.07\times 10^{-1},
\qquad
\|[M_u,M_d]\|_F \approx 1.12\times 10^{-1},
\]
while the numerical unitarity error is tiny,
\[
\|V^\dagger V-\mathbf 1\| \approx 7.1\times 10^{-16}.
\]
Therefore the complex phase is produced by genuine sectoral noncommutativity,
not by numerical instability.

The honest current conclusion is
\[
\boxed{
\text{one extra complex Hermitian texture is sufficient to generate a nontrivial CKM phase and a realistic }J,
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{it is still not sufficient for a fully precise simultaneous fit of all CKM magnitudes and the phase.}
}
\]

The most economical next step is not a radical reparametrization,
but a minimally enlarged ansatz such as
\[
B_H \to B_H^{(1)}+B_H^{(2)}+B_H^{(3)},
\]
or
\[
B_1 \to B_1^{(\mathrm{real})}+B_1^{(\mathrm{cx},1)}+B_1^{(\mathrm{cx},2)},
\]
so that the magnitude sector and the CP phase can be tuned more independently.

\section{Final summary}

We extended the reduced TECT flavor toy model by adding one complex Hermitian texture mode to \(B_1\).
This preserves Hermiticity of \(M_u\) and \(M_d\), while allowing genuinely complex flavor misalignment.

The main result is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{with one extra complex mode, the model can generate }J\neq 0\text{ and }\delta\neq 0.
}
\]

A representative balanced fit gives
\[
|V_{us}| \approx 0.2306,\qquad
|V_{cb}| \approx 0.0399,\qquad
|V_{ub}| \approx 0.00456,
\]
\[
\delta \approx 0.913\ \text{rad},\qquad
J \approx 3.23\times 10^{-5}.
\]

Thus the model already reproduces the correct order of magnitude of CP violation:
\[
J_{\rm toy}\sim J_{\rm exp}.
\]

However, a precise simultaneous fit of all CKM magnitudes and the phase is still not achieved.
The current ansatz is therefore strong enough to demonstrate genuine emergent CP structure,
but not yet strong enough for precision phenomenology.

Hence the honest status is
\[
\boxed{
\text{CP violation is now numerically present in the reduced TECT flavor model,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{one additional complex texture mode beyond this is likely needed for a precision CKM+phase fit.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Local sensitivity audit of the one-complex-mode CKM ansatz}

We now analyze the local structure of the reduced TECT flavor ansatz with one additional complex Hermitian texture mode.
The purpose is not another blind global search, but a direct local audit of whether the current ansatz
can simultaneously improve the CKM magnitudes and the CP-violating phase near the current best point.

The current best balanced fit is
\[
|V_{\rm CKM}|
\approx
\begin{pmatrix}
0.973044 & 0.230574 & 0.004563\\
0.230501 & 0.972253 & 0.039918\\
0.007379 & 0.039494 & 0.999193
\end{pmatrix},
\]
with
\[
\delta \approx 0.912742,
\qquad
J \approx 3.230584\times 10^{-5},
\qquad
\mathrm{score}=4.548907.
\]

To test the local flexibility of the ansatz, we performed two complementary scans:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a one-parameter finite scan, in which each parameter was perturbed by a small \(\pm\) step and the responses of
\[
|V_{us}|,\ |V_{cb}|,\ |V_{ub}|,\ \delta,\ J,\ \mathrm{score}
\]
were recorded;

\item a local random-neighborhood scan consisting of \(6000\) small perturbations around the current best point.
\end{enumerate}

The most important result is the following.

Among the \(6000\) local random perturbations, the best improved point has
\[
\mathrm{score}=2.788096,
\]
with
\[
|V_{us}|=0.219799,\qquad
|V_{cb}|=0.044385,\qquad
|V_{ub}|=0.003374,
\]
\[
\delta = 1.172249,\qquad
J = 2.956551\times 10^{-5}.
\]

Thus the score can indeed be improved locally, and the phase can even become more realistic.
However, this improvement occurs only at the price of reducing the Cabibbo entry:
\[
|V_{us}|:\ 0.230574 \longrightarrow 0.219799.
\]

This already suggests a local tension:
the dominant nearby descent directions improve the phase sector and \(|V_{ub}|\),
but move \(|V_{us}|\) in the wrong direction.

This conclusion becomes much stronger when one inspects the whole neighborhood sample.
In the local scan we find
\[
\boxed{
\#\left\{
\Delta\mathrm{score}<0\ \text{and}\ \Delta|V_{us}|>0
\right\}=0.
}
\]
That is, among all \(6000\) tested local perturbations, there is not a single point that both
improves the total score and increases \(|V_{us}|\).

This is not a proof of impossibility, but it is strong numerical evidence that the present ansatz
has reached a local Pareto wall:
\[
\text{near the current optimum, improving the global fit tends to require lowering } |V_{us}|.
\]

Conversely, local points with increased \(|V_{us}|\) do exist, but they worsen the overall fit.
The best local point with
\[
\Delta |V_{us}|>0
\]
has
\[
\mathrm{score}=8.214184,
\]
with
\[
|V_{us}|=0.231139,\qquad
|V_{cb}|=0.046548,\qquad
|V_{ub}|=0.004584,
\]
\[
\delta=1.421370,\qquad
J=4.7\times 10^{-5},
\]
which shows that the increase of the Cabibbo entry is accompanied by noticeable distortions in
other observables.

The one-parameter finite scan supports the same interpretation.
The strongest score-improving one-step moves are approximately:
\[
q_{H,2}\downarrow,\qquad
q_{H,1}\uparrow,\qquad
\kappa_H\uparrow,\qquad
\mathrm{amp}_{H,1}\uparrow,\qquad
\phi_{H,2}\uparrow.
\]
But these directions almost uniformly decrease \(|V_{us}|\).
Hence the local best-response directions of the current ansatz are not aligned with the
remaining Cabibbo improvement that is still needed.

A linearized local influence analysis also shows that the same small set of parameters controls both
the magnitude and phase sectors.
The dominant local drivers of \(|V_{us}|\) are
\[
\kappa_Y,\qquad x_3,\qquad \delta_1,\qquad \ell_{\rm cp},\qquad \epsilon_2,\qquad \mathrm{amp}_{\rm cp},\qquad q_{\rm cp},
\]
while the dominant local drivers of \(\delta\) are
\[
x_3,\qquad \epsilon_2,\qquad \kappa_Y,\qquad x_2,\qquad \ell_{\rm cp},\qquad q_{\rm cp}.
\]
In particular, the overlap
\[
\{\kappa_Y,\ \epsilon_2,\ \ell_{\rm cp},\ q_{\rm cp},\ x_3\}
\]
shows that the phase-sensitive and Cabibbo-sensitive directions are still strongly entangled.

Therefore the honest conclusion is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{one additional complex Hermitian texture mode is sufficient to generate } J\neq 0 \text{ and } \delta\neq 0,
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{it is not locally flexible enough to improve the full CKM+phase fit without Cabibbo tension.}
}
\]

The most natural next step is therefore not a larger blind search, but a minimal ansatz enlargement
that decouples the Cabibbo-sensitive sector from the CP-phase-sensitive sector.
The most economical possibilities are:
\[
B_1 \to B_1^{(\mathrm{real})}+B_1^{(\mathrm{cx},1)}+B_1^{(\mathrm{cx},2)},
\]
or
\[
B_H \to B_H^{(1)}+B_H^{(2)}+B_H^{(3)},
\]
so that the \(1\text{--}2\) mixing, the \(1\text{--}3\) leakage, and the CP phase can be tuned more independently.

\section{Final summary}

We performed a local sensitivity audit around the current best point of the reduced TECT flavor ansatz
with one additional complex Hermitian texture mode.

The audit shows three clear facts.

First,
\[
\boxed{
J\neq 0 \quad \text{and} \quad \delta\neq 0
}
\]
are robustly present, so the ansatz genuinely enters a CP-violating CKM regime.

Second, local score improvements do exist, but they systematically tend to reduce the Cabibbo entry:
\[
|V_{us}| \downarrow
\quad \text{when} \quad
\mathrm{score}\downarrow.
\]

Third, in a neighborhood scan of \(6000\) perturbations, no sample was found with
\[
\Delta \mathrm{score}<0
\quad \text{and} \quad
\Delta |V_{us}|>0.
\]
This is strong numerical evidence that the present ansatz has reached a local Pareto wall.

Hence the honest current status is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{one complex texture mode is enough for emergent CP violation,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{it is still too rigid for a locally unconstrained precision CKM+phase fit.}
}
\]

Therefore the next correct move is a minimal ansatz enlargement that separates
Cabibbo control from CP-phase control.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Two-complex-mode continuation of the reduced CKM+phase search}

We extended the reduced TECT flavor toy ansatz by allowing two independent complex Hermitian texture modes in \(B_1\):
\[
B_1
=
B_1^{(\mathrm{real})}
+
B_1^{(\mathrm{cx},1)}
+
B_1^{(\mathrm{cx},2)}.
\]
Each complex mode is taken in the Hermitian form
\[
\bigl(B_1^{(\mathrm{cx},i)}\bigr)_{ab}
=
A^{(i)}_{ab}
\left[
\cos\!\bigl(q_i(x_a-x_b)\bigr)
+
i\,\chi_i \sin\!\bigl(q_i(x_a-x_b)\bigr)
\right],
\qquad i=1,2,
\]
with real symmetric envelope
\[
A^{(i)}_{ab}
=
\epsilon_i\,
S_{ab}\,f_R(m_{ab})
\exp\!\left(
-\frac{(m_{ab}-c_i)^2}{2\ell_i^2}
\right).
\]
Hence \(B_1\) remains Hermitian, and so do
\[
M_u=\left(B_0-\frac23 B_1\right)+B_H,
\qquad
M_d=\left(B_0+\frac13 B_1\right)-B_H.
\]

The purpose of this continuation was to test whether the previously observed tension
between the Cabibbo entry and the phase sector is genuinely removed by the second complex mode.

The first important result is that the search does find points with substantially improved score
relative to the previous one-complex-mode best fit
\[
\mathrm{score}_{\rm old}=4.548907.
\]
The best overall point found in the present continuation has
\[
\mathrm{score}_{\rm new}=2.385929,
\]
which is an improvement of approximately
\[
\frac{\mathrm{score}_{\rm old}-\mathrm{score}_{\rm new}}{\mathrm{score}_{\rm old}}
\approx 47.5\%.
\]

Its observables are
\[
|V_{us}|=0.225964,\qquad
|V_{cb}|=0.046134,\qquad
|V_{ub}|=0.003968,
\]
\[
|V_{td}|=0.010131,\qquad
|V_{ts}|=0.045182,
\]
\[
\delta = 1.307556,\qquad
J = 3.88615\times 10^{-5}.
\]

However, the crucial structural fact is that at this best overall point
\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{amp}_{\rm cp,2}=0.
}
\]
Therefore the best fit found in the enlarged search space is effectively a retuned one-complex-mode point.

This has an important methodological consequence.
It shows that the previously suspected local wall was not absolute:
better basins do exist.
But it does \emph{not} yet prove that the second complex mode is structurally required at the optimum.

The second important result is that there also exist genuinely two-mode points,
with nonzero second complex amplitude, that improve over the previous one-mode best.
The best genuine two-mode point found in this continuation has
\[
\mathrm{score}=3.015898,
\]
with
\[
|V_{us}|=0.220669,\qquad
|V_{cb}|=0.038485,\qquad
|V_{ub}|=0.003479,
\]
\[
|V_{td}|=0.008308,\qquad
|V_{ts}|=0.037738,
\]
\[
\delta = 1.314586,\qquad
J = 2.78523\times 10^{-5},
\]
and
\[
\mathrm{amp}_{\rm cp,2}=0.148203.
\]

Thus the second complex mode is not inert.
It does open nontrivial improved directions in parameter space.
Nevertheless, in the current search the globally best point still collapses back to an effective one-mode optimum.

The honest interpretation is therefore the following.

First,
\[
\boxed{
\text{the reduced TECT flavor model robustly generates nontrivial CKM magnitudes and nonzero CP structure.}
}
\]

Second,
\[
\boxed{
\text{the previously suspected local obstruction was not global: better basins exist.}
}
\]

Third,
\[
\boxed{
\text{the current evidence does not yet show that a second complex mode is strictly necessary at the optimum.}
}
\]

This means that the true current bottleneck is likely mixed:
it is not only the number of complex modes,
but also the detailed parameterization and optimization strategy.

In particular, the present numerical evidence suggests the following refined conclusion:
\[
\text{mode enlargement helps exploration,}
\qquad
\text{but structural necessity of the second mode remains unproven.}
\]

Hence the next mathematically nonredundant task is not simply to add even more modes,
but to separate two questions:

\begin{enumerate}
\item Does the one-complex-mode ansatz already admit a substantially better optimum under a stronger search?
\item If one enforces \(\mathrm{amp}_{\rm cp,2}\ge \epsilon_0>0\), does the best achievable score beat the best one-mode optimum?
\end{enumerate}

Only after this constrained comparison can one honestly claim that the second complex mode is or is not structurally necessary.

\section{Final summary}

We performed a two-complex-mode continuation of the reduced TECT CKM+phase toy search.

The main numerical findings are:

\begin{enumerate}
\item The previous best score
\[
4.548907
\]
was improved substantially to
\[
2.385929.
\]

\item The best overall point has
\[
|V_{us}|=0.225964,\quad
|V_{cb}|=0.046134,\quad
|V_{ub}|=0.003968,\quad
\delta=1.307556,\quad
J=3.88615\times 10^{-5},
\]
but also
\[
\mathrm{amp}_{\rm cp,2}=0,
\]
so it is effectively a retuned one-complex-mode optimum.

\item The best genuinely two-mode point has
\[
\mathrm{score}=3.015898,
\]
with nonzero second complex amplitude,
and it also improves over the previous one-mode best.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the correct current conclusion is
\[
\boxed{
\text{better CKM+phase basins do exist, so the previously suspected local wall was not absolute.}
}
\]
But also
\[
\boxed{
\text{the present evidence still does not prove that the second complex mode is structurally required at the optimum.}
}
\]

Thus the next decisive step is a constrained comparison:
\[
\text{best one-mode optimum}
\quad \text{vs.} \quad
\text{best two-mode optimum under } \mathrm{amp}_{\rm cp,2}\ge \epsilon_0.
\]
Only that comparison can settle whether the second mode is genuinely necessary.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Constrained two-mode search and revised structural interpretation}

We performed a constrained continuation of the reduced TECT CKM+phase toy search by imposing
\[
\mathrm{amp}_{\rm cp,2}\ge \epsilon_0>0,
\]
so that the second complex Hermitian mode cannot collapse to zero.

The primary purpose was to test the previously open question:
\[
\text{is a genuinely nonzero second complex mode structurally necessary for the best CKM+phase fit?}
\]

We scanned the constrained branches
\[
\epsilon_0 \in \{0.01,0.02,0.05,0.10,0.15\}.
\]

The best constrained points found are:

\[
\epsilon_0=0.01:
\quad
\mathrm{score}\approx 3.4434,
\quad
|V_{us}|\approx 0.22588,
\quad
|V_{cb}|\approx 0.04165,
\quad
|V_{ub}|\approx 0.00232,
\quad
\delta\approx 0.9770.
\]

\[
\epsilon_0=0.02:
\quad
\mathrm{score}\approx 2.8529,
\quad
|V_{us}|\approx 0.22342,
\quad
|V_{cb}|\approx 0.03652,
\quad
|V_{ub}|\approx 0.00366,
\quad
\delta\approx 1.2691.
\]

\[
\epsilon_0=0.05:
\quad
\mathrm{score}\approx 2.7937,
\quad
|V_{us}|\approx 0.21950,
\quad
|V_{cb}|\approx 0.04281,
\quad
|V_{ub}|\approx 0.00417,
\quad
\delta\approx 1.1967.
\]

\[
\epsilon_0=0.10:
\quad
\mathrm{score}\approx 1.9933,
\quad
|V_{us}|\approx 0.22172,
\quad
|V_{cb}|\approx 0.04031,
\quad
|V_{ub}|\approx 0.00289,
\quad
\delta\approx 1.0986.
\]

\[
\epsilon_0=0.15:
\quad
\mathrm{score}\approx 2.2591,
\quad
|V_{us}|\approx 0.22294,
\quad
|V_{cb}|\approx 0.03986,
\quad
|V_{ub}|\approx 0.00487,
\quad
\delta\approx 1.2587.
\]

Thus the most promising constrained branch is
\[
\boxed{
\epsilon_0\approx 0.10.
}
\]

We then took the \(\epsilon_0=0.10\) best point and performed additional local refinements.
The best refined point found is
\[
|V_{us}| \approx 0.223279,
\qquad
|V_{cb}| \approx 0.039836,
\qquad
|V_{ub}| \approx 0.004172,
\]
\[
|V_{td}| \approx 0.008056,
\qquad
|V_{ts}| \approx 0.039235,
\]
\[
\delta \approx 1.131806,
\qquad
J \approx 3.27119\times 10^{-5},
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{score}\approx 0.717543.
}
\]

This point is substantially better than the previously recorded baselines:
\[
\mathrm{score}_{\rm old\,one\text{-}mode}\approx 4.5489,
\qquad
\mathrm{score}_{\rm old\,unconstrained\,overall}\approx 2.3859,
\qquad
\mathrm{score}_{\rm old\,best\,genuine\,two\text{-}mode}\approx 3.0159.
\]

Hence the constrained continuation proves that much better CKM+phase basins exist.

However, the structural interpretation is subtle and important.
At the new best refined point we find
\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{amp}_{\rm cp,1}=0,
\qquad
\mathrm{amp}_{\rm cp,2}\approx 0.533.
}
\]
Therefore the best current point is not a truly two-active-mode optimum.
It is effectively a \emph{single active complex mode} solution.

This implies that the current evidence does \emph{not} prove that two simultaneously active complex modes are structurally necessary.
Instead, it supports the more cautious conclusion:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the two-mode search was valuable because it opened access to a much better basin,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{the resulting optimum itself is still effectively one-complex-mode.}
}
\]

Therefore the present bottleneck is likely not the minimal number of active complex modes,
but rather the optimizer basin structure and the detailed parameterization of the single complex mode sector.

The revised honest conclusion is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item Nontrivial CKM hierarchy remains robust.
\item Nonzero CP structure (\(J\neq0\), \(\delta\neq0\)) remains robust.
\item The previously suspected local obstruction was too strong a statement.
\item The current best point does not demonstrate necessity of two active complex modes.
\item The evidence now suggests that a stronger one-mode search or a reparameterized one-mode ansatz may already achieve a near-precision fit.
\end{enumerate}

What remains visibly imperfect in the current best refined point is mainly the pair
\[
|V_{cb}| \text{ slightly low},
\qquad
|V_{ub}| \text{ slightly high}.
\]
So the next numerical objective is no longer to ``turn on more CP modes'' blindly,
but to separate the \(2\text{--}3\) control from the \(1\text{--}3\) leakage while preserving the already good
\(|V_{us}|\), \(\delta\), and \(J\).

\section{Final summary}

We forced the second complex texture mode to remain nonzero by imposing
\[
\mathrm{amp}_{\rm cp,2}\ge \epsilon_0>0,
\]
and scanned several constrained branches.

The best constrained branch occurs near
\[
\epsilon_0 \approx 0.10,
\]
and after additional local refinement yields
\[
|V_{us}| \approx 0.223279,
\qquad
|V_{cb}| \approx 0.039836,
\qquad
|V_{ub}| \approx 0.004172,
\]
\[
\delta \approx 1.131806,
\qquad
J \approx 3.27119\times 10^{-5},
\qquad
\mathrm{score}\approx 0.717543.
\]

This is substantially better than all previously recorded fits.

However, the same best point satisfies
\[
\mathrm{amp}_{\rm cp,1}=0,
\qquad
\mathrm{amp}_{\rm cp,2}\neq 0,
\]
so it is still effectively a one-active-mode solution.

Therefore the correct current conclusion is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{two-mode search is a powerful basin-finding tool,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{the current evidence still does not prove that two simultaneously active complex modes are necessary.}
}
\]

The strongest current interpretation is that the previous one-mode search underexplored the parameter space,
and that a better one-mode-like optimum exists.

The immediate remaining numerical tension is
\[
|V_{cb}| \text{ slightly low},
\qquad
|V_{ub}| \text{ slightly high},
\]
while \(|V_{us}|\), \(\delta\), and \(J\) are already close to target.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Dual-active amplitude constraint and the distinction between amplitude and actual operator activity}

We now imposed the stronger numerical constraint
\[
\mathrm{amp}_{\rm cp,1}\ge \epsilon,
\qquad
\mathrm{amp}_{\rm cp,2}\ge \epsilon,
\]
with
\[
\epsilon\in\{0.01,\,0.03,\,0.05,\,0.08,\,0.10,\,0.15,\,0.25,\,0.45\},
\]
in order to test whether two simultaneously active complex texture modes are genuinely required.

The first result is that high-quality CKM+phase fits remain available under this dual floor.
Across all tested \(\epsilon\), the best point repeatedly converges to essentially the same observable values:
\[
|V_{us}| \approx 0.223279,
\qquad
|V_{cb}| \approx 0.039836,
\qquad
|V_{ub}| \approx 0.004172,
\]
\[
|V_{td}| \approx 0.008056,
\qquad
|V_{ts}| \approx 0.039235,
\]
\[
\delta \approx 1.131806,
\qquad
J \approx 3.27119\times 10^{-5},
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{score}\approx 0.717543.
}
\]

This is substantially better than the previous baselines:
\[
\mathrm{score}_{\rm old\,one\text{-}mode}\approx 4.5489,
\qquad
\mathrm{score}_{\rm old\,unconstrained\,two\text{-}mode}\approx 2.3859,
\qquad
\mathrm{score}_{\rm old\,constrained\,amp_{cp,2}}\approx 1.9933.
\]

Hence the reduced TECT flavor toy model remains highly viable even when both complex-mode amplitudes are forced to be nonzero.

However, the decisive structural diagnostic is not the amplitudes themselves, but the actual operator sizes of the two complex modes.
For the best point at \(\epsilon=0.45\), one finds
\[
\mathrm{amp}_{\rm cp,1}=0.45,
\qquad
\mathrm{amp}_{\rm cp,2}\approx 0.532758,
\]
but
\[
\|B_1^{(\mathrm{cp},1)}\|_F \approx 9.20\times 10^{-12},
\qquad
\|B_1^{(\mathrm{cp},2)}\|_F \approx 5.07\times 10^{-2}.
\]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
\|B_1^{(\mathrm{cp},1)}\|_F \ll \|B_1^{(\mathrm{cp},2)}\|_F,
}
\]
and in practice the first complex mode is numerically negligible even though its amplitude is strictly nonzero.

This happens because the first complex mode is localized far away from the actual family-overlap region.
Its envelope parameters are approximately
\[
c_{\rm cp,1}\approx 1.94,
\qquad
\ell_{\rm cp,1}\approx 0.333,
\]
whereas the relevant midpoint coordinates satisfy
\[
m_{ab}\in[-1.89,\,-0.46].
\]
Hence the Gaussian envelope factor
\[
\exp\!\left(
-\frac{(m_{ab}-c_{\rm cp,1})^2}{2\ell_{\rm cp,1}^2}
\right)
\]
is exponentially suppressed on the entire family-support region.

Thus the dual amplitude floor does \emph{not} prove that two complex modes are simultaneously operative in the effective flavor matrix.
It only proves that both amplitudes are nonzero in parameter space.
This is a crucial distinction.

The correct conclusion is therefore:
\[
\boxed{
\text{a dual amplitude floor is insufficient as a test of genuine two-mode necessity.}
}
\]

What the calculation actually shows is the following.

First,
\[
\boxed{
\text{the reduced TECT flavor toy model robustly supports CKM hierarchy and nonzero CP structure.}
}
\]

Second,
\[
\boxed{
\text{good fits persist even when both complex amplitudes are forced to be positive.}
}
\]

Third,
\[
\boxed{
\text{the current optimum is still effectively a one-contributing-complex-mode solution.}
}
\]

Therefore the next mathematically honest test of genuine two-mode necessity is not
\[
\mathrm{amp}_{\rm cp,1},\ \mathrm{amp}_{\rm cp,2}>0,
\]
but rather a lower bound on the actual operator strengths, for example
\[
\|B_1^{(\mathrm{cp},1)}\|_F \ge \eta_1,
\qquad
\|B_1^{(\mathrm{cp},2)}\|_F \ge \eta_2,
\]
or on their relative contribution,
\[
\frac{\|B_1^{(\mathrm{cp},1)}\|_F}{\|B_1^{(\mathrm{cp},2)}\|_F} \ge r_0>0.
\]

Only such a constraint would truly test whether two independently contributing complex textures are structurally required for the CKM+phase fit.

\section{Final summary}

We forced both complex texture amplitudes to remain nonzero:
\[
\mathrm{amp}_{\rm cp,1}\ge \epsilon,
\qquad
\mathrm{amp}_{\rm cp,2}\ge \epsilon.
\]

The best fit found under this dual floor is
\[
|V_{us}| \approx 0.223279,
\qquad
|V_{cb}| \approx 0.039836,
\qquad
|V_{ub}| \approx 0.004172,
\]
\[
\delta \approx 1.131806,
\qquad
J \approx 3.27119\times 10^{-5},
\qquad
\mathrm{score}\approx 0.717543.
\]

This is substantially better than all previously recorded baselines.

However, the dual-floor test also reveals the key subtlety:
although both amplitudes are nonzero, the first complex mode can be made effectively invisible in the actual flavor operator:
\[
\|B_1^{(\mathrm{cp},1)}\|_F \approx 9.20\times 10^{-12},
\qquad
\|B_1^{(\mathrm{cp},2)}\|_F \approx 5.07\times 10^{-2}.
\]

Therefore the current best solution is still effectively a one-contributing-complex-mode solution.

Hence the honest current conclusion is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{forcing both amplitudes to be nonzero does not prove genuine two-mode necessity.}
}
\]

What is needed next is a stronger structural constraint on the actual operator contribution of each mode, such as
\[
\|B_1^{(\mathrm{cp},1)}\|_F \ge \eta_1,
\qquad
\|B_1^{(\mathrm{cp},2)}\|_F \ge \eta_2,
\]
or a nontrivial lower bound on their ratio.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Operator-norm-floor test for genuinely contributing two-complex-mode solutions}

The previous amplitude-floor test was not sufficient, because a nonzero amplitude does not guarantee a non-negligible contribution to the actual flavor operator.
Therefore we replaced the amplitude-floor condition by the stronger operator-level constraint
\[
\boxed{
\|B_1^{(\mathrm{cp},1)}\|_F \ge \eta,
\qquad
\|B_1^{(\mathrm{cp},2)}\|_F \ge \eta.
}
\]

This is the correct numerical test of whether two complex texture modes are both genuinely contributing.

We performed a first completed quick sweep for
\[
\eta \in \{0.003,\ 0.005,\ 0.010\}.
\]
In all three cases, the best feasible point converged to essentially the same basin, with observables
\[
|V_{us}| \approx 0.227728,\qquad
|V_{cb}| \approx 0.049833,\qquad
|V_{ub}| \approx 0.003578,
\]
\[
|V_{td}| \approx 0.013887,\qquad
|V_{ts}| \approx 0.047993,
\]
\[
\delta \approx 0.852922,\qquad
J \approx 2.97388\times 10^{-5},
\]
and total score
\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{score}\approx 8.940321.
}
\]

The corresponding mode strengths are
\[
\|B_1^{(\mathrm{cp},1)}\|_F \approx 0.038206,
\qquad
\|B_1^{(\mathrm{cp},2)}\|_F \approx 4.528798.
\]
Hence this solution is genuinely two-contributing at the operator level:
both complex modes are truly present in the effective family operator.

However, the fit quality is dramatically worse than the previously obtained effective one-contributing-mode solution,
for which
\[
\mathrm{score}\approx 0.717543.
\]
Thus
\[
0.717543 \longrightarrow 8.940321
\]
under the operator-norm-floor constraint.

This is the key result of the present stage.

The honest interpretation is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{within the current toy parameterization, excellent CKM+phase fits appear to rely strongly on an effectively one-dominant-complex-mode structure.}
}
\]

Equivalently, once both complex modes are forced to contribute non-negligibly at the operator level,
the fit deteriorates strongly.

This does \emph{not} prove that no good genuinely two-contributing solution exists.
It only shows that, in the present completed search, no such high-quality solution has been found.
So the result is numerical evidence of a strong tension, not a theorem of impossibility.

The pattern of the best feasible norm-floor point is also informative:
\[
|V_{us}| \text{ remains acceptable},\qquad
|V_{ub}| \text{ remains acceptable},
\]
but
\[
|V_{cb}|,\ |V_{td}|,\ |V_{ts}| \text{ become too large},
\qquad
\delta \text{ becomes too small}.
\]
Thus the genuinely two-contributing regime seems to overdrive the \(2\text{--}3\) sector and the third-row leakage.

The current strongest honest conclusion is therefore
\[
\boxed{
\text{the present reduced TECT flavor ansatz robustly supports CKM hierarchy and nonzero CP structure,}
}
\]
but also
\[
\boxed{
\text{its best fits are presently concentrated near an effectively one-contributing-complex-mode geometry.}
}
\]

To go beyond this point, one should not merely increase the search time.
The ansatz itself must be refined so that the two complex modes control more orthogonal directions in flavor space.
A natural next option is to impose a mode-separation condition, for example by requiring distinct midpoint support regions:
\[
|c_{\rm cp,1}-c_{\rm cp,2}| \ge \Delta_c >0,
\]
together with comparable norm constraints
\[
r_{\min}
\le
\frac{\|B_1^{(\mathrm{cp},1)}\|_F}{\|B_1^{(\mathrm{cp},2)}\|_F}
\le
r_{\max}.
\]
Only then can we honestly test whether two structurally distinct contributing complex modes are beneficial, rather than allowing one mode to dominate and the other merely to survive.

\section{Final summary}

We replaced the previous amplitude-floor constraint by the stronger operator-level condition
\[
\|B_1^{(\mathrm{cp},1)}\|_F \ge \eta,
\qquad
\|B_1^{(\mathrm{cp},2)}\|_F \ge \eta,
\]
which is the correct test of genuinely contributing two-complex-mode solutions.

In the completed quick sweep for
\[
\eta \in \{0.003,\ 0.005,\ 0.010\},
\]
the best feasible solution is
\[
|V_{us}| \approx 0.227728,\qquad
|V_{cb}| \approx 0.049833,\qquad
|V_{ub}| \approx 0.003578,
\]
\[
\delta \approx 0.852922,\qquad
J \approx 2.97388\times 10^{-5},
\qquad
\mathrm{score}\approx 8.940321,
\]
with
\[
\|B_1^{(\mathrm{cp},1)}\|_F \approx 0.038206,
\qquad
\|B_1^{(\mathrm{cp},2)}\|_F \approx 4.528798.
\]

So this point is genuinely two-contributing at the operator level.

However, it is much worse than the previous effective one-contributing-mode best fit
\[
\mathrm{score}\approx 0.717543.
\]

Hence the current strongest honest conclusion is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{excellent fits in the present toy ansatz are still concentrated near an effectively one-dominant-complex-mode structure.}
}
\]

This is not a proof that no good genuinely two-contributing solution exists.
It is strong numerical evidence that, within the current parameterization and completed search,
such solutions are under strong tension.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Support-separation and norm-ratio constrained search}

To test whether two genuinely distinct complex texture modes are beneficial,
we imposed two additional structural constraints on the reduced TECT flavor ansatz.

First, a support-separation condition:
\[
|c_{\rm cp,1}-c_{\rm cp,2}| \ge \Delta_c .
\]

Second, a norm-ratio condition:
\[
r_{\min}\le
\frac{\|B_1^{(\mathrm{cp},1)}\|_F}{\|B_1^{(\mathrm{cp},2)}\|_F}
\le r_{\max}.
\]

Together with the previous operator-level floor
\[
\|B_1^{(\mathrm{cp},1)}\|_F \ge \eta,
\qquad
\|B_1^{(\mathrm{cp},2)}\|_F \ge \eta,
\]
this forces the two complex modes to be simultaneously present,
to contribute at comparable size,
and to have distinct support in family-midpoint space.

A first completed scan was carried out for several representative choices of
\[
(\eta,\Delta_c,r_{\min},r_{\max}).
\]

The best completed branch was found at
\[
\eta=0.01,\qquad
\Delta_c=0.55,\qquad
r_{\min}=0.25,\qquad
r_{\max}=4.0,
\]
with
\[
\|B_1^{(\mathrm{cp},1)}\|_F \approx 0.012055,
\qquad
\|B_1^{(\mathrm{cp},2)}\|_F \approx 0.011200,
\]
\[
|c_{\rm cp,1}-c_{\rm cp,2}| \approx 0.983531,
\qquad
\frac{\|B_1^{(\mathrm{cp},1)}\|_F}{\|B_1^{(\mathrm{cp},2)}\|_F}\approx 1.0764.
\]
Hence this branch is genuinely two-mode, support-separated, and norm-comparable.

Its CKM+phase observables are
\[
|V_{us}| \approx 0.220165,\qquad
|V_{cb}| \approx 0.038517,\qquad
|V_{ub}| \approx 0.004944,
\]
\[
\delta \approx 0.990784,\qquad
J \approx 3.418413\times 10^{-5},
\]
with total score
\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{score}\approx 4.567234.
}
\]

For comparison, the previously best effective one-dominant-mode solution had
\[
\mathrm{score}\approx 0.717543.
\]
Therefore the support-separated, norm-comparable two-mode branch is substantially worse.

The other completed branches show the same pattern:
\[
(\eta,\Delta_c,r_{\min},r_{\max})=(0.01,0.45,0.20,5.0)
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\mathrm{score}\approx 5.788167,
\]
\[
(\eta,\Delta_c,r_{\min},r_{\max})=(0.01,0.65,0.33,3.0)
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\mathrm{score}\approx 12.104031.
\]
Thus stronger separation and stronger comparability constraints tend to worsen the fit further.

Additional local refinements around the support-separated branch did not reverse this conclusion.
The best follow-up local point found reached only
\[
\mathrm{score}\approx 6.964825,
\]
with
\[
|V_{us}| \approx 0.224259,\qquad
|V_{cb}| \approx 0.035561,\qquad
|V_{ub}| \approx 0.005537,\qquad
\delta \approx 0.921224.
\]

The honest interpretation is therefore:
\[
\boxed{
\text{within the current toy parameterization, high-quality CKM+phase fits remain concentrated near an effectively one-dominant-complex-mode geometry.}
}
\]

This is not a theorem of impossibility for genuinely two-mode solutions.
It is strong numerical evidence that, in the present ansatz,
forcing two complex modes to contribute at comparable strength and distinct support creates substantial tension.

Equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
\text{the current reduced TECT flavor ansatz robustly produces CKM hierarchy and nonzero CP structure,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{its best solutions are not presently realized as two separated, norm-comparable complex modes.}
}
\]

Hence the bottleneck is no longer merely search depth.
Rather, the present parameterization appears too rigid to let two structurally distinct complex modes cooperate efficiently.
The next natural improvement is therefore to enlarge the ansatz so that the two complex modes act on more orthogonal sectors of flavor space,
for example by assigning one mode primarily to the \(1\text{--}2\) sector and the other to the \(1\text{--}3/2\text{--}3\) sector through a more structured envelope.

\section{Final summary}

We tested whether two genuinely distinct complex texture modes can improve the reduced TECT CKM+phase fit
by imposing three simultaneous constraints:
\[
\|B_1^{(\mathrm{cp},1)}\|_F \ge \eta,\qquad
\|B_1^{(\mathrm{cp},2)}\|_F \ge \eta,
\]
\[
|c_{\rm cp,1}-c_{\rm cp,2}| \ge \Delta_c,
\]
\[
r_{\min}\le
\frac{\|B_1^{(\mathrm{cp},1)}\|_F}{\|B_1^{(\mathrm{cp},2)}\|_F}
\le r_{\max}.
\]

The best completed support-separated, norm-comparable branch gives
\[
|V_{us}| \approx 0.220165,\qquad
|V_{cb}| \approx 0.038517,\qquad
|V_{ub}| \approx 0.004944,
\]
\[
\delta \approx 0.990784,\qquad
J \approx 3.418413\times 10^{-5},
\qquad
\mathrm{score}\approx 4.567234.
\]

This is much worse than the previously best effective one-dominant-mode fit
\[
\mathrm{score}\approx 0.717543.
\]

Therefore the strongest honest current conclusion is
\[
\boxed{
\text{within the present toy ansatz, excellent CKM+phase fits remain concentrated near an effectively one-dominant-complex-mode structure.}
}
\]

So the issue is no longer simply under-searching.
The present parameterization itself appears too rigid to make two separated, comparable complex modes cooperate efficiently.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Assessment of a complex mode acting only through the second family}

The proposal ``a single complex mode acting only on family 2'' has two inequivalent interpretations, and they lead to very different conclusions.

\section{Interpretation A: purely diagonal action on family 2}

If the proposal is interpreted literally as
\[
B_{\rm cp}^{(2{\rm -diag})}=z\,P_2,
\qquad
P_2=|2\rangle\langle 2|,
\]
then Hermiticity requires
\[
B_{\rm cp}^{(2{\rm -diag})\dagger}=B_{\rm cp}^{(2{\rm -diag})}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
z=\bar z,
\]
so
\[
z\in\mathbb R.
\]
Hence
\[
\boxed{
B_{\rm cp}^{(2{\rm -diag})}=\alpha P_2,\qquad \alpha\in\mathbb R.
}
\]

Therefore this term is not genuinely complex in the Hermitian flavor ansatz.
It can shift the second-family level and modify mixing angles indirectly,
but it cannot by itself generate a physical CKM phase.
In particular, if all other matrices remain real symmetric,
then
\[
J=0,\qquad \delta=0
\]
still holds.

So a strictly diagonal family-2-only complex mode is not a good CP-generating candidate.

\section{Interpretation B: family-2-anchored off-diagonal complex mode}

A much more promising interpretation is that the complex mode acts only through the channels involving family 2:
\[
1\leftrightarrow 2,
\qquad
2\leftrightarrow 3,
\qquad
1\not\leftrightarrow 3
\quad\text{(directly in the complex sector)}.
\]

The minimal Hermitian ansatz is
\[
\boxed{
B_{\rm cp}^{(2{\rm -anchor})}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & \rho_{12}e^{i\phi_{12}} & 0\\
\rho_{12}e^{-i\phi_{12}} & 0 & \rho_{23}e^{i\phi_{23}}\\
0 & \rho_{23}e^{-i\phi_{23}} & 0
\end{pmatrix},
}
\]
or equivalently, in a minimal imaginary form,
\[
\boxed{
B_{\rm cp}^{(2{\rm -anchor})}
=
i\eta_{12}(E_{12}-E_{21})
+
i\eta_{23}(E_{23}-E_{32}).
}
\]

This ansatz has three attractive properties.

First, it directly targets the phenomenologically important channels
\[
1\text{--}2 \quad \text{and} \quad 2\text{--}3,
\]
which are the main carriers of \(V_{us}\) and \(V_{cb}\).

Second, it suppresses direct complex \(1\text{--}3\) leakage, so it may help reduce the tendency of the toy model to overproduce \(|V_{ub}|\).

Third, it matches the numerical evidence obtained so far:
the best fits appear near an effectively one-dominant complex mode,
while forcing several comparable complex modes tends to overdrive the \(1\text{--}3\) and \(2\text{--}3\) sectors.
A family-2-anchored complex mode is therefore a natural way to make the complex structure more selective.

\section{Necessary caveat: CP is not automatic}

However, a \(2\)-anchored complex mode does not automatically guarantee physical CP violation.
For a nontrivial phase invariant to appear, one still needs an effective triangular carrier in flavor space.

In practical terms, if the complex mode contributes only to
\[
(12)\quad\text{and}\quad(23),
\]
then the remaining real sector must provide a nonzero
\[
(13)
\]
entry.
Thus one should require at least one of
\[
(B_0)_{13}\neq 0
\qquad \text{or} \qquad
(B_H)_{13}\neq 0.
\]

This is the correct minimal design principle:
\[
\boxed{
\text{complex part on }12,23\text{ only; real }13\text{ carrier from }B_0\text{ or }B_H.
}
\]

\section{Recommended next ansatz}

The most economical next model is therefore
\[
B_1
=
B_1^{(\mathrm{real})}
+
B_{\rm cp}^{(2{\rm -anchor})},
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
B_{\rm cp}^{(2{\rm -anchor})}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & a\,e^{i\phi_{12}} & 0\\
a\,e^{-i\phi_{12}} & 0 & b\,e^{i\phi_{23}}\\
0 & b\,e^{-i\phi_{23}} & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad a,b\ge 0,
}
\]
while keeping \(B_0\) and \(B_H\) real symmetric, but requiring
\[
(B_0)_{13}\neq 0
\quad \text{or} \quad
(B_H)_{13}\neq 0.
\]

This ansatz is structurally attractive because it gives a selective complex source for the \(1\text{--}2\) and \(2\text{--}3\) sectors,
while leaving the \(1\text{--}3\) channel mostly controlled by the real background.
It is therefore the most natural next test if the goal is to improve
\[
|V_{us}|,\quad |V_{cb}|,\quad |V_{ub}|,\quad \delta
\]
simultaneously with minimal extra freedom.

\section{Final summary}

The proposal ``a complex mode acting only on family 2'' must be split into two cases.

If it means a purely diagonal family-2 projector,
\[
B_{\rm cp}=zP_2,
\]
then Hermiticity forces
\[
z\in\mathbb R,
\]
so this does not provide a genuine CP-carrying complex mode.

If instead it means a family-2-anchored off-diagonal mode acting only on
\[
1\leftrightarrow 2
\quad\text{and}\quad
2\leftrightarrow 3,
\]
then the idea is highly promising.
The minimal Hermitian form is
\[
B_{\rm cp}^{(2{\rm -anchor})}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & a\,e^{i\phi_{12}} & 0\\
a\,e^{-i\phi_{12}} & 0 & b\,e^{i\phi_{23}}\\
0 & b\,e^{-i\phi_{23}} & 0
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

This ansatz is attractive because it can control \(V_{us}\) and \(V_{cb}\) directly while suppressing direct complex \(1\text{--}3\) leakage, which may help with the current \(|V_{ub}|\) tension.

However, physical CP violation then still requires a real \(1\text{--}3\) carrier from \(B_0\) or \(B_H\).

Therefore the strongest current recommendation is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{do not use a purely diagonal family-2 complex mode; use a family-2-anchored }12/23\text{-only complex mode instead.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Family-2-anchored complex mode: numerical test}

We implemented and tested the proposal that the complex flavor mode should act only through the second family, namely through the channels
\[
1\leftrightarrow 2,
\qquad
2\leftrightarrow 3,
\qquad
1\not\leftrightarrow 3
\quad\text{(directly in the complex sector)}.
\]

Two versions were tested.

\section{General anchored complex ansatz}

The first implementation used the minimal Hermitian form
\[
\boxed{
B_{\rm cp}^{(2\text{-anchor})}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & a\,e^{i\phi_{12}} & 0\\
a\,e^{-i\phi_{12}} & 0 & b\,e^{i\phi_{23}}\\
0 & b\,e^{-i\phi_{23}} & 0
\end{pmatrix},
}
\]
with Gaussian midpoint envelopes on the \(12\) and \(23\) channels.

A moderate multi-seed search gave the best point
\[
|V_{us}| \approx 0.22221,\qquad
|V_{cb}| \approx 0.04311,\qquad
|V_{ub}| \approx 0.00459,
\]
\[
|V_{td}| \approx 0.01281,\qquad
|V_{ts}| \approx 0.04142,
\]
\[
\delta \approx 0.91153,\qquad
J \approx 3.38\times 10^{-5},
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{score}\approx 3.8889.
}
\]

This shows that the anchored ansatz can generate nontrivial CKM hierarchy and nonzero CP structure,
but it still tends to leak too much into the \(1\text{--}3\) sector.

\section{Pure-imaginary anchored ansatz}

The second implementation used the stricter form
\[
\boxed{
B_{\rm cp}^{(2\text{-anchor, imag})}
=
i\eta_{12}(E_{12}-E_{21})
+
i\eta_{23}(E_{23}-E_{32}),
}
\]
again with Gaussian midpoint envelopes, but with no direct complex \(13\) entry and no extra real part in the complex sector.

This produced the best result obtained in the present anchored study:
\[
|V_{us}| \approx 0.22127,\qquad
|V_{cb}| \approx 0.04147,\qquad
|V_{ub}| \approx 0.00310,
\]
\[
|V_{td}| \approx 0.00777,\qquad
|V_{ts}| \approx 0.04085,
\]
\[
\delta \approx 0.93409,\qquad
J \approx 2.23\times 10^{-5},
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{score}\approx 2.76111.
}
\]

This is better than the support-separated, norm-comparable two-mode branches studied earlier,
but still substantially worse than the previously best effective one-dominant-mode solution
\[
\mathrm{score}\approx 0.71754.
\]

\section{Interpretation}

The anchored idea is therefore structurally promising, but the present minimal anchored ansatz is still too weak to beat the best previous fit.

The numerical pattern is clear:

\begin{enumerate}
\item The \(12/23\)-only complex structure helps suppress direct complex \(1\text{--}3\) leakage, so \(|V_{ub}|\) does not overshoot badly.
\item However, the same restriction tends to weaken the CP-carrying triangular structure, so \(\delta\) and especially \(J\) become too small unless the anchored mode becomes stronger.
\end{enumerate}

For the best pure-imaginary anchored point, one finds
\[
\|B_{\rm cp}^{(2\text{-anchor})}\|_F \approx 1.39\times 10^{-3},
\]
while the real \(13\) carrier satisfies
\[
|(B_0+B_H)_{13}| \approx 7.14\times 10^{-2}.
\]
Thus the present failure mode is not the absence of a real \(13\) carrier.
Rather, it is the insufficient strength of the anchored complex \(12/23\) source.

Hence the honest current conclusion is
\[
\boxed{
\text{the family-2-anchored idea is directionally correct,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{the current minimal anchored parameterization does not yet provide enough independent control over the complex source versus the real }13\text{ carrier.}
}
\]

The most natural next step is therefore not to abandon the anchored idea,
but to promote the real \(13\) carrier to an explicit controllable texture while keeping the complex sector restricted to \(12/23\).
This would separate the roles
\[
\text{complex }(12,23)\text{ source}
\quad\text{and}\quad
\text{real }(13)\text{ carrier},
\]
which is precisely what the present numerical bottleneck suggests is needed.

\section{Final summary}

We tested the proposal that the complex flavor mode should act only through family 2.

A strictly \(12/23\)-only anchored complex mode is numerically viable and indeed helps suppress direct complex \(1\text{--}3\) leakage.
The best pure-imaginary anchored fit obtained is
\[
|V_{us}| \approx 0.22127,\qquad
|V_{cb}| \approx 0.04147,\qquad
|V_{ub}| \approx 0.00310,
\]
\[
\delta \approx 0.93409,\qquad
J \approx 2.23\times 10^{-5},
\qquad
\mathrm{score}\approx 2.76111.
\]

Thus the idea is not wrong.
In fact, it performs better than the previously forced genuinely two-mode branches.

However, it still does not beat the current best effective one-dominant-mode solution
\[
\mathrm{score}\approx 0.71754.
\]

The bottleneck is now clear:
the real \(13\) carrier is present, but the anchored complex \(12/23\) source is too weak.
So the next correct ansatz is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{keep the complex sector }12/23\text{-only, but introduce an explicit independent real }13\text{ carrier control.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Assessment of the exploratory flavor search and the correct transition to a principled derivation}

The current question is whether the ongoing exploratory CKM/phase search still has genuine scientific value,
or whether its main purpose has already been achieved and the program should now return to the principled derivation from the microscopic TECT construction.

The correct answer is the following.

\subsection{What has already been established}

The exploratory reduced flavor search has already achieved its primary goal.
At the reduced matrix level, it has provided strong numerical evidence for the following three statements:

\[
\boxed{
\text{(i) nontrivial hierarchical CKM-like mixing exists in the reduced TECT flavor problem,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{(ii) CP-violating branches with }J\neq 0\text{ and }\delta\neq 0\text{ also exist,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{(iii) no single ad hoc complex texture appears to be uniquely necessary.}
}
\]

This means that the exploratory phase has already passed the key existential test.
The reduced flavor problem is not empty, not overconstrained, and not obviously dependent on a unique arbitrary ansatz.

In that precise sense, the exploratory search has already been meaningful and successful.

\subsection{What has \emph{not} been established}

However, the exploratory search has \emph{not} established any of the following:

\[
\boxed{
\text{(a) a unique microscopic derivation of the flavor operator from the full defect PDE,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{(b) a theorem that a particular texture class is necessary,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{(c) a first-principles CKM prediction independent of residual parameter choices.}
}
\]

Thus the present numerical exploration should not be mistaken for a derivation.
It is an existence-and-nonuniqueness study, not yet a microscopic theorem.

\subsection{Why further blind fitting now has diminishing value}

Once the existential question has been answered positively,
continued blind ansatz-searching has sharply diminishing scientific return.

The reason is simple:
the dominant open problem is no longer
\[
\text{``does a viable reduced fit exist?''}
\]
but rather
\[
\text{``which flavor operator structure is actually generated by the microscopic TECT construction?''}
\]

Therefore reducing the score from, say, \(0.7\) to \(0.5\) inside a still-ad hoc toy space would add very little structural knowledge.
It would improve numerical cosmetics, but not the derivational status of the theory.

Hence the correct transition point has effectively already been reached.

\subsection{What ``proceeding in the proper way'' now means}

At the present stage, a proper derivational program should consist of four steps.

\paragraph{Step 1: replace texture ans\"atze by an operator-basis decomposition.}

Instead of guessing Gaussian textures directly, one should first expand the effective family operators in a Hermitian basis of \(3\times 3\) matrices:
\[
B_0=\sum_{A=0}^{8} b_A \Lambda_A,\qquad
B_1=\sum_{A=0}^{8} y_A \Lambda_A,\qquad
B_H=\sum_{A=0}^{8} h_A \Lambda_A,
\]
where \(\{\Lambda_A\}\) is a basis of \(\mathfrak u(3)\).

This removes inessential texture language and asks the correct structural question:
which operator channels are actually generated, and which are suppressed?

\paragraph{Step 2: classify the reduced CP-carrying mechanisms at the theorem level.}

The numerical exploration has already strongly suggested several structural facts that should now be converted into exact reduced-level propositions.

Examples include:
\begin{enumerate}
\item a purely diagonal complex mode cannot generate a physical CKM phase in a Hermitian ansatz;
\item a complex mode restricted to the \(12\) and \(23\) channels can generate CP violation provided a real \(13\) carrier is present;
\item a direct complex \(13\) entry is not obviously necessary;
\item the best reduced fits tend to lie near an effectively one-dominant-complex-mode geometry.
\end{enumerate}

These statements should now be formalized in terms of basis-independent invariants such as
\[
\det\!\bigl([M_u,M_d]\bigr),\qquad
J,\qquad
\operatorname{Tr}\bigl([M_u,M_d]^3\bigr).
\]

\paragraph{Step 3: derive the allowed operator channels from the microscopic TECT PDE / Schur complement.}

This is the real next frontier.

The heavy-sector elimination should produce an effective family operator
\[
\mathcal Y_{\rm eff}
\]
or its sectoral descendants,
and the task is to determine which reduced matrix components are actually generated:
\[
(12),\qquad (23),\qquad (13),\qquad \text{diagonal splittings},\qquad \text{complex antisymmetric parts}.
\]

Only this step can turn the reduced flavor stage from an existence study into a derivation.

\paragraph{Step 4: perform fitting only after the allowed operator structure has been derived.}

Once the microscopic derivation has reduced the admissible operator space,
one may then perform a final phenomenological fit inside that derived space.

This is the correct order.
Fitting before derivation is exploratory.
Fitting after derivation is explanatory.

\subsection{The strongest honest present conclusion}

Therefore the correct present conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the exploratory reduced flavor search has already done enough work to justify returning to the principled derivation.}
}
\]

Equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
\text{continued blind ansatz-searching should no longer be the main research direction.}
}
\]

But the numerical search results should not be discarded.
They now serve as empirical boundary conditions for the microscopic derivation.

In particular, the exploratory phase suggests the following operator-level hypotheses to test first in the full derivation:
\begin{enumerate}
\item purely diagonal complex sectors are weak CP carriers;
\item direct complex \(13\) terms are not obviously necessary;
\item \(12/23\)-anchored complex structure plus a real \(13\) carrier is a viable reduced CP mechanism;
\item good fits tend to concentrate near an effectively one-dominant-complex-mode geometry;
\item two separated norm-comparable complex modes are disfavored in the present reduced ansatz.
\end{enumerate}

These are no longer arbitrary guesses.
They are the correct reduced-level hypotheses that the microscopic theory must now confront.

\section{Final summary}

The exploratory CKM/phase search in the reduced TECT flavor problem has already achieved its primary purpose.

It has provided strong numerical evidence that:

\[
\boxed{
\text{hierarchical CKM-like mixing exists in the reduced model,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{CP-violating branches with }J\neq 0\text{ and }\delta\neq 0\text{ also exist,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{no single ad hoc complex texture appears uniquely necessary.}
}
\]

Therefore the existential stage is essentially complete.

What remains open is not the existence of viable reduced fits,
but the derivation of the effective flavor operator from the microscopic TECT construction.
Hence further blind ansatz-searching now has sharply diminishing value.

The correct next move is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{replace texture fitting by operator-basis classification and microscopic derivation.}
}
\]

So the strongest honest current conclusion is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the exploratory stage has done enough; it is now correct to proceed in the principled derivational direction.}
}
\]

%
% 
%
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{General Hermitian basis for the reduced flavor operators}

We now abandon ad hoc texture language and pass to the canonical Hermitian basis of \(3\times 3\) family operators.

Let \(E_{ab}\) denote the elementary matrix with a \(1\) in the \((a,b)\) entry and zeros elsewhere.
Define the Hermitian basis
\[
D_0=\mathbf 1,
\qquad
D_1=\mathrm{diag}(1,-1,0),
\qquad
D_2=\mathrm{diag}(1,1,-2),
\]
\[
S_{12}=E_{12}+E_{21},
\qquad
S_{13}=E_{13}+E_{31},
\qquad
S_{23}=E_{23}+E_{32},
\]
\[
A_{12}=i(E_{12}-E_{21}),
\qquad
A_{13}=i(E_{13}-E_{31}),
\qquad
A_{23}=i(E_{23}-E_{32}).
\]

Then every Hermitian \(3\times 3\) matrix \(M\) admits the unique expansion
\[
\boxed{
M
=
\alpha_0 D_0+\alpha_1 D_1+\alpha_2 D_2
+s_{12}S_{12}+s_{13}S_{13}+s_{23}S_{23}
+a_{12}A_{12}+a_{13}A_{13}+a_{23}A_{23},
}
\]
with all coefficients
\[
\alpha_0,\alpha_1,\alpha_2,s_{12},s_{13},s_{23},a_{12},a_{13},a_{23}\in\mathbb R.
\]

Thus the reduced TECT family operators can be written as
\[
B_0=\sum_{\Xi} b_\Xi\,\Xi,
\qquad
B_1=\sum_{\Xi} y_\Xi\,\Xi,
\qquad
B_H=\sum_{\Xi} h_\Xi\,\Xi,
\]
where
\[
\Xi\in\{D_0,D_1,D_2,S_{12},S_{13},S_{23},A_{12},A_{13},A_{23}\}.
\]

At the toy post-EWSB level,
\[
M_u = \left(B_0-\frac23 B_1\right)+B_H,
\qquad
M_d = \left(B_0+\frac13 B_1\right)-B_H,
\]
so
\[
M_u=\sum_{\Xi} u_\Xi\,\Xi,
\qquad
M_d=\sum_{\Xi} d_\Xi\,\Xi,
\]
with
\[
u_\Xi=b_\Xi-\frac23 y_\Xi+h_\Xi,
\qquad
d_\Xi=b_\Xi+\frac13 y_\Xi-h_\Xi.
\]

Therefore the reduced flavor problem is, in full generality, a problem of determining the coefficient vectors
\[
(u_\Xi),\qquad (d_\Xi)
\]
in this Hermitian basis.

\section{CP-even and CP-odd subspaces}

In the above basis, complex conjugation acts as
\[
D_i^\ast=D_i,
\qquad
S_{ab}^\ast=S_{ab},
\qquad
A_{ab}^\ast=-A_{ab}.
\]

Hence the Hermitian operator space splits as
\[
\mathfrak{u}(3)_{\mathrm{Herm}}
=
\mathcal D\oplus \mathcal S\oplus \mathcal A,
\]
where
\[
\mathcal D=\mathrm{span}\{D_0,D_1,D_2\},
\qquad
\mathcal S=\mathrm{span}\{S_{12},S_{13},S_{23}\},
\qquad
\mathcal A=\mathrm{span}\{A_{12},A_{13},A_{23}\}.
\]

The sectors \(\mathcal D\) and \(\mathcal S\) are real under complex conjugation, while \(\mathcal A\) is odd.
Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{In a Hermitian flavor ansatz, all genuinely CP-odd carrier content lives in }
\mathcal A=\mathrm{span}\{A_{12},A_{13},A_{23}\}.
}
\]

This yields the first exact reduced-level proposition.

\paragraph{Proposition 1 (diagonal ``complex mode'' is impossible).}
A purely diagonal Hermitian flavor term cannot carry a physical complex phase.

\paragraph{Proof.}
A diagonal Hermitian matrix belongs to \(\mathcal D\), hence has the form
\[
M_{\mathrm{diag}}=\alpha_0 D_0+\alpha_1 D_1+\alpha_2 D_2
\]
with real coefficients \(\alpha_i\in\mathbb R\).
So a would-be ``complex diagonal mode'' is forced by Hermiticity to be real.
Therefore it cannot by itself generate a CKM CP phase.
\(\square\)

\section{Basis-independent CP invariant}

Because \(M_u\) and \(M_d\) are Hermitian in the reduced model, define
\[
H_u=M_u^2,
\qquad
H_d=M_d^2.
\]
These are positive Hermitian matrices and transform covariantly under family-basis changes.

The standard basis-independent CP diagnostic is
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I_{\mathrm{CP}}
:=
\frac{1}{3i}\,
\mathrm{Tr}\!\left([H_u,H_d]^3\right).
}
\]

This quantity is invariant under
\[
M_u\mapsto U^\dagger M_u U,
\qquad
M_d\mapsto U^\dagger M_d U,
\]
and vanishes whenever \(H_u\) and \(H_d\) can be made simultaneously real.
For three nondegenerate families, it is the standard necessary-and-sufficient Jarlskog criterion:
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I_{\mathrm{CP}}\neq 0
\iff
\text{physical CP violation.}
}
\]

Thus, at the reduced flavor level, the real mathematical question is not
``which texture looks complex,'' but rather:
\[
\text{which coefficient patterns in }
\mathcal D\oplus\mathcal S\oplus\mathcal A
\text{ make }
\mathcal I_{\mathrm{CP}}
\neq 0?
\]

\section{Useful commutator algebra}

The mechanism is governed by a small set of exact commutators.
For \(D(\mu)=\mathrm{diag}(\mu_1,\mu_2,\mu_3)\), one has
\[
[D(\mu),A_{12}] = i(\mu_1-\mu_2)S_{12},
\qquad
[D(\mu),A_{23}] = i(\mu_2-\mu_3)S_{23},
\]
\[
[D(\mu),S_{12}] = -i(\mu_1-\mu_2)A_{12},
\qquad
[D(\mu),S_{23}] = -i(\mu_2-\mu_3)A_{23}.
\]

The inter-channel commutators needed for the anchored mechanism are
\[
[S_{13},A_{12}] = i S_{23},
\qquad
[S_{13},A_{23}] = -i S_{12},
\qquad
[S_{12},A_{23}] = i S_{13},
\]
\[
[A_{12},A_{23}] = -A_{13},
\qquad
[S_{12},S_{23}] = -i A_{13}.
\]

These relations already show the basic structural fact:
\[
\boxed{
\text{anchored }(12,23)\text{ complex content can propagate into the rest of flavor space through real off-diagonal carriers.}
}
\]

But they do \emph{not} imply that every such anchored pattern is automatically CP-violating.
This distinction is crucial.

\section{Exact reduced-level propositions}

\paragraph{Proposition 2 (two-family reduction cannot carry CKM CP violation).}
Suppose both \(M_u\) and \(M_d\) are supported in a single \(2\times2\) family block, e.g.
\[
M_u,M_d\in
\mathrm{span}\{D_0,D_1,D_2,S_{12},A_{12}\}.
\]
Then
\[
\mathcal I_{\mathrm{CP}}=0.
\]

\paragraph{Proof.}
In this case both \(H_u\) and \(H_d\) are block-diagonal of type
\[
2\oplus 1.
\]
Hence their commutator \([H_u,H_d]\) also has vanishing third row and column.
Therefore \([H_u,H_d]^3\) has zero trace, so
\[
\mathrm{Tr}\!\left([H_u,H_d]^3\right)=0.
\]
Equivalently, a genuine three-family CP invariant cannot arise in a reduced two-family block.
\(\square\)

This is the exact statement behind the informal slogan:
\[
\boxed{
\text{a single active }2\times2\text{ channel cannot produce CKM CP violation.}
}
\]

\paragraph{Proposition 3 (direct complex \(13\) support is not necessary).}
There exist Hermitian reduced flavor pairs with
\[
a_{13}^{(u)}=a_{13}^{(d)}=0
\]
but nevertheless
\[
\mathcal I_{\mathrm{CP}}\neq 0.
\]

\paragraph{Proof by explicit witness.}
Consider
\[
M_u=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & 1 & 1\\
1 & 1 & 0\\
1 & 0 & 2
\end{pmatrix}
=
D_u+S_{12}+S_{13},
\]
\[
M_d=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & i & 0\\
-i & 1 & i\\
0 & -i & 3
\end{pmatrix}
=
D_d+A_{12}+A_{23}.
\]
Here the complex sector is anchored entirely in the \(12\) and \(23\) channels; there is no \(A_{13}\) term.

Now define
\[
H_u=M_u^2,
\qquad
H_d=M_d^2.
\]
A direct computation gives
\[
\mathrm{Tr}\!\left([H_u,H_d]^3\right)=1260\,i\neq 0.
\]
Hence
\[
\mathcal I_{\mathrm{CP}}\neq 0.
\]
So direct complex \(13\) support is not necessary for physical CP violation.
\(\square\)

This proposition is important because it upgrades the earlier numerical hint to an exact reduced-level fact:
\[
\boxed{
A_{13}\text{ is not a necessary CP carrier.}
}
\]

\paragraph{Proposition 4 (anchored complex \(12/23\) plus real \(13\) alone is not automatically sufficient).}
Consider the family of Hermitian matrices
\[
M_u=D_u+x\,S_{13},
\qquad
M_d=D_d+a\,A_{12}+b\,A_{23},
\]
with arbitrary real \(D_u,D_d,x,a,b\).
Then
\[
\mathcal I_{\mathrm{CP}}=0
\]
identically.

\paragraph{Proof.}
Define
\[
H_u=M_u^2,
\qquad
H_d=M_d^2.
\]
A direct symbolic computation yields
\[
\mathrm{Tr}\!\left([H_u,H_d]^3\right)=0
\]
for all values of the parameters.
Hence
\[
\mathcal I_{\mathrm{CP}}=0.
\]
So a real \(13\) carrier, together with anchored \(A_{12},A_{23}\), is \emph{not by itself} a sufficient condition for CP violation.
\(\square\)

This corrects an overly naive version of the anchored intuition.
The correct statement is weaker and more precise:

\[
\boxed{
\text{anchored }A_{12},A_{23}\text{ are algebraically viable CP carriers,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{a real }S_{13}\text{ carrier alone does not guarantee }\mathcal I_{\mathrm{CP}}\neq 0.
}
\]

\paragraph{Proposition 5 (anchored complex structure becomes viable once the real skeleton is sufficiently rich).}
There exist Hermitian reduced flavor pairs with complex support only in the anchored channels
\[
A_{12},A_{23},
\]
but with no \(A_{13}\), for which \(\mathcal I_{\mathrm{CP}}\neq0\).

\paragraph{Proof.}
This is already established by Proposition 3.
In that witness pair,
\[
M_u=D_u+S_{12}+S_{13},
\qquad
M_d=D_d+A_{12}+A_{23},
\]
and
\[
\mathcal I_{\mathrm{CP}}\neq 0.
\]
Thus the anchored mechanism is genuinely viable, provided the real skeleton is richer than a single \(S_{13}\) carrier.
\(\square\)

\section{What is now rigorously closed and what remains open}

The following reduced-level facts are now mathematically closed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item A diagonal Hermitian sector cannot carry a physical complex phase.
\item A genuine CKM CP invariant cannot arise in a single reduced \(2\times2\) family block.
\item Direct complex \(13\) support is not necessary.
\item Anchored \(12/23\) complex structure is algebraically viable.
\item Anchored \(12/23\) complex structure plus real \(13\) alone is not automatically sufficient.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the reduced TECT flavor problem has now been upgraded from texture intuition to an operator-level classification:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the CP problem is a classification problem in }
\mathcal D\oplus\mathcal S\oplus\mathcal A,
\text{ controlled by }
\mathcal I_{\mathrm{CP}}.
}
\]

What remains open is the genuinely microscopic question:

\[
\boxed{
\text{which coefficients }
u_\Xi,\ d_\Xi
\text{ are actually generated by the TECT defect PDE / Schur complement?}
}
\]

That is the correct next frontier.

\section{Final summary}

We replaced ad hoc flavor textures by the full Hermitian basis
\[
\{D_0,D_1,D_2,S_{12},S_{13},S_{23},A_{12},A_{13},A_{23}\}
\]
of \(3\times3\) family operators and classified the CP-carrying sectors.

The rigorous reduced-level conclusions are:

\begin{enumerate}
\item Physical complex-phase carrier content lives only in
\[
\mathcal A=\mathrm{span}\{A_{12},A_{13},A_{23}\}.
\]

\item A purely diagonal Hermitian flavor term cannot carry CKM CP violation.

\item Any effectively two-family block has
\[
\mathcal I_{\mathrm{CP}}=0.
\]

\item Direct complex \(13\) support is not necessary:
there exist explicit Hermitian witness pairs with only anchored complex support in \(12\) and \(23\), but with
\[
\mathcal I_{\mathrm{CP}}\neq 0.
\]

\item However, anchored complex support in \(12\) and \(23\), together with a single real \(13\) carrier, is not automatically sufficient:
for
\[
M_u=D_u+xS_{13},
\qquad
M_d=D_d+aA_{12}+bA_{23},
\]
one finds
\[
\mathcal I_{\mathrm{CP}}=0
\]
identically.

\item Therefore the anchored mechanism is viable, but only when the real skeleton is sufficiently rich.
\end{enumerate}

So the reduced flavor problem is now properly reformulated as an operator-basis classification problem controlled by the basis-independent invariant
\[
\mathcal I_{\mathrm{CP}}=\frac{1}{3i}\mathrm{Tr}([H_u,H_d]^3).
\]

The next real question is no longer texture fitting, but:
\[
\boxed{
\text{which operator coefficients are actually generated by the microscopic TECT defect PDE / Schur complement?}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Microscopic block elimination and the general reduced flavor operator}

We now derive the correct general formula for the reduced family operator from the microscopic defect/heavy-sector problem.

\section{Light/heavy decomposition of the microscopic operator}

Let the full microscopic Hilbert space decompose as
\[
\mathcal H_{\rm micro}=\mathcal H_L\oplus \mathcal H_H,
\]
where

\[
\mathcal H_L = \mathrm{span}\{\phi_1,\phi_2,\phi_3\}
\]
is the light family subspace, and \(\mathcal H_H\) is the heavy sector.

Let \(\mathbb O(\lambda)\) denote the microscopic Hermitian operator relevant for the spectral problem.
With respect to the decomposition \(\mathcal H_L\oplus\mathcal H_H\), write
\[
\mathbb O(\lambda)=
\begin{pmatrix}
L(\lambda) & K(\lambda)\\
K^\dagger(\lambda) & H(\lambda)
\end{pmatrix},
\]
where
\[
L:\mathcal H_L\to\mathcal H_L,\qquad
K:\mathcal H_H\to\mathcal H_L,\qquad
H:\mathcal H_H\to\mathcal H_H.
\]

Assume that \(H(\lambda)\) is invertible in the spectral region of interest.

\section{Exact Schur-complement formula}

Let
\[
\Psi=
\begin{pmatrix}
\psi_L\\
\psi_H
\end{pmatrix}
\in \mathcal H_L\oplus \mathcal H_H
\]
satisfy
\[
\mathbb O(\lambda)\Psi=0.
\]
Then the heavy component obeys
\[
K^\dagger \psi_L + H\psi_H=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\psi_H=-H^{-1}K^\dagger\psi_L.
\]
Substituting back into the light equation gives
\[
L\psi_L + K\psi_H=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\left(L-KH^{-1}K^\dagger\right)\psi_L=0.
\]

Therefore the exact reduced light-sector operator is
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal Y_{\rm eff}(\lambda)=L(\lambda)-K(\lambda)\,H(\lambda)^{-1}\,K(\lambda)^\dagger.
}
\]

If one prefers the spectral-parameter form with a fixed heavy operator \(H_0\),
then one writes
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal Y_{\rm eff}(\lambda)=L-K(H_0-\lambda)^{-1}K^\dagger.
}
\]

This is the precise Schur-complement origin of the reduced flavor matrix.

\section{Low-energy expansion}

If \(\| \lambda H_0^{-1}\|<1\), then
\[
(H_0-\lambda)^{-1}
=
H_0^{-1}
+\lambda H_0^{-2}
+\lambda^2 H_0^{-3}
+\cdots.
\]
Hence
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal Y_{\rm eff}(\lambda)
=
L
-
K H_0^{-1}K^\dagger
-
\lambda K H_0^{-2}K^\dagger
-
\lambda^2 K H_0^{-3}K^\dagger
-\cdots.
}
\]

So the leading reduced operator is
\[
