They are safer than the shorter unsymmetrized formulas, because they do not presuppose extra equalities beyond the locked form itself.

\section{Exact microscopic renormalization of }(g_c,g_E,g_O)

Let
\[
M_i=M_i^{\rm ref}+\Delta M_i,
\qquad
\Delta M_i=P_*(\partial_{k_i}\Delta H_{\rm eff})P_*.
\]

Then the Class II branch renormalizes the reduced invariants through
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\lambda_\parallel^{\rm ref}+\Delta\lambda_\parallel,
\qquad
\alpha=\alpha^{\rm ref}+\Delta\alpha,
\qquad
\beta=\beta^{\rm ref}+\Delta\beta,
\]
with
\[
\Delta\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3\Delta M_\parallel),
\]
\[
\Delta\alpha=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_1\Delta M_1+\sigma_2\Delta M_2),
\qquad
\Delta\beta=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_2\Delta M_1-\sigma_1\Delta M_2).
\]

Thus the exact Class II microscopic renormalization of the Dirac data is carried entirely by the Schur-complement correction \(\Delta H_{\rm eff}\).

Now define the microscopic overlap constants \(C_c,C_E,C_O\) by
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=C_c\,g_c,
\qquad
\alpha=C_E\,g_E,
\qquad
\beta=C_O\,g_O.
}
\]

Then the extracted Class II coefficients are
\[
\boxed{
g_c=\frac{\lambda_\parallel}{C_c},
\qquad
g_E=\frac{\alpha}{C_E},
\qquad
g_O=\frac{\beta}{C_O}.
}
\]

Only after an explicit overlap evaluation may one specialize
\[
C_c=\frac12 I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
C_E=I_\theta^{(E)},
\qquad
C_O=I_\theta^{(O)}.
\]
If the locked branch symmetry further implies
\[
I_\theta^{(E)}=I_\theta^{(O)}=:I_\theta,
\]
then one recovers the compressed working dictionary
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{g_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=g_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=g_O I_\theta.
}
\]

\section{What is now actually closed}

Within the explicit refined locked + Class II working branch, the following points are now fixed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the heavy mediator enters as a light/heavy block system whose quadratic elimination is exact at the fluctuation level;
\item the mediator correction to the shell operator is the Schur complement
\[
\Delta H_{\rm eff}(k)
=
-
H_{\Psi X}(k)H_{XX}(k)^{-1}H_{X\Psi}(k);
\]
\item the transport matrices are
\[
M_i=P_*\left.\partial_{k_i}H_{\rm eff}(k)\right|_{k=k_*}P_*;
\]
\item the reduced locked coefficients are obtained by Pauli traces;
\item the microscopic Class II renormalization of \((g_c,g_E,g_O)\) is read directly from those projected traces.
\end{enumerate}

So this branch is now fully integrated into the general Schur-complement operator formalism.

\section{What remains explicit but not yet fully evaluated}

What still remains to be inserted from the concrete branch data is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the fully explicit formulas for the current vertices \(\mathcal J_i^a(k)\) and \(\mathcal K_i^a(k)\);
\item the explicit locked-branch proof of the Pauli selection rule;
\item the actual overlap evaluation of \(C_c,C_E,C_O\).
\end{enumerate}

These are no longer conceptual gaps.
They are the remaining branch-specific algebraic computations.

\section{Final summary}

The refined locked + Class II working branch can now be cleanly inserted into the general reduced-operator formalism.

Starting from
\[
\mathcal L_{\rm mic}
=
\mathcal L_\Psi^{\rm ref}
+\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+\alpha_X X_i^a J_i^a
+\beta_X X_i^a K_i^a,
\]
the quadratic Bloch fiber operator takes the block form
\[
\mathcal H_{\rm Bloch}(k)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k) & H_{\Psi X}(k)\\
H_{X\Psi}(k) & H_{XX}(k)
\end{pmatrix},
\]
with
\[
H_{\Psi X}(k)=\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k).
\]

The heavy mediator is eliminated exactly at quadratic level by the Schur complement
\[
H_{\rm eff}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)-H_{\Psi X}(k)H_{XX}(k)^{-1}H_{X\Psi}(k).
\]

After shell projection and spectral valley projection
\[
P_*=\frac{1}{2\pi i}\oint_\Gamma (z-H_{\rm shell}(0))^{-1}dz,
\]
the transport matrices are
\[
M_i
=
P_*\left.\partial_{k_i}H_{\rm eff}(k)\right|_{k=k_*}P_*.
\]

If the locked branch symmetry enforces
\[
M_\parallel=\lambda_\parallel\sigma_3,\qquad
M_1=\alpha\sigma_1+\beta\sigma_2,\qquad
M_2=\alpha\sigma_2-\beta\sigma_1,
\]
then
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3M_\parallel),
\qquad
\alpha=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_1M_1+\sigma_2M_2),
\qquad
\beta=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_2M_1-\sigma_1M_2).
\]

Thus the microscopic Class II branch renormalizes the reduced invariants entirely through the projected derivative of the Schur-complement correction.

Finally, introducing overlap constants
\[
\lambda_\parallel=C_c g_c,\qquad
\alpha=C_E g_E,\qquad
\beta=C_O g_O,
\]
one obtains the exact extraction formulas
\[
g_c=\frac{\lambda_\parallel}{C_c},
\qquad
g_E=\frac{\alpha}{C_E},
\qquad
g_O=\frac{\beta}{C_O}.
\]

So the explicit working branch is now fully connected to the general microscopic coefficient-extraction formalism.
What remains is only the branch-specific algebra:
the explicit vertices \(\mathcal J,\mathcal K\), the locked Pauli selection rule, and the overlap integrals \(C_c,C_E,C_O\).

\section{Bloch-space current vertices and explicit Class II coefficient extraction}

We now continue the microscopic derivation by writing the explicit Bloch-space structure of the mixed vertices
\[
H_{\Psi X}(k)=\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k)
\]
for the refined locked + Class II working branch, and then deriving the corresponding renormalization formulas for
\[
(g_c,g_E,g_O).
\]

\section{Working microscopic branch and fluctuation space}

We start from the explicit working branch
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{\rm mic}
=
\mathcal L_{\Psi}^{\rm ref}[\Psi,P]
+\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+\alpha_X X_i^a J_i^a[\Psi,P]
+\beta_X X_i^a K_i^a[P,\Psi].
}
\]

Let
\[
(\bar\Psi,\bar P,\bar X)
\]
be a locked BCC stationary branch.
We write
\[
\Psi=\bar\Psi+\delta\Psi,
\qquad
X=\bar X+\delta X.
\]

If the quadratic fluctuation problem mixes \(\delta\Psi\) and \(\delta\Psi^\dagger\), then one should pass to the doubled Nambu field
\[
\Upsilon
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\delta\Psi\\
\delta\Psi^\dagger
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
All formulas below remain valid after replacing \(\delta\Psi\) by \(\Upsilon\).
For notational simplicity we denote the linear fluctuation field again by \(\Psi\).

\section{Linearized current operators}

The mixed Hessian block is determined by the linearization of the currents around the locked background.
Define the Fr\'echet derivatives
\[
\mathbb J_i^a[\bar\Psi,\bar P]\,\delta\Psi
:=
\left.\frac{d}{d\varepsilon}J_i^a[\bar\Psi+\varepsilon\delta\Psi,\bar P]\right|_{\varepsilon=0},
\]
\[
\mathbb K_i^a[\bar P,\bar\Psi]\,\delta\Psi
:=
\left.\frac{d}{d\varepsilon}K_i^a[\bar P,\bar\Psi+\varepsilon\delta\Psi]\right|_{\varepsilon=0}.
\]

Then the mixed quadratic vertex is
\[
\boxed{
H_{\Psi X}(x)
=
\alpha_X\,\mathbb J(x)+\beta_X\,\mathbb K(x),
}
\]
where \(\mathbb J(x)\) and \(\mathbb K(x)\) bundle the indices \((i,a)\).

For the working Class II branch, the natural general assumption is that these linearized current operators are local and at most first-order in spatial derivatives:
\[
\boxed{
\mathbb J_i^a
=
\mathbb A_i^a(x)+\mathbb B_{ij}^a(x)(-i\partial_j),
\qquad
\mathbb K_i^a
=
\mathbb C_i^a(x)+\mathbb D_{ij}^a(x)(-i\partial_j).
}
\]
Here \(\mathbb A,\mathbb B,\mathbb C,\mathbb D\) are periodic matrix-valued coefficient fields on the locked BCC background.
This is the correct universal form for the Bloch calculation.
No stronger assumption is needed at this stage.

\section{Bloch-harmonic expansion}

Let \(\Lambda^*\) be the reciprocal lattice of the locked BCC branch.
A Bloch fluctuation at quasi-momentum \(k\) is written as
\[
\Psi_k(x)
=
e^{ik\cdot x}u_k(x),
\qquad
u_k(x)=\sum_{G\in\Lambda^*}u_G(k)e^{iG\cdot x}.
\]

Likewise, if needed, the mediator fluctuation is expanded as
\[
X_{i}^{a}(x;k)
=
e^{ik\cdot x}\sum_{G\in\Lambda^*}x_{i}^{a}(G;k)e^{iG\cdot x}.
\]

Expand the periodic coefficient fields in Fourier series:
\[
\mathbb A_i^a(x)=\sum_{Q\in\Lambda^*}\mathbb A_i^a(Q)e^{iQ\cdot x},
\qquad
\mathbb B_{ij}^a(x)=\sum_{Q\in\Lambda^*}\mathbb B_{ij}^a(Q)e^{iQ\cdot x},
\]
\[
\mathbb C_i^a(x)=\sum_{Q\in\Lambda^*}\mathbb C_i^a(Q)e^{iQ\cdot x},
\qquad
\mathbb D_{ij}^a(x)=\sum_{Q\in\Lambda^*}\mathbb D_{ij}^a(Q)e^{iQ\cdot x}.
\]

Then the Bloch-space matrix elements of the current vertices are
\[
\boxed{
(\mathcal J_i^a(k))_{GG'}
=
\sum_{Q\in\Lambda^*}
\delta_{G,G'+Q}
\Bigl[
\mathbb A_i^a(Q)+\mathbb B_{ij}^a(Q)(k_j+G'_j)
\Bigr],
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
(\mathcal K_i^a(k))_{GG'}
=
\sum_{Q\in\Lambda^*}
\delta_{G,G'+Q}
\Bigl[
\mathbb C_i^a(Q)+\mathbb D_{ij}^a(Q)(k_j+G'_j)
\Bigr].
}
\]

Therefore the exact mixed Bloch block is
\[
\boxed{
(H_{\Psi X}(k))_{GG';\,ia}
=
\alpha_X(\mathcal J_i^a(k))_{GG'}
+
\beta_X(\mathcal K_i^a(k))_{GG'}.
}
\]

This is the explicit universal harmonic-space vertex formula.

\section{Bragg-point derivative of the mixed vertex}

Because the dependence on \(k\) is affine at first-order differential level, the \(k\)-derivative is immediate:
\[
\boxed{
\left(\partial_{k_\ell}\mathcal J_i^a(k)\right)_{GG'}
=
\sum_{Q\in\Lambda^*}
\delta_{G,G'+Q}\,
\mathbb B_{i\ell}^a(Q),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\left(\partial_{k_\ell}\mathcal K_i^a(k)\right)_{GG'}
=
\sum_{Q\in\Lambda^*}
\delta_{G,G'+Q}\,
\mathbb D_{i\ell}^a(Q).
}
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
\partial_{k_\ell}H_{\Psi X}(k)
=
\alpha_X\,\partial_{k_\ell}\mathcal J(k)
+\beta_X\,\partial_{k_\ell}\mathcal K(k).
}
\]

Evaluating at the folded Bragg point \(k_*=G_*/2\) gives the exact first-order transport data required for the valley reduction.

\section{Schur-complement correction in the pure auxiliary Class II truncation}

At the working level, the heavy mediator block is
\[
\boxed{
H_{XX}(k)=M_X^2\,\mathbf 1_X
}
\]
up to subleading algebraic background corrections.
Thus
\[
H_{XX}^{-1}(k)=M_X^{-2}\mathbf 1_X
\]
and the heavy-mediated correction is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta H_{\rm eff}(k)
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\bigl(\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k)\bigr)
\bigl(\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k)\bigr)^\dagger.
}
\]

Expanding by channels,
\[
\boxed{
\Delta H_{\rm eff}(k)
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\,\mathcal J\mathcal J^\dagger
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,(\mathcal J\mathcal K^\dagger+\mathcal K\mathcal J^\dagger)
-\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\,\mathcal K\mathcal K^\dagger.
}
\]

This is the exact Class II quadratic renormalization of the shell operator.

\section{Derivative of the effective operator}

Differentiating the Schur correction gives
\[
\boxed{
\partial_{k_\ell}\Delta H_{\rm eff}(k)
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\Bigl[
(\partial_{k_\ell}\mathcal V)\mathcal V^\dagger
+
\mathcal V(\partial_{k_\ell}\mathcal V^\dagger)
\Bigr],
}
\]
where
\[
\mathcal V(k):=\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k).
\]

Expanding by channels,
\[
\partial_{k_\ell}\Delta H_{\rm eff}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\,\mathfrak D_\ell^{JJ}
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,\mathfrak D_\ell^{JK}
-\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\,\mathfrak D_\ell^{KK},
\]
with
\[
\mathfrak D_\ell^{JJ}
:=
(\partial_{k_\ell}\mathcal J)\mathcal J^\dagger
+
\mathcal J(\partial_{k_\ell}\mathcal J^\dagger),
\]
\[
\mathfrak D_\ell^{JK}
:=
(\partial_{k_\ell}\mathcal J)\mathcal K^\dagger
+
\mathcal J(\partial_{k_\ell}\mathcal K^\dagger)
+
(\partial_{k_\ell}\mathcal K)\mathcal J^\dagger
+
\mathcal K(\partial_{k_\ell}\mathcal J^\dagger),
\]
\[
\mathfrak D_\ell^{KK}
:=
(\partial_{k_\ell}\mathcal K)\mathcal K^\dagger
+
\mathcal K(\partial_{k_\ell}\mathcal K^\dagger).
\]

The total transport operator is therefore
\[
\boxed{
K_\ell
=
\left.\partial_{k_\ell}H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)\right|_{k=k_*}
-
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\,\mathfrak D_\ell^{JJ}(k_*)
-
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,\mathfrak D_\ell^{JK}(k_*)
-
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\,\mathfrak D_\ell^{KK}(k_*).
}
\]

\section{Valley projection and Pauli decomposition}

Let
\[
P_*
=
\frac{1}{2\pi i}\oint_\Gamma (z-H_{\rm shell}(0))^{-1}dz
\]
be the exact Riesz projector onto the low valley doublet.
Define
\[
M_\ell:=P_*K_\ell P_*.
\]

In an adapted defect frame \((\hat n,e_1,e_2)\), let
\[
M_\parallel=\hat n_\ell M_\ell,
\qquad
M_1=e_{1\ell}M_\ell,
\qquad
M_2=e_{2\ell}M_\ell.
\]

Under the locked branch symmetry selection rule,
\[
M_\parallel=\lambda_\parallel \sigma_3,
\qquad
M_1=\alpha \sigma_1+\beta \sigma_2,
\qquad
M_2=\alpha \sigma_2-\beta \sigma_1.
\]

Thus the exact reduced coefficients are
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3M_\parallel),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\alpha=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_1M_1+\sigma_2M_2),
\qquad
\beta=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_2M_1-\sigma_1M_2).
}
\]

\section{Exact Class II renormalization of }(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)

Split
\[
M_\mu=M_\mu^{\rm ref}+\Delta M_\mu.
\]
Then
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\lambda_\parallel^{\rm ref}+\Delta\lambda_\parallel,
\qquad
\alpha=\alpha^{\rm ref}+\Delta\alpha,
\qquad
\beta=\beta^{\rm ref}+\Delta\beta,
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
\Delta\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_c^{JJ}
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\Lambda_c^{JK}
-\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_c^{KK},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\Delta\alpha
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_E^{JJ}
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\Lambda_E^{JK}
-\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_E^{KK},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\Delta\beta
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_O^{JJ}
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\Lambda_O^{JK}
-\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_O^{KK},
}
\]
where the channel overlaps are defined by the projected Pauli traces
\[
\Lambda_c^{UV}
:=
\frac12\Tr\!\Bigl(
\sigma_3\,P_*(\hat n_\ell\,\mathfrak D_\ell^{UV}(k_*))P_*
\Bigr),
\]
\[
\Lambda_E^{UV}
:=
\frac14\Tr\!\Bigl(
\sigma_1\,P_*(e_{1\ell}\mathfrak D_\ell^{UV}(k_*))P_*
+
\sigma_2\,P_*(e_{2\ell}\mathfrak D_\ell^{UV}(k_*))P_*
\Bigr),
\]
\[
\Lambda_O^{UV}
:=
\frac14\Tr\!\Bigl(
\sigma_2\,P_*(e_{1\ell}\mathfrak D_\ell^{UV}(k_*))P_*
-
\sigma_1\,P_*(e_{2\ell}\mathfrak D_\ell^{UV}(k_*))P_*
\Bigr),
\]
with
\[
(U,V)\in\{(J,J),(J,K),(K,K)\}.
\]

This is the exact microscopic Class II renormalization formula for the reduced locked coefficients.

\section{Extraction of }(g_c,g_E,g_O)

Introduce the exact overlap constants
\[
\lambda_\parallel=C_c\,g_c,
\qquad
\alpha=C_E\,g_E,
\qquad
\beta=C_O\,g_O.
\]
Then
\[
\boxed{
g_c=\frac{\lambda_\parallel}{C_c},
\qquad
g_E=\frac{\alpha}{C_E},
\qquad
g_O=\frac{\beta}{C_O}.
}
\]

Substituting the Class II renormalized coefficients,
\[
\boxed{
g_c
=
\frac{\lambda_\parallel^{\rm ref}}{C_c}
-
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\frac{\Lambda_c^{JJ}}{C_c}
-
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\frac{\Lambda_c^{JK}}{C_c}
-
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\frac{\Lambda_c^{KK}}{C_c},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
g_E
=
\frac{\alpha^{\rm ref}}{C_E}
-
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\frac{\Lambda_E^{JJ}}{C_E}
-
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\frac{\Lambda_E^{JK}}{C_E}
-
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\frac{\Lambda_E^{KK}}{C_E},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
g_O
=
\frac{\beta^{\rm ref}}{C_O}
-
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\frac{\Lambda_O^{JJ}}{C_O}
-
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\frac{\Lambda_O^{JK}}{C_O}
-
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\frac{\Lambda_O^{KK}}{C_O}.
}
\]

Only after explicit overlap evaluation may one specialize
\[
C_c=\frac12 I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
C_E=I_\theta^{(E)},
\qquad
C_O=I_\theta^{(O)},
\]
and, if the locked branch symmetry enforces it,
\[
I_\theta^{(E)}=I_\theta^{(O)}=:I_\theta.
\]

\section{What is now closed}

At the working branch level, the following are now explicit:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the universal Bloch-harmonic form of the mixed current vertices;
\item the exact Schur-complement correction generated by the heavy Class II mediator;
\item the exact \(k\)-derivative formula for the effective transport operator;
\item the projected Pauli-trace extraction of \((\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)\);
\item the exact channel decomposition of the Class II renormalization of \((g_c,g_E,g_O)\).
\end{enumerate}

\section{What remains branch-specific}

Only three branch-specific algebraic ingredients remain to be inserted:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the explicit Fourier coefficients
\[
\mathbb A_i^a(Q),\ \mathbb B_{ij}^a(Q),\ \mathbb C_i^a(Q),\ \mathbb D_{ij}^a(Q);
\]
\item the locked-branch proof that the projected transport matrices have the special Pauli form;
\item the actual overlap evaluation of
\[
C_c,\ C_E,\ C_O.
\]
\end{enumerate}

These are no longer conceptual gaps.
They are the remaining explicit calculations of the chosen working branch.

\section{Final summary}

For the refined locked + Class II working branch, the mixed Bloch vertex has the universal harmonic-space form
\[
H_{\Psi X}(k)=\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k),
\]
where, under the natural first-order local-current assumption,
\[
(\mathcal J_i^a(k))_{GG'}
=
\sum_Q \delta_{G,G'+Q}
\Bigl[
\mathbb A_i^a(Q)+\mathbb B_{ij}^a(Q)(k_j+G'_j)
\Bigr],
\]
\[
(\mathcal K_i^a(k))_{GG'}
=
\sum_Q \delta_{G,G'+Q}
\Bigl[
\mathbb C_i^a(Q)+\mathbb D_{ij}^a(Q)(k_j+G'_j)
\Bigr].
\]

In the pure auxiliary Class II truncation,
\[
H_{XX}(k)=M_X^2\mathbf 1_X,
\]
so the heavy-mediated correction is exactly
\[
\Delta H_{\rm eff}(k)
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\bigl(\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k)\bigr)
\bigl(\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k)\bigr)^\dagger.
\]

Differentiating at the Bragg point and projecting to the exact valley doublet yields
\[
M_i=P_*\left.\partial_{k_i}H_{\rm eff}(k)\right|_{k=k_*}P_*.
\]

Under the locked Pauli selection rule,
\[
M_\parallel=\lambda_\parallel\sigma_3,\qquad
M_1=\alpha\sigma_1+\beta\sigma_2,\qquad
M_2=\alpha\sigma_2-\beta\sigma_1,
\]
so
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3M_\parallel),
\qquad
\alpha=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_1M_1+\sigma_2M_2),
\qquad
\beta=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_2M_1-\sigma_1M_2).
\]

Thus the Class II mediator renormalizes the reduced invariants by
\[
\Delta\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_c^{JJ}
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\Lambda_c^{JK}
-\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_c^{KK},
\]
\[
\Delta\alpha
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_E^{JJ}
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\Lambda_E^{JK}
-\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_E^{KK},
\]
\[
\Delta\beta
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_O^{JJ}
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\Lambda_O^{JK}
-\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\Lambda_O^{KK}.
\]

Finally,
\[
g_c=\frac{\lambda_\parallel}{C_c},\qquad
g_E=\frac{\alpha}{C_E},\qquad
g_O=\frac{\beta}{C_O},
\]
with \(C_c,C_E,C_O\) determined by explicit overlap integrals.

Therefore the only remaining work is branch-specific algebra:
the explicit Fourier-space current coefficients, the locked Pauli selection-rule proof, and the overlap integrals.

\section{Block-norm and Gershgorin budget theorem for the final remote-gap slot}

\section{Setup}

Let
\[
H_R(p)=D_R(p)+R_R(p),
\qquad |p|\le \rho,
\]
act on the remote sector \(\mathcal H_R\), and assume that for every \(|p|\le \rho\),
\[
H_R(p)=H_R(p)^\dagger,
\qquad
D_R(p)=D_R(p)^\dagger,
\qquad
R_R(p)=R_R(p)^\dagger.
\]

We assume that \(D_R(p)\) is the benchmark remote operator and \(R_R(p)\) is the residual remote mixing/remainder.

Define the benchmark gap
\[
\delta_{0,\rho}
:=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(0,\operatorname{spec}(D_R(p))\bigr).
\]
Define also the residual norm budget
\[
\eta_{R,\rho}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_R(p)\|.
\]

Then the basic perturbative spectral isolation criterion is:

\paragraph{Lemma (uniform perturbative remote-gap criterion).}
If
\[
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho},
\]
then
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap
\bigl(-\Delta_\rho,\Delta_\rho\bigr)=\varnothing,
\qquad
\Delta_\rho:=\delta_{0,\rho}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0,
\]
for all \(|p|\le \rho\).

\paragraph{Proof.}
By standard spectral stability for self-adjoint bounded perturbations,
\[
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(0,\operatorname{spec}(D_R(p)+R_R(p))\bigr)
\ge
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(0,\operatorname{spec}(D_R(p))\bigr)-\|R_R(p)\|.
\]
Taking the infimum in \(p\) gives the claim.
\(\square\)

Thus the only remaining task is to produce usable upper bounds on \(\eta_{R,\rho}\).

\section{Sectorwise block decomposition}

At the minimal truncation level, suppose
\[
\mathcal H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong}}.
\]

Write the residual block in sector form
\[
R_R(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & R_{\mathrm{vol,high}} & R_{\mathrm{vol,non}} & R_{\mathrm{vol,wrong}}\\
R_{\mathrm{high,vol}} & 0 & R_{\mathrm{high,non}} & R_{\mathrm{high,wrong}}\\
R_{\mathrm{non,vol}} & R_{\mathrm{non,high}} & 0 & R_{\mathrm{non,wrong}}\\
R_{\mathrm{wrong,vol}} & R_{\mathrm{wrong,high}} & R_{\mathrm{wrong,non}} & 0
\end{pmatrix}(p),
\]
where
\[
R_{ab}(p):\mathcal H_b\to \mathcal H_a.
\]

Define the pairwise block budgets
\[
\eta_{ab,\rho}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_{ab}(p)\|.
\]

\section{Basic block-norm budget}

Since
\[
R_R(p)=\sum_{a\neq b} E_{ab}R_{ab}(p),
\]
where \(E_{ab}R_{ab}(p)\) denotes the operator with only the \((a,b)\) block nonzero,
the triangle inequality gives
\[
\|R_R(p)\|
\le
\sum_{a\neq b}\|R_{ab}(p)\|.
\]
Hence
\[
\boxed{
\eta_{R,\rho}
\le
\sum_{a\neq b}\eta_{ab,\rho}.
}
\]

Therefore a sufficient explicit criterion for remote isolation is
\[
\boxed{
\delta_{0,\rho}
>
\sum_{a\neq b}\eta_{ab,\rho}.
}
\]

This bound is crude but rigorous.

\section{Gershgorin budget for the finite truncated remote matrix}

Assume now that \(H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(p)\) is represented in a finite orthonormal basis of the truncated remote space.
Let
\[
(H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(p))_{mn}
\]
be its matrix elements, and define the row sums
\[
\mathcal R_m(p):=
\sum_{n\neq m}\bigl|(H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(p))_{mn}\bigr|.
\]

Define the Gershgorin lower bound
\[
\Delta_{G,\rho}
:=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\min_m
\Bigl(
\bigl|(H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(p))_{mm}\bigr|
-
\mathcal R_m(p)
\Bigr).
\]

If
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{G,\rho}>0,
}
\]
then by Gershgorin's theorem and self-adjointness,
\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{spec}(H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(p))
\cap
(-\Delta_{G,\rho},\Delta_{G,\rho})
=
\varnothing
\qquad (|p|\le \rho).
}
\]

This route is often sharper than the block-norm budget when the truncated remote matrix is sparse.

\section{Full remote completion}

For the full remote sector, let
\[
H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p)=D_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)+R_{\mathrm{rem}}(p),
\]
where \(D_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)\) is the full benchmark operator and \(R_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)\) contains:

\begin{enumerate}
\item all off-diagonal remote--remote couplings,
\item all couplings to tail sectors,
\item all bounded residual corrections to the diagonal benchmark.
\end{enumerate}

Define
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)\|,
\]
and let
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}
\]
be any explicit lower bound such that
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}
\le
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(0,\operatorname{spec}(D_{\mathrm{rem}}(p))\bigr).
}
\]

Then the sufficient final Task IV criterion is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}
>
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\]

Under this condition,
\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{spec}(H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p))
\cap
(-\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho},\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho})
=
\varnothing,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}-\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}>0.
}
\]

\section{Explicit power-counting / heavy-suppression budget}

By the previously established tail-coupling estimate theorem, one may assume
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
\le
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}
K_a\,\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}
\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a},
\qquad
r_a\ge 1.
\]

Thus all remote mixing is at least \(O(\rho)\) near the crossing, and heavy-mediated sectors carry additional inverse-mass suppression.

\section{Final closure statement}

Therefore the final remote-gap slot is closed once one supplies an explicit benchmark lower bound
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}
\]
for the benchmark operator \(D_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)\) and verifies
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}
>
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}
K_a\,\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}
\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a}.
}
\]

This is the cleanest final Task IV criterion.

\section{Model-specific benchmark lower bound}

Assume the benchmark operator \(D_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)\) is block-diagonal across the remote sectors and that the following explicit lower bounds have already been established on \(|p|\le \rho\):
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho},
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{high},\rho},
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int},\rho},
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}.
\]
Then one may take
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}
=
\min\Bigl\{
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho},
\Delta_{\mathrm{high},\rho},
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int},\rho},
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\Bigr\}.
}
\]

If, for example, the previously derived explicit lower bounds are
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho}=4K-|r_*|,\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{high},\rho}=\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\]
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int},\rho}
=
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|,
\]
then these may be inserted directly into the minimum above, provided each term is already known to be positive on the regime of interest.

\section{Final summary}

The proposed block-norm / Gershgorin budget strategy for the final remote-gap slot is mathematically correct in structure.

The main logic is:

\[
H_R(p)=D_R(p)+R_R(p),
\qquad
\delta_{0,\rho}
=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(0,\operatorname{spec}(D_R(p))\bigr),
\qquad
\eta_{R,\rho}
=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_R(p)\|.
\]

If
\[
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho},
\]
then
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta_\rho,\Delta_\rho)=\varnothing,
\qquad
\Delta_\rho=\delta_{0,\rho}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0.
\]

The block budget
\[
\eta_{R,\rho}\le \sum_{a\neq b}\eta_{ab,\rho}
\]
is a valid crude norm estimate.

The Gershgorin route is also valid, but should be stated explicitly for the finite truncated remote matrix.

For the full remote completion, the clean final condition is
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho},
\]
where
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}
\le
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(0,\operatorname{spec}(D_{\mathrm{rem}}(p))\bigr).
\]

Thus the theorem is essentially correct, but to be fully closed and submission-safe it should explicitly include:

\begin{enumerate}
\item self-adjointness of \(H_R,D_R,R_R\);
\item the benchmark gap defined as a spectral distance, not merely as a diagonal heuristic;
\item a clear statement that the Gershgorin part applies to the finite truncated remote matrix;
\item a cleaned-up model-specific formula for \(\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}\).
\end{enumerate}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Block-norm and Gershgorin budget theorem for the final remote-gap slot}

\section{Setup}

Let
\[
H_R(p)=D_R(p)+R_R(p),
\qquad |p|\le \rho,
\]
be the remote-sector operator on a Hilbert space \(\mathcal H_R\).
Assume that for each \(|p|\le \rho\),
\[
H_R(p)=H_R(p)^\dagger,
\qquad
D_R(p)=D_R(p)^\dagger,
\qquad
R_R(p)=R_R(p)^\dagger.
\]

Here \(D_R(p)\) is the benchmark remote operator and \(R_R(p)\) is the residual remote mixing/remainder.

Define the benchmark spectral distance
\[
\delta_{0,\rho}
:=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(0,\operatorname{spec}(D_R(p))\bigr),
\]
and the residual norm budget
\[
\eta_{R,\rho}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_R(p)\|.
\]

\section{Uniform perturbative remote-gap criterion}

\paragraph{Theorem 1 (uniform remote-gap criterion).}
If
\[
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho},
\]
then
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))
\cap
(-\Delta_\rho,\Delta_\rho)
=
\varnothing
\qquad (|p|\le \rho),
\]
where
\[
\Delta_\rho:=\delta_{0,\rho}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0.
\]

\paragraph{Proof.}
Fix \(|p|\le \rho\).
Since \(D_R(p)\) and \(R_R(p)\) are self-adjoint, standard spectral stability under bounded self-adjoint perturbations gives
\[
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(0,\operatorname{spec}(D_R(p)+R_R(p))\bigr)
\ge
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(0,\operatorname{spec}(D_R(p))\bigr)-\|R_R(p)\|.
\]
Hence
\[
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(0,\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\bigr)
\ge
\delta_{0,\rho}-\eta_{R,\rho}
=
\Delta_\rho>0.
\]
Therefore
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))
\cap
(-\Delta_\rho,\Delta_\rho)
=
\varnothing.
\]
Since the bound is uniform in \(|p|\le \rho\), the claim follows.
\(\square\)

\section{Sectorwise block decomposition}

Assume now that the minimal truncated remote space splits as
\[
\mathcal H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}.
\]

Write the off-diagonal residual block as
\[
R_R(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & R_{\mathrm{vol,high}} & R_{\mathrm{vol,non}} & R_{\mathrm{vol,wrong}}\\
R_{\mathrm{high,vol}} & 0 & R_{\mathrm{high,non}} & R_{\mathrm{high,wrong}}\\
R_{\mathrm{non,vol}} & R_{\mathrm{non,high}} & 0 & R_{\mathrm{non,wrong}}\\
R_{\mathrm{wrong,vol}} & R_{\mathrm{wrong,high}} & R_{\mathrm{wrong,non}} & 0
\end{pmatrix}(p),
\]
where
\[
R_{ab}(p):\mathcal H_b\to\mathcal H_a
\]
are the pairwise off-diagonal couplings.

Define the pairwise budgets
\[
\eta_{ab,\rho}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_{ab}(p)\|.
\]

\paragraph{Proposition 2 (basic block-norm budget).}
One has the crude but rigorous estimate
\[
\eta_{R,\rho}
\le
\sum_{a\neq b}\eta_{ab,\rho}.
\]

\paragraph{Proof.}
For each \(|p|\le \rho\),
\[
R_R(p)=\sum_{a\neq b} E_{ab}R_{ab}(p),
\]
where \(E_{ab}R_{ab}(p)\) denotes the operator with only the \((a,b)\)-block nonzero.
By the triangle inequality,
\[
\|R_R(p)\|
\le
\sum_{a\neq b}\|R_{ab}(p)\|.
\]
Taking the supremum over \(|p|\le \rho\) yields
\[
\eta_{R,\rho}
\le
\sum_{a\neq b}\eta_{ab,\rho}.
\]
\(\square\)

\paragraph{Corollary 3 (block-budget remote isolation).}
If
\[
\delta_{0,\rho}
>
\sum_{a\neq b}\eta_{ab,\rho},
\]
then
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))
\cap
(-\Delta_\rho,\Delta_\rho)
=
\varnothing
\qquad (|p|\le \rho),
\]
with
\[
\Delta_\rho
\ge
\delta_{0,\rho}-\sum_{a\neq b}\eta_{ab,\rho}>0.
\]

\section{Gershgorin budget for the finite truncated remote matrix}

We now assume that \(H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(p)\) is represented in a finite orthonormal basis of the truncated remote space.
Let
\[
(H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(p))_{mn}
\]
denote the corresponding matrix elements.

Define the row sums
\[
\mathcal R_m(p)
:=
\sum_{n\neq m}\bigl|(H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(p))_{mn}\bigr|.
\]

Define the uniform Gershgorin budget
\[
\Delta_{G,\rho}
:=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}
\min_m
\Bigl(
\bigl|(H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(p))_{mm}\bigr|
-
\mathcal R_m(p)
\Bigr).
\]

\paragraph{Theorem 4 (Gershgorin remote-gap criterion for the finite truncation).}
If
\[
\Delta_{G,\rho}>0,
\]
then
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(p))
\cap
(-\Delta_{G,\rho},\Delta_{G,\rho})
=
\varnothing
\qquad (|p|\le \rho).
\]

\paragraph{Proof.}
For each fixed \(|p|\le \rho\), Gershgorin's circle theorem implies that every eigenvalue \(\lambda\in\operatorname{spec}(H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(p))\) belongs to at least one disk
\[
|\lambda-(H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(p))_{mm}|\le \mathcal R_m(p).
\]
Hence
\[
|\lambda|
\ge
\bigl|(H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(p))_{mm}\bigr|-\mathcal R_m(p)
\]
for some \(m\), and therefore
\[
|\lambda|
\ge
\min_m
\Bigl(
\bigl|(H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(p))_{mm}\bigr|-\mathcal R_m(p)
\Bigr)
\ge
\Delta_{G,\rho}>0.
\]
Thus
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(p))
\cap
(-\Delta_{G,\rho},\Delta_{G,\rho})
=
\varnothing.
\]
Since the bound is uniform in \(|p|\le \rho\), the claim follows.
\(\square\)

\section{Full remote completion with tails}

For the full remote sector, write
\[
H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p)=D_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)+R_{\mathrm{rem}}(p),
\]
where:

\begin{itemize}
\item \(D_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)\) is the global benchmark remote operator;
\item \(R_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)\) contains all off-diagonal remote--remote mixing, all couplings to tail sectors, and all bounded residual corrections to the benchmark part.
\end{itemize}

Assume
\[
H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p)=H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p)^\dagger,
\qquad
D_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)=D_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)^\dagger,
\qquad
R_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)=R_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)^\dagger.
\]

Define
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)\|,
\]
and let
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}
\]
be any explicit lower bound satisfying
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}
\le
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(0,\operatorname{spec}(D_{\mathrm{rem}}(p))\bigr).
}
\]

\paragraph{Theorem 5 (final Task IV remote isolation criterion).}
If
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}
>
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho},
}
\]
then
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p))
\cap
(-\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho},\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho})
=
\varnothing
\qquad (|p|\le \rho),
\]
with
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}-\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}>0.
\]

\paragraph{Proof.}
Apply Theorem 1 with
\[
D_R=D_{\mathrm{rem}},
\qquad
R_R=R_{\mathrm{rem}},
\qquad
\delta_{0,\rho}
=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(0,\operatorname{spec}(D_{\mathrm{rem}}(p))\bigr).
\]
Since
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}\le \delta_{0,\rho},
\]
the inequality
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
\]
implies
\[
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
\]
The claim follows immediately from Theorem 1.
\(\square\)

\section{Explicit power-counting / heavy-suppression budget}

Assume the previously established tail-coupling estimate theorem gives
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
\le
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}
K_a\,\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}
\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a},
\qquad
r_a\ge 1.
\]

Then all remote mixing is at least \(O(\rho)\) near the crossing, and heavy-mediated sectors carry additional inverse-mass suppression.

Hence a fully explicit sufficient final criterion is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}
>
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}
K_a\,\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}
\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a}.
}
\]

\section{Model-specific benchmark lower bound}

Assume the benchmark operator \(D_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)\) is block-diagonal across the remote sectors, and that the following explicit lower bounds have already been established for \(|p|\le \rho\):
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho},
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{high},\rho},
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int},\rho},
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}.
\]

Then one may take
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}
=
\min\Bigl\{
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho},
\Delta_{\mathrm{high},\rho},
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int},\rho},
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\Bigr\}.
}
\]

If, for example, the explicit lower bounds are
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho}=4K-|r_*|,
\]
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{high},\rho}
=
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\]
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int},\rho}
=
q_*^2
\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|,
\]
then these may be inserted directly into the minimum above, provided each quantity is already known to be positive in the parameter regime under consideration.

\section{Final closure statement}

Therefore the final remote-gap slot is closed once one has:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a self-adjoint benchmark decomposition
\[
H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p)=D_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)+R_{\mathrm{rem}}(p);
\]

\item an explicit lower bound
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}
\le
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(0,\operatorname{spec}(D_{\mathrm{rem}}(p))\bigr);
\]

\item an explicit residual budget bound
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
\le
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}
K_a\,\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}
\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Under the single inequality
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}
>
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho},
}
\]
the complete remote block is uniformly spectrally isolated from zero.

\section{Final summary}

We rewrote the final remote-gap slot in a fully submission-safe form.

The key definitions are:
\[
H_R(p)=D_R(p)+R_R(p),
\qquad
\delta_{0,\rho}
=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(0,\operatorname{spec}(D_R(p))\bigr),
\qquad
\eta_{R,\rho}
=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_R(p)\|.
\]

If
\[
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho},
\]
then
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta_\rho,\Delta_\rho)=\varnothing,
\qquad
\Delta_\rho=\delta_{0,\rho}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0.
\]

For the finite truncated remote matrix, a sharper alternative is the Gershgorin bound
\[
\Delta_{G,\rho}
=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\min_m
\Bigl(
|(H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(p))_{mm}|-\mathcal R_m(p)
\Bigr),
\]
which implies spectral isolation whenever \(\Delta_{G,\rho}>0\).

For the full remote completion, let
\[
H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p)=D_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)+R_{\mathrm{rem}}(p),
\qquad
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)\|.
\]
If
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}
\le
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(0,\operatorname{spec}(D_{\mathrm{rem}}(p))\bigr)
\]
and
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho},
\]
then
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R^{\mathrm{full}}(p))
\cap
(-\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho},\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho})
=
\varnothing,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{full},\rho}
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}-\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}>0.
\]

Thus the final Task IV closure reduces to an explicit benchmark lower bound plus an explicit residual mixing budget.

\section{Status report: what the main task actually was, and what is and is not finished}

The main program was never merely the remote-gap theorem or the exploratory CKM fitting by itself.
The actual main line has been

\[
\boxed{
\text{TECT microscopic defect PDE}
\;\longrightarrow\;
\text{single-defect light mode}
\;\longrightarrow\;
\text{three-defect family projector}
\;\longrightarrow\;
\text{Schur-complement reduced operator}
\;\longrightarrow\;
\text{Dirac/valley block and microscopic flavor coefficients.}
}
\]

Equivalently, the main target has been
\[
\boxed{
\mathbb O_{\rm 1def}^{(0)}
\to
P_L
\to
\mathcal Y_{\rm eff}
\to
(B_0,B_1,B_H)
\to
(H_Q,H_u,H_d,\dots)
\to
(g_c,g_E,g_O)
\to
\text{flavor/CKM structure.}
}
\]

\section{What is essentially finished}

Several important auxiliary layers are now essentially closed.

\paragraph{(i) Exploratory flavor existence stage.}
At the reduced-model level, one already has strong numerical evidence that the flavor problem is nonempty:
hierarchical CKM-like mixing exists, and CP-violating branches with
\[
J\neq 0,\qquad \delta\neq 0
\]
exist as well.
Thus the existential stage has done its job.

\paragraph{(ii) Reduced operator formalism.}
The abstract Schur-complement structure is already in place:
\[
\mathcal Y_{\rm eff}=L-KH^{-1}K^\dagger,
\]
together with the Hermitian basis decomposition
\[
\{D_0,D_1,D_2,S_{12},S_{13},S_{23},A_{12},A_{13},A_{23}\}.
\]
The reduced CP-odd coefficients have already been identified as heavy-mediated imaginary overlaps.

\paragraph{(iii) Remote-gap / Task IV closure theorem.}
The remote spectral isolation module is now essentially complete as an auxiliary theorem:
the block-norm and Gershgorin budget strategy has been rewritten in a submission-safe form.
So this part should be regarded as an almost-finished support theorem, not as the main unfinished bottleneck.

\section{What is not finished}

The main program is not finished, because the genuinely TECT-specific microscopic input has not yet been derived.

\paragraph{(a) Actual TECT reference operator.}
The form
\[
\mathbb O_{\rm 1def}^{(0)}
=
i\widetilde\Gamma^i_{\rm def}(\partial_i+\Omega_i^{\rm def})+\Phi_{\rm def}
\]
has been established only as an abstract operator-theoretic template.
It has not yet been derived from the actual microscopic TECT PDE.

\paragraph{(b) One defect \(\leftrightarrow\) one light mode.}
The abstract theorem schema
\[
\text{Callias-type structure}
+
\text{bulk gap}
+
\text{grading}
+
\operatorname{Ind}=1
\Longrightarrow
\text{one protected light mode}
\]
has been identified, but the actual TECT index computation has not been done.
So the statement
\[
\text{``one defect carries one family mode''}
\]
is still conditional, not yet a first-principles theorem of TECT.

\paragraph{(c) Explicit Class II microscopic coefficient extraction.}
The explicit working branch
\[
\mathcal L_{\rm mic}
=
\mathcal L_\Psi^{\rm ref}
+\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+\alpha_X X_i^aJ_i^a
+\beta_X X_i^aK_i^a
\]
has already been connected to the abstract Schur-complement formalism,
and the universal Bloch-vertex structure has been written down.

However, the actual branch-specific Fourier coefficients
\[
\mathbb A,\ \mathbb B,\ \mathbb C,\ \mathbb D
\]
have not yet been inserted and evaluated.
So this stage is structurally organized but not numerically/computationally completed.

\section{Correct current conclusion}

Therefore the correct status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{many supporting layers are finished or nearly finished,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{the main TECT-specific microscopic extraction problem is not yet finished.}
}
\]

In more operational terms:
\[
\boxed{
\text{existence, abstract structure, and auxiliary isolation theorems are largely in place;}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{actual microscopic coefficient extraction from the TECT defect background remains the main unfinished task.}
}
\]

\section{Immediate next step}

The correct next step is no longer another auxiliary theorem.
It is to return to the main line and specify a minimal actual TECT microscopic field content,
write the corresponding
\[
K^0(\mathfrak B),\qquad K^i(\mathfrak B),\qquad \mathcal M(\mathfrak B),
\]
linearize around a defect background, and then compute
\[
G^0_{\rm def},\quad G^i_{\rm def},\quad M_{\rm def},
\]
followed by
\[
P_L,\qquad V_{ab}^{(I)},\qquad K_{a\alpha}^{(I)},\qquad E_\alpha.
\]

Only that step will turn the current framework into a first-principles microscopic coefficient extraction.

\section{Final summary}

The main task was not merely the remote-gap theorem or the exploratory CKM fit.
The actual main program has been

\[
\text{TECT defect PDE}
\to
\text{single-defect light mode}
\to
\text{three-defect family projector}
\to
\text{Schur-complement reduced operator}
\to
\text{microscopic flavor coefficients.}
\]

At present:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the exploratory flavor existence stage is essentially finished;
\item the abstract reduced-operator formalism is in place;
\item the remote-gap / Task IV theorem is essentially finished as an auxiliary support result;
\item but the genuinely TECT-specific microscopic coefficient extraction is not finished.
\end{enumerate}

The unfinished core is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{derive the actual TECT defect fluctuation operator, verify the one-mode structure, and compute the explicit microscopic overlap coefficients.}
}
\]

So the honest status is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the support theorems are largely in place, but the main microscopic extraction problem is still open.}
}
\]

\section{Minimal microscopic multiplet and explicit coefficient extraction template}

We now fix a minimal structurally correct microscopic working ansatz for the TECT coefficient-extraction program.

\section{Minimal working microscopic multiplet}

The smallest multiplet that can support the previously derived operator-theoretic program is
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak B=(P^A,\Psi,X_i^a).
}
\]

Here:

\begin{itemize}
\item \(P^A(x,t)\) is the locked condensate / order-parameter background field;
\item \(\Psi(x,t)\) is the bundle-valued fluctuation field whose low spectral sector is ultimately projected onto the family space;
\item \(X_i^a(x,t)\) is the heavy Class II mediator field.
\end{itemize}

This is not yet claimed to be the unique microscopic TECT field content.
It is the minimal working multiplet sufficient for actual coefficient extraction.

\section{Minimal first-order Hermitian microscopic action}

We take the microscopic working action to be
\[
\boxed{
S[P,\Psi,X]
=
\int dt\,d^3x\;
\Bigl(
\mathcal L_P[P]
+
\mathcal L_{\Psi}^{\rm ref}[\Psi,P]
+
\mathcal L_X[X]
+
\mathcal L_{\Psi X}[\Psi,P,X]
\Bigr),
}
\]
with the pieces defined as follows.

\paragraph{Reference \(\Psi\)-sector.}
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{\Psi}^{\rm ref}
=
\frac{i}{2}\Psi^\dagger Z^0(P)\!\stackrel{\leftrightarrow}{\partial_t}\!\Psi
+
\frac{i}{2}\Psi^\dagger Z^i(P)\!\stackrel{\leftrightarrow}{\partial_i}\!\Psi
-
\Psi^\dagger M_0(P)\Psi.
}
\]

\paragraph{Heavy mediator sector.}
At the present working truncation level,
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal L_X=\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a.
}
\]
This is the auxiliary heavy Class II truncation used throughout the current extraction branch.

\paragraph{Class II couplings.}
We now choose the explicit local-current ansatz
\[
\boxed{
J_i^a[\Psi,P]
=
\Psi^\dagger A_i^a(P)\Psi
+
\frac{i}{2}\Psi^\dagger B_{ij}^a(P)\!\stackrel{\leftrightarrow}{\partial_j}\!\Psi,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
K_i^a[P,\Psi]
=
\Psi^\dagger C_i^a(P)\Psi
+
\frac{i}{2}\Psi^\dagger D_{ij}^a(P)\!\stackrel{\leftrightarrow}{\partial_j}\!\Psi.
}
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{\Psi X}
=
\alpha_X X_i^a J_i^a[\Psi,P]
+
\beta_X X_i^a K_i^a[P,\Psi].
}
\]

\section{Hermiticity conditions}

To ensure a well-defined Hermitian fluctuation operator, we assume
\[
Z^0(P)=Z^0(P)^\dagger,
\qquad
Z^i(P)=Z^i(P)^\dagger,
\qquad
M_0(P)=M_0(P)^\dagger,
\]
and likewise
\[
A_i^a(P)=A_i^a(P)^\dagger,
\qquad
B_{ij}^a(P)=B_{ij}^a(P)^\dagger,
\]
\[
C_i^a(P)=C_i^a(P)^\dagger,
\qquad
D_{ij}^a(P)=D_{ij}^a(P)^\dagger.
\]

Under these conditions, the total quadratic \(\Psi\)-sector is Hermitian.

\section{Unified first-order coefficient fields}

It is convenient to define the combined Class II coefficient fields
\[
\boxed{
U_i^a(P):=\alpha_X A_i^a(P)+\beta_X C_i^a(P),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
V_{ij}^a(P):=\alpha_X B_{ij}^a(P)+\beta_X D_{ij}^a(P).
}
\]

Then
\[
\mathcal L_{\Psi X}
=
X_i^a\Psi^\dagger U_i^a(P)\Psi
+
\frac{i}{2}X_i^a\Psi^\dagger V_{ij}^a(P)\!\stackrel{\leftrightarrow}{\partial_j}\!\Psi.
\]

So the working microscopic action becomes
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{\rm mic}
=
\mathcal L_P[P]
+
\frac{i}{2}\Psi^\dagger Z^0(P)\!\stackrel{\leftrightarrow}{\partial_t}\!\Psi
+
\frac{i}{2}\Psi^\dagger\Bigl(Z^i(P)+X_j^aV_{ji}^a(P)\Bigr)\!\stackrel{\leftrightarrow}{\partial_i}\!\Psi
-
\Psi^\dagger\Bigl(M_0(P)-X_i^aU_i^a(P)\Bigr)\Psi
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a.
}
\]

This is the explicit minimal microscopic coefficient template.

\section{Euler--Lagrange equation for the \(\Psi\) sector}

Varying with respect to \(\Psi^\dagger\) gives the first-order field equation
\[
i\,K^0(P,X)\,\partial_t\Psi
+
i\,K^i(P,X)\,\partial_i\Psi
+
M(P,X,\partial P,\partial X)\Psi
=
0,
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
K^0(P,X)=Z^0(P),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
K^i(P,X)=Z^i(P)+X_j^aV_{ji}^a(P),
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
M(P,X,\partial P,\partial X)
=
\frac{i}{2}\partial_i K^i(P,X)
-
\Bigl(M_0(P)-X_i^aU_i^a(P)\Bigr).
}
\]

This is the exact coefficient identification for the working ansatz.

\section{Defect-background specialization}

Let
\[
(\bar P(x),\bar X_i^a(x))
\]
be a static single-defect background of the working branch.
Then the linearized reference fluctuation equation for the \(\Psi\)-sector is
\[
\boxed{
i\,K^0_{\rm def}(x)\,\partial_t\psi
+
i\,K^i_{\rm def}(x)\,\partial_i\psi
+
M_{\rm def}(x)\psi
=
0,
}
\]
where
\[
\boxed{
K^0_{\rm def}(x)=Z^0(\bar P(x)),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
K^i_{\rm def}(x)=Z^i(\bar P(x))+\bar X_j^a(x)\,V_{ji}^a(\bar P(x)),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
M_{\rm def}(x)
=
\frac{i}{2}\partial_i K^i_{\rm def}(x)
-
\Bigl(
M_0(\bar P(x))
-
\bar X_i^a(x)U_i^a(\bar P(x))
\Bigr).
}
\]

These are the actual microscopic coefficient fields entering the defect spectral problem.

\section{Two important special cases}

\paragraph{Case 1: reference branch with \(\bar X=0\).}
If the locked reference background carries no mediator expectation value, then
\[
\boxed{
K^0_{\rm def}=Z^0(\bar P),
\qquad
K^i_{\rm def}=Z^i(\bar P),
\qquad
M_{\rm def}
=
\frac{i}{2}\partial_i Z^i(\bar P)-M_0(\bar P).
}
\]
In this case the Class II mediator enters only through the quadratic Schur-complement correction and not through the reference operator itself.

\paragraph{Case 2: algebraically induced \(\bar X\neq 0\).}
If the background stationarity equation produces a nonzero mediator profile
\[
M_X^2\bar X_i^a+\alpha_X J_i^a[\bar\Psi,\bar P]+\beta_X K_i^a[\bar P,\bar\Psi]=0,
\]
then \(\bar X\) shifts the reference transport and mass coefficients through the explicit formulas above.
So the Class II branch contributes both:
\begin{enumerate}
\item to the reference first-order coefficients through \(\bar X\);
\item to the quadratic effective operator through heavy-field elimination.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Canonical normalized defect operator}

Assume
\[
K^0_{\rm def}(x)=K^0_{\rm def}(x)^\dagger>0.
\]
Define
\[
S(x):=\bigl(K^0_{\rm def}(x)\bigr)^{1/2},
\qquad
\chi=S\psi.
\]
Then the defect fluctuation equation becomes
\[
i\partial_t\chi
=
\mathbb H_{\rm def}\chi,
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
\mathbb H_{\rm def}
=
-i\,\Gamma^i_{\rm def}(x)\partial_i
+
W_{\rm def}(x),
}
\]
where
\[
\boxed{
\Gamma^i_{\rm def}
=
S^{-1}K^i_{\rm def}S^{-1},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
W_{\rm def}
=
-i\,S^{-1}K^i_{\rm def}\,\partial_i(S^{-1})
-
S^{-1}M_{\rm def}S^{-1}.
}
\]

Equivalently, after choosing a bundle frame and covariant derivative convention,
\[
\boxed{
\mathbb O_{\rm 1def}^{(0)}
=
i\widetilde\Gamma^i_{\rm def}(\partial_i+\Omega_i^{\rm def})
+
\Phi_{\rm def}.
}
\]

Thus the reference operator is now extracted from an explicit minimal microscopic ansatz rather than from a purely abstract placeholder.

\section{Connection to the Bloch/Class II extraction program}

The same local-current ansatz also determines the Bloch-space mixed vertices used previously.

Indeed, after harmonic expansion on the locked BCC branch,
\[
\mathcal J_i^a(k)
\sim
A_i^a(Q)+B_{ij}^a(Q)(k_j+G'_j),
\qquad
\mathcal K_i^a(k)
\sim
C_i^a(Q)+D_{ij}^a(Q)(k_j+G'_j),
\]
so
\[
H_{\Psi X}(k)=\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k)
\]
is precisely the Bloch-space realization of the same microscopic coefficients \(A,B,C,D\).

Therefore the single-defect reference operator program and the refined locked + Class II Bloch extraction program are no longer separate constructions:
they are two specializations of the same minimal microscopic coefficient template.

\section{What is now rigorously fixed}

At the level of the working microscopic ansatz, the following are now explicit:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the minimal microscopic multiplet
\[
(P^A,\Psi,X_i^a);
\]

\item the local-current realization of \(J_i^a\) and \(K_i^a\);

\item the exact coefficient fields
\[
K^0(P,X),\qquad K^i(P,X),\qquad M(P,X,\partial P,\partial X);
\]

\item the defect-background coefficients
\[
K^0_{\rm def},\qquad K^i_{\rm def},\qquad M_{\rm def};
\]

\item the canonically normalized reference operator
\[
\mathbb O_{\rm 1def}^{(0)}
=
i\widetilde\Gamma^i_{\rm def}(\partial_i+\Omega_i^{\rm def})+\Phi_{\rm def}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

\section{What still remains open}

What remains TECT-specific and still open is not the coefficient-extraction skeleton, but the actual concrete choice of
\[
Z^0(P),\quad Z^i(P),\quad M_0(P),\quad A_i^a(P),\quad B_{ij}^a(P),\quad C_i^a(P),\quad D_{ij}^a(P),
\]
together with:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the explicit locked BCC defect background \(\bar P,\bar X\);
\item the proof of asymptotic bulk invertibility;
\item the grading and index analysis;
\item the explicit overlap integrals for the reduced family coefficients.
\end{enumerate}

So the operator-theoretic and coefficient-extraction framework is now fixed.
What remains is to insert the actual TECT constitutive data into it.

\section{Final summary}

We fixed a minimal working microscopic multiplet for the TECT flavor program:
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak B=(P^A,\Psi,X_i^a).
}
\]

The corresponding minimal first-order Hermitian microscopic action is
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal L_{\rm mic}
=
\mathcal L_P[P]
+
\frac{i}{2}\Psi^\dagger Z^0(P)\!\stackrel{\leftrightarrow}{\partial_t}\!\Psi
+
\frac{i}{2}\Psi^\dagger\Bigl(Z^i(P)+X_j^aV_{ji}^a(P)\Bigr)\!\stackrel{\leftrightarrow}{\partial_i}\!\Psi
-
\Psi^\dagger\Bigl(M_0(P)-X_i^aU_i^a(P)\Bigr)\Psi
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a,
}
\]
where
\[
U_i^a=\alpha_X A_i^a+\beta_X C_i^a,
\qquad
V_{ij}^a=\alpha_X B_{ij}^a+\beta_X D_{ij}^a,
\]
and
\[
J_i^a=\Psi^\dagger A_i^a\Psi+\frac{i}{2}\Psi^\dagger B_{ij}^a\!\stackrel{\leftrightarrow}{\partial_j}\!\Psi,
\qquad
K_i^a=\Psi^\dagger C_i^a\Psi+\frac{i}{2}\Psi^\dagger D_{ij}^a\!\stackrel{\leftrightarrow}{\partial_j}\!\Psi.
\]

From this action, the exact first-order coefficient fields are
\[
K^0(P,X)=Z^0(P),
\qquad
K^i(P,X)=Z^i(P)+X_j^aV_{ji}^a(P),
\]
\[
M(P,X,\partial P,\partial X)
=
\frac{i}{2}\partial_i K^i(P,X)
-
\Bigl(M_0(P)-X_i^aU_i^a(P)\Bigr).
\]

Therefore, on a static defect background \((\bar P,\bar X)\), the defect fluctuation equation is
\[
iK^0_{\rm def}\partial_t\psi+iK^i_{\rm def}\partial_i\psi+M_{\rm def}\psi=0,
\]
with
\[
K^0_{\rm def}=Z^0(\bar P),
\qquad
K^i_{\rm def}=Z^i(\bar P)+\bar X_j^aV_{ji}^a(\bar P),
\]
\[
M_{\rm def}
=
\frac{i}{2}\partial_iK^i_{\rm def}
-
\Bigl(M_0(\bar P)-\bar X_i^aU_i^a(\bar P)\Bigr).
\]

After canonical normalization this yields the reference operator
\[
\boxed{
\mathbb O_{\rm 1def}^{(0)}
=
i\widetilde\Gamma^i_{\rm def}(\partial_i+\Omega_i^{\rm def})
+
\Phi_{\rm def}.
}
\]

So the microscopic coefficient-extraction skeleton is now explicit.
The remaining open input is purely TECT-specific:
the actual constitutive matrices \(Z^0,Z^i,M_0,A,B,C,D\), the explicit defect background, and the corresponding gap/index analysis.

\section{Minimal constitutive choice compatible with the locked BCC background}

We now fix a minimal working constitutive ansatz compatible with the locked BCC branch and with the previously derived operator-extraction formalism.

\section{Locked geometric data extracted from the condensate field}

Let the condensate field \(P^A(x)\) determine the following local geometric data:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a scalar amplitude
\[
\sigma(x):=\sigma(P(x));
\]

\item a unit defect-axis field
\[
\hat n_i(x):=\hat n_i(P(x)),
\qquad
\hat n_i\hat n_i=1;
\]

\item a local locked frame
\[
E_i{}^a(x):=E_i{}^a(P(x))\in SO(3),
\qquad
E_i{}^a E_i{}^b=\delta^{ab},
\qquad
E_i{}^a E_j{}^a=\delta_{ij}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

The field \(E_i{}^a\) expresses the locking between spatial and internal directions, while \(\hat n_i\) selects the distinguished defect axis.

The corresponding transverse projector is
\[
\Pi^\perp_{ij}:=\delta_{ij}-\hat n_i\hat n_j.
\]

\section{Internal Clifford data}

Let the fluctuation field \(\Psi\) take values in an internal bundle carrying Hermitian matrices
\[
\Gamma^i,\qquad i=1,2,3,
\]
satisfying the Euclidean Clifford relations
\[
\{\Gamma^i,\Gamma^j\}=2\delta^{ij}\mathbf 1.
\]

Assume also the existence of a Hermitian matrix
\[
\Gamma^\sharp=(\Gamma^\sharp)^\dagger,
\qquad
(\Gamma^\sharp)^2=\mathbf 1,
\qquad
\{\Gamma^\sharp,\Gamma^i\}=0,
\]
which will play the role of the mass/Higgs endomorphism.

Define the defect-axis gamma
\[
\Gamma_{\hat n}:=\hat n_i\Gamma^i.
\]

\section{Minimal reference constitutive choice}

We take the reference \(\Psi\)-sector coefficients to depend only on the scalar amplitude \(\sigma\):
\[
\boxed{
Z^0(P)=z_0(\sigma)\,\mathbf 1,
\qquad
z_0(\sigma)>0,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
Z^i(P)
=
v_\perp(\sigma)\Gamma^i
+
v_c(\sigma)\,\hat n^i\,\Gamma_{\hat n},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
M_0(P)=m(\sigma)\,\Gamma^\sharp.
}
\]

This is the minimal isotropic-plus-axis-anisotropic Dirac form.
The coefficient \(v_\perp\) controls the transverse transport, while \(v_c\) is the longitudinal defect-axis correction.

\section{Minimal Class II current constitutive choice}

We now choose the Class II local-current coefficients in the simplest locked form.

\paragraph{Mass-type current coupling.}
\[
\boxed{
A_i^a(P)=u(\sigma)\,E_i{}^a\,\Gamma^\sharp,
\qquad
C_i^a(P)=\tilde u(\sigma)\,E_i{}^a\,\Gamma^\sharp.
}
\]

\paragraph{Transport-type current coupling.}
We take
\[
\boxed{
B_{ij}^a(P)
=
E_i{}^a
\Bigl[
b_E(\sigma)\,\delta_{j\ell}
+
b_O(\sigma)\,\epsilon_{j\ell m}\hat n_m
+
b_c(\sigma)\,\hat n_j\hat n_\ell
\Bigr]\Gamma^\ell,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
D_{ij}^a(P)
=
E_i{}^a
\Bigl[
d_E(\sigma)\,\delta_{j\ell}
+
d_O(\sigma)\,\epsilon_{j\ell m}\hat n_m
+
d_c(\sigma)\,\hat n_j\hat n_\ell
\Bigr]\Gamma^\ell.
}
\]

All coefficient functions
\[
z_0,\ v_\perp,\ v_c,\ m,\ u,\ \tilde u,\ b_E,b_O,b_c,\ d_E,d_O,d_c
\]
are real scalar functions of \(\sigma\).

This is the minimal constitutive ansatz that is simultaneously:

\begin{enumerate}
\item local;
\item Hermitian;
\item compatible with spatial/internal locking;
\item rich enough to generate the three transport channels later identified as \((g_E,g_O,g_c)\).
\end{enumerate}

\section{Unified Class II transport and mass coefficients}

Recall
\[
U_i^a=\alpha_X A_i^a+\beta_X C_i^a,
\qquad
V_{ij}^a=\alpha_X B_{ij}^a+\beta_X D_{ij}^a.
\]

Define the combined scalar functions
\[
\boxed{
u_X(\sigma):=\alpha_X u(\sigma)+\beta_X\tilde u(\sigma),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
v_E^{(X)}(\sigma):=\alpha_X b_E(\sigma)+\beta_X d_E(\sigma),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
v_O^{(X)}(\sigma):=\alpha_X b_O(\sigma)+\beta_X d_O(\sigma),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
v_c^{(X)}(\sigma):=\alpha_X b_c(\sigma)+\beta_X d_c(\sigma).
}
\]

Then
\[
\boxed{
U_i^a(P)=u_X(\sigma)\,E_i{}^a\,\Gamma^\sharp,
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
V_{ij}^a(P)
=
E_i{}^a
\Bigl[
v_E^{(X)}(\sigma)\,\delta_{j\ell}
+
v_O^{(X)}(\sigma)\,\epsilon_{j\ell m}\hat n_m
+
v_c^{(X)}(\sigma)\,\hat n_j\hat n_\ell
\Bigr]\Gamma^\ell.
}
\]

\section{Locked Class II background contraction}

Define the locked mediator scalar projection
\[
\boxed{
\chi_X(x):=\frac13\,\bar X_i^a(x)\,E_i{}^a(x),
}
\]
on the static defect background \((\bar P,\bar X)\).

If the background is strictly locked,
\[
\bar X_i^a(x)=X_*(x)\,E_i{}^a(x),
\]
then
\[
\chi_X(x)=X_*(x).
\]

Under this locked contraction,
\[
\bar X_j^a V_{ji}^a
=
3\chi_X
\Bigl[
v_E^{(X)}\delta_{i\ell}
+
v_O^{(X)}\epsilon_{i\ell m}\hat n_m
+
v_c^{(X)}\hat n_i\hat n_\ell
\Bigr]\Gamma^\ell,
\]
and
\[
\bar X_i^a U_i^a
=
3\chi_X\,u_X\,\Gamma^\sharp.
\]

\section{Explicit defect-background coefficients}

Therefore the defect-background first-order coefficients are

\[
\boxed{
K^0_{\rm def}(x)=z_0(\bar\sigma(x))\,\mathbf 1,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
K^i_{\rm def}(x)
=
v_\perp(\bar\sigma)\Gamma^i
+
v_c(\bar\sigma)\hat n^i\Gamma_{\hat n}
+
3\chi_X
\Bigl[
v_E^{(X)}(\bar\sigma)\delta_{i\ell}
+
v_O^{(X)}(\bar\sigma)\epsilon_{i\ell m}\hat n_m
+
v_c^{(X)}(\bar\sigma)\hat n_i\hat n_\ell
\Bigr]\Gamma^\ell,
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
M_{\rm def}(x)
=
\frac{i}{2}\partial_iK^i_{\rm def}(x)
-
m_{\rm eff}(x)\Gamma^\sharp,
}
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
m_{\rm eff}(x):=
m(\bar\sigma(x))-3\chi_X(x)\,u_X(\bar\sigma(x)).
}
\]

Thus the mediator modifies:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the transverse even transport channel through \(v_E^{(X)}\);
\item the transverse odd channel through \(v_O^{(X)}\);
\item the longitudinal/c-axis channel through \(v_c^{(X)}\);
\item the local mass gap through \(u_X\).
\end{enumerate}

\section{Effective transport coefficients and their microscopic meaning}

It is convenient to group the effective transport coefficients as
\[
\boxed{
g_E^{\rm eff}(x)
:=
v_\perp(\bar\sigma(x))+3\chi_X(x)\,v_E^{(X)}(\bar\sigma(x)),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
g_O^{\rm eff}(x)
:=
3\chi_X(x)\,v_O^{(X)}(\bar\sigma(x)),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
g_c^{\rm eff}(x)
:=
v_c(\bar\sigma(x))+3\chi_X(x)\,v_c^{(X)}(\bar\sigma(x)).
}
\]

Then
\[
\boxed{
K^i_{\rm def}(x)
=
g_E^{\rm eff}(x)\Gamma^i
+
g_O^{\rm eff}(x)\,\epsilon_{i\ell m}\hat n_m\Gamma^\ell
+
g_c^{\rm eff}(x)\,\hat n_i\Gamma_{\hat n}.
}
\]

This is the exact minimal constitutive origin of the three reduced transport channels.

\section{Canonical normalized defect operator}

Since
\[
K^0_{\rm def}(x)=z_0(\bar\sigma(x))\mathbf 1>0,
\]
define
\[
S(x)=\sqrt{z_0(\bar\sigma(x))}\,\mathbf 1,
\qquad
\chi=S\psi.
\]
Then
\[
i\partial_t\chi=\mathbb H_{\rm def}\chi,
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
\mathbb H_{\rm def}
=
-i\,\Gamma^i_{\rm can}(x)\partial_i
+
W_{\rm def}(x),
}
\]
where
\[
\boxed{
\Gamma^i_{\rm can}(x)
=
\frac{1}{z_0(\bar\sigma(x))}
\Bigl[
g_E^{\rm eff}(x)\Gamma^i
+
g_O^{\rm eff}(x)\epsilon_{i\ell m}\hat n_m\Gamma^\ell
+
g_c^{\rm eff}(x)\hat n_i\Gamma_{\hat n}
\Bigr],
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
W_{\rm def}(x)
=
-\frac{i}{z_0(\bar\sigma)}K^i_{\rm def}\,\partial_i\!\bigl(z_0(\bar\sigma)^{-1/2}\bigr)
-
\frac{1}{z_0(\bar\sigma)}
\Bigl(
\frac{i}{2}\partial_iK^i_{\rm def}-m_{\rm eff}\Gamma^\sharp
\Bigr).
}
\]

Equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
\mathbb O_{\rm 1def}^{(0)}
=
i\widetilde\Gamma^i_{\rm def}(\partial_i+\Omega_i^{\rm def})
+
\Phi_{\rm def},
}
\]
with
\[
\widetilde\Gamma^i_{\rm def}=-\Gamma^i_{\rm can},
\]
and \(\Omega_i^{\rm def},\Phi_{\rm def}\) defined by the decomposition of \(W_{\rm def}\) into connection-type and endomorphism-type pieces.

\section{Interpretation}

This minimal constitutive choice has three important consequences.

\paragraph{(1) The three reduced transport channels are now explicit.}
The coefficients later read as \((g_E,g_O,g_c)\) are no longer abstract placeholders.
They arise directly from the constitutive functions
\[
v_\perp,\ v_c,\ v_E^{(X)},\ v_O^{(X)},\ v_c^{(X)}
\]
and the locked mediator scalar \(\chi_X\).

\paragraph{(2) The same coefficients control both the single-defect reference operator and the Bloch/Class II extraction branch.}
The Fourier-space vertex coefficients \(\mathbb A,\mathbb B,\mathbb C,\mathbb D\) introduced previously are exactly the harmonic expansions of
\[
A_i^a,\ B_{ij}^a,\ C_i^a,\ D_{ij}^a
\]
from the present constitutive ansatz.

\paragraph{(3) The remaining ambiguity is now only constitutive, not structural.}
The operator skeleton is fixed.
What remains is to determine the actual TECT constitutive functions
\[
z_0,\ v_\perp,\ v_c,\ m,\ u,\ \tilde u,\ b_E,b_O,b_c,\ d_E,d_O,d_c.
\]

\section{What is now closed and what remains open}

The following are now fixed within the working microscopic program:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the minimal microscopic multiplet \((P^A,\Psi,X_i^a)\);
\item a locked BCC-compatible local constitutive ansatz;
\item the explicit formulas for
\[
K^0_{\rm def},\quad K^i_{\rm def},\quad M_{\rm def};
\]
\item the explicit constitutive origin of the reduced transport channels
\[
(g_E^{\rm eff},g_O^{\rm eff},g_c^{\rm eff});
\]
\item the corresponding canonical single-defect reference operator.
\end{enumerate}

What remains open is TECT-specific:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the actual constitutive functions of the theory;
\item the explicit defect solution \((\bar P,\bar X)\);
\item the asymptotic bulk gap condition;
\item the grading/index computation for the single-defect light mode;
\item the later overlap and projector integrals for the three-defect reduction.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Final summary}

We fixed a minimal locked-BCC-compatible constitutive ansatz for the TECT working microscopic program.

The condensate field \(P\) determines:
\[
\sigma(P),\qquad
\hat n_i(P),\qquad
E_i{}^a(P)\in SO(3).
\]

The reference \(\Psi\)-sector is taken as
\[
Z^0(P)=z_0(\sigma)\mathbf 1,
\qquad
Z^i(P)=v_\perp(\sigma)\Gamma^i+v_c(\sigma)\hat n^i\Gamma_{\hat n},
\qquad
M_0(P)=m(\sigma)\Gamma^\sharp.
\]

The Class II couplings are chosen as
\[
A_i^a=u(\sigma)E_i{}^a\Gamma^\sharp,
\qquad
C_i^a=\tilde u(\sigma)E_i{}^a\Gamma^\sharp,
\]
\[
B_{ij}^a
=
E_i{}^a
\Bigl[
b_E(\sigma)\delta_{j\ell}
+b_O(\sigma)\epsilon_{j\ell m}\hat n_m
+b_c(\sigma)\hat n_j\hat n_\ell
\Bigr]\Gamma^\ell,
\]
\[
D_{ij}^a
=
E_i{}^a
\Bigl[
d_E(\sigma)\delta_{j\ell}
+d_O(\sigma)\epsilon_{j\ell m}\hat n_m
+d_c(\sigma)\hat n_j\hat n_\ell
\Bigr]\Gamma^\ell.
\]

On a locked defect background, defining
\[
\chi_X=\frac13\bar X_i^aE_i{}^a,
\]
the defect coefficients become
\[
K^0_{\rm def}=z_0(\bar\sigma)\mathbf 1,
\]
\[
K^i_{\rm def}
=
g_E^{\rm eff}\Gamma^i
+
g_O^{\rm eff}\epsilon_{i\ell m}\hat n_m\Gamma^\ell
+
g_c^{\rm eff}\hat n_i\Gamma_{\hat n},
\]
with
\[
g_E^{\rm eff}=v_\perp+3\chi_Xv_E^{(X)},
\qquad
g_O^{\rm eff}=3\chi_Xv_O^{(X)},
\qquad
g_c^{\rm eff}=v_c+3\chi_Xv_c^{(X)},
\]
and
\[
M_{\rm def}
=
\frac{i}{2}\partial_iK^i_{\rm def}
-
m_{\rm eff}\Gamma^\sharp,
\qquad
m_{\rm eff}=m-3\chi_Xu_X.
\]

After canonical normalization, this yields the explicit single-defect reference operator
\[
\mathbb O_{\rm 1def}^{(0)}
=
i\widetilde\Gamma^i_{\rm def}(\partial_i+\Omega_i^{\rm def})
+
\Phi_{\rm def}.
\]

Therefore the operator skeleton is no longer abstract:
the reduced transport channels \((g_E,g_O,g_c)\) now have an explicit microscopic constitutive origin.

The remaining open input is purely TECT-specific:
the actual constitutive functions, the explicit defect profile, the bulk gap, and the index analysis.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Radial single-defect ansatz and explicit defect-frame form of the reference operator}

We now specialize the minimal constitutive ansatz to a radial single-defect background and derive the explicit defect-frame form of the single-defect reference operator.

\section{Radial single-defect background ansatz}

We assume a static radial defect centered at the origin.
Let
\[
r:=|x|,
\qquad
\hat n_i(x):=\frac{x_i}{r}.
\]
We take the condensate amplitude to be radial:
\[
\bar\sigma(x)=\bar\sigma(r).
\]

For the locked frame, we choose a local orthonormal spatial/internal frame adapted to the defect:
\[
E_i{}^a(x)\in SO(3),
\qquad
E_i{}^a E_i{}^b=\delta^{ab},
\qquad
E_i{}^a E_j{}^a=\delta_{ij},
\]
with the distinguished radial direction aligned,
\[
E_i{}^{3}(x)=\hat n_i(x).
\]

Equivalently, one may think of \(E_i{}^a(x)\) as a local rotation sending the internal axis \(a=3\) to the spatial radial unit vector \(\hat n_i\).
The remaining two columns span the local tangent frame on \(S^2\).

\section{Locked mediator radial decomposition}

The most general rotationally covariant locked mediator profile has the form
\[
\boxed{
\bar X_i{}^a(x)
=
X_\perp(r)\bigl(\delta_i{}^a-\hat n_i\hat n^a\bigr)
+
X_\parallel(r)\hat n_i\hat n^a.
}
\]
Equivalently, in terms of the locked frame,
\[
\bar X_i{}^a(x)
=
X_\perp(r)\sum_{\alpha=1}^{2}E_i{}^\alpha E_r{}^\alpha
+
X_\parallel(r)E_i{}^3E_r{}^3,
\]
where \(E_r{}^3=1\) in the adapted frame.
The scalar locked contraction defined previously becomes
\[
\chi_X(r)
=
\frac13\,\bar X_i{}^a E_i{}^a
=
\frac13\bigl(2X_\perp(r)+X_\parallel(r)\bigr).
\]

\section{Radial specialization of the constitutive coefficients}

From the previous minimal constitutive choice, define
\[
g_E^{\rm eff}(r)
:=
v_\perp(\bar\sigma(r))
+
3\chi_X(r)\,v_E^{(X)}(\bar\sigma(r)),
\]
\[
g_O^{\rm eff}(r)
:=
3\chi_X(r)\,v_O^{(X)}(\bar\sigma(r)),
\]
\[
g_c^{\rm eff}(r)
:=
v_c(\bar\sigma(r))
+
3\chi_X(r)\,v_c^{(X)}(\bar\sigma(r)),
\]
and
\[
m_{\rm eff}(r)
:=
m(\bar\sigma(r))
-
3\chi_X(r)\,u_X(\bar\sigma(r)).
\]

Thus the first-order coefficients are radial functions only:
\[
K^0_{\rm def}(r)=z_0(\bar\sigma(r))\,\mathbf 1,
\]
\[
K^i_{\rm def}(r)
=
g_E(r)\Gamma^i
+
g_O(r)\,\epsilon_{i\ell m}\hat n_m\Gamma^\ell
+
g_c(r)\hat n_i\Gamma_{\hat n},
\]
where for brevity we write
\[
g_E(r):=g_E^{\rm eff}(r),
\qquad
g_O(r):=g_O^{\rm eff}(r),
\qquad
g_c(r):=g_c^{\rm eff}(r),
\qquad
\Gamma_{\hat n}:=\hat n_i\Gamma^i.
\]

\section{Radial/transverse decomposition of the transport tensor}

Introduce the transverse projector
\[
\Pi^\perp_{ij}:=\delta_{ij}-\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\]
and the transverse Clifford matrices
\[
\Gamma^\perp_i:=\Pi^\perp_{i\ell}\Gamma^\ell.
\]
Since
\[
\Gamma^i=\Gamma^\perp_i+\hat n_i\Gamma_{\hat n},
\]
we obtain
\[
\boxed{
K^i_{\rm def}(r)
=
g_E(r)\Gamma^\perp_i
+
\bigl(g_E(r)+g_c(r)\bigr)\hat n_i\Gamma_{\hat n}
+
g_O(r)\,\epsilon_{i\ell m}\hat n_m\Gamma^\ell.
}
\]

It is convenient to define the odd transverse operator
\[
\boxed{
J_i(\hat n):=\epsilon_{i\ell m}\hat n_m\Gamma^\ell.
}
\]
This satisfies
\[
\hat n_i J_i(\hat n)=0,
\]
so it is purely tangential.
Therefore the transport tensor is split into exactly three channels:

\[
\boxed{
K^i_{\rm def}(r)
=
g_E(r)\Gamma^\perp_i
+
g_R(r)\hat n_i\Gamma_{\hat n}
+
g_O(r)J_i(\hat n),
}
\qquad
g_R(r):=g_E(r)+g_c(r).
\]

This is the precise radial meaning of the three reduced transport coefficients.

\section{Explicit zeroth-order term \(M_{\rm def}(r)\)}

Recall
\[
M_{\rm def}
=
\frac{i}{2}\partial_i K^i_{\rm def}
-
m_{\rm eff}(r)\Gamma^\sharp.
\]
We now compute \(\partial_i K^i_{\rm def}\).

First,
\[
\partial_i \hat n_j=\frac{1}{r}\Pi^\perp_{ij},
\qquad
\partial_i\hat n_i=\frac{2}{r}.
\]
Next,
\[
\partial_i \Gamma_{\hat n}
=
(\partial_i\hat n_j)\Gamma^j
=
\frac{1}{r}\Pi^\perp_{ij}\Gamma^j.
\]

For the radial part,
\[
\partial_i\bigl(g_R(r)\hat n_i\Gamma_{\hat n}\bigr)
=
g_R'(r)\Gamma_{\hat n}
+
\frac{2g_R(r)}{r}\Gamma_{\hat n}
+
\frac{g_R(r)}{r}\Pi^\perp_{ij}\hat n_i\Gamma^j.
\]
Since \(\Pi^\perp_{ij}\hat n_i=0\), the last term vanishes, hence
\[
\boxed{
\partial_i\bigl(g_R(r)\hat n_i\Gamma_{\hat n}\bigr)
=
\left(g_R'(r)+\frac{2g_R(r)}{r}\right)\Gamma_{\hat n}.
}
\]

For the even tangential part,
\[
\partial_i\bigl(g_E(r)\Gamma^\perp_i\bigr)
=
g_E'(r)\hat n_i\Gamma^\perp_i
+
g_E(r)\partial_i\Gamma^\perp_i.
\]
Because \(\hat n_i\Gamma^\perp_i=0\), only the second term survives.
Now
\[
\Gamma^\perp_i=\Gamma^i-\hat n_i\Gamma_{\hat n},
\]
so
\[
\partial_i\Gamma^\perp_i
=
-\partial_i(\hat n_i\Gamma_{\hat n})
=
-\frac{2}{r}\Gamma_{\hat n}-\frac{1}{r}\Pi^\perp_{ij}\hat n_i\Gamma^j
=
-\frac{2}{r}\Gamma_{\hat n}.
\]
Therefore
\[
\boxed{
\partial_i\bigl(g_E(r)\Gamma^\perp_i\bigr)
=
-\frac{2g_E(r)}{r}\Gamma_{\hat n}.
}
\]

For the odd tangential part,
\[
\partial_i\bigl(g_O(r)J_i(\hat n)\bigr)
=
g_O'(r)\hat n_i J_i(\hat n)
+
g_O(r)\partial_i J_i(\hat n).
\]
The first term vanishes because \(\hat n_iJ_i(\hat n)=0\).
Moreover,
\[
J_i(\hat n)=\epsilon_{i\ell m}\hat n_m\Gamma^\ell,
\]
so
\[
\partial_iJ_i(\hat n)
=
\epsilon_{i\ell m}(\partial_i\hat n_m)\Gamma^\ell
=
\frac1r \epsilon_{i\ell m}\Pi^\perp_{im}\Gamma^\ell
=
0,
\]
since \(\Pi^\perp_{im}\) is symmetric in \(i,m\) while \(\epsilon_{i\ell m}\) is antisymmetric.
Hence
\[
\boxed{
\partial_i\bigl(g_O(r)J_i(\hat n)\bigr)=0.
}
\]

Combining everything, we obtain
\[
\boxed{
\partial_i K^i_{\rm def}(r)
=
\left(
g_R'(r)+\frac{2g_R(r)}{r}-\frac{2g_E(r)}{r}
\right)\Gamma_{\hat n}
=
\left(
g_R'(r)+\frac{2g_c(r)}{r}
\right)\Gamma_{\hat n}.
}
\]

Therefore the zeroth-order term is
\[
\boxed{
M_{\rm def}(r)
=
\frac{i}{2}\left(
g_R'(r)+\frac{2g_c(r)}{r}
\right)\Gamma_{\hat n}
-
m_{\rm eff}(r)\Gamma^\sharp.
}
\]

This is already a strong structural result:
the odd transport channel \(g_O(r)\) does not contribute directly to \(\partial_iK^i_{\rm def}\), but only to the first-order angular transport operator.

\section{Canonical normalization}

Since
\[
K^0_{\rm def}(r)=z_0(\bar\sigma(r))\mathbf 1>0,
\]
define
\[
S(r)=\sqrt{z_0(\bar\sigma(r))}\,\mathbf 1,
\qquad
\chi=S(r)\psi.
\]
Then
\[
i\partial_t\chi=\mathbb H_{\rm def}\chi,
\]
with
\[
\mathbb H_{\rm def}
=
-i\,\Gamma^i_{\rm can}(r,\hat n)\partial_i
+
W_{\rm def}(r,\hat n),
\]
where
\[
\boxed{
\Gamma^i_{\rm can}(r,\hat n)
=
\frac{1}{z_0(r)}
\Bigl[
g_E(r)\Gamma^\perp_i
+
g_R(r)\hat n_i\Gamma_{\hat n}
+
g_O(r)J_i(\hat n)
\Bigr].
}
\]

The zeroth-order piece is
\[
W_{\rm def}
=
-\frac{i}{z_0(r)}K^i_{\rm def}\partial_i\bigl(z_0(r)^{-1/2}\bigr)
-
\frac{1}{z_0(r)}M_{\rm def}(r).
\]
Since \(z_0\) is radial,
\[
\partial_i\bigl(z_0(r)^{-1/2}\bigr)
=
\bigl(z_0^{-1/2}\bigr)'(r)\hat n_i,
\]
hence only the radial transport part contributes:
\[
K^i_{\rm def}\partial_i(z_0^{-1/2})
=
g_R(r)\Gamma_{\hat n}\,(z_0^{-1/2})'(r).
\]
Therefore
\[
\boxed{
W_{\rm def}(r,\hat n)
=
-\frac{i\,g_R(r)}{z_0(r)}(z_0^{-1/2})'(r)\Gamma_{\hat n}
-
\frac{i}{2z_0(r)}
\left(
g_R'(r)+\frac{2g_c(r)}{r}
\right)\Gamma_{\hat n}
+
\frac{m_{\rm eff}(r)}{z_0(r)}\Gamma^\sharp.
}
\]

So the canonically normalized single-defect operator is explicitly
\[
\boxed{
\mathbb H_{\rm def}
=
-\frac{i}{z_0(r)}
\Bigl[
g_E(r)\Gamma^\perp_i
+
g_R(r)\hat n_i\Gamma_{\hat n}
+
g_O(r)J_i(\hat n)
\Bigr]\partial_i
+
W_{\rm def}(r,\hat n).
}
\]

\section{Radial/angular decomposition}

Using
\[
\partial_i=\hat n_i\partial_r+\frac{1}{r}\nabla_i^{S^2},
\]
one gets
\[
\Gamma^\perp_i\partial_i
=
\frac{1}{r}\Gamma^\perp_i\nabla_i^{S^2},
\qquad
\hat n_i\Gamma_{\hat n}\partial_i
=
\Gamma_{\hat n}\partial_r,
\]
\[
J_i(\hat n)\partial_i
=
\frac{1}{r}J_i(\hat n)\nabla_i^{S^2}.
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
\mathbb H_{\rm def}
=
-\frac{i\,g_R(r)}{z_0(r)}\Gamma_{\hat n}\partial_r
-\frac{i\,g_E(r)}{z_0(r)r}\Gamma^\perp_i\nabla_i^{S^2}
-\frac{i\,g_O(r)}{z_0(r)r}J_i(\hat n)\nabla_i^{S^2}
+
W_{\rm def}(r,\hat n).
}
\]

This is the final radial single-defect reference form.
It cleanly separates:

\begin{enumerate}
\item radial transport through \(g_R(r)\);
\item even tangential Dirac transport through \(g_E(r)\);
\item odd tangential/torsion-like transport through \(g_O(r)\);
\item mass/gap structure through \(m_{\rm eff}(r)\).
\end{enumerate}

\section{Interpretation and what is now closed}

The explicit radial form shows the precise microscopic meaning of the three transport channels:

\[
\boxed{
g_E(r)\ \text{controls even tangential transport,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
g_O(r)\ \text{controls odd tangential transport,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
g_c(r)\ \text{enters only through }g_R(r)=g_E(r)+g_c(r)\text{ and through the radial divergence term.}
}
\]

Moreover, the mass profile is
\[
\boxed{
m_{\rm eff}(r)=m(\bar\sigma(r))-3\chi_X(r)u_X(\bar\sigma(r)).
}
\]
So the asymptotic bulk gap is controlled by
\[
m_{\rm eff}(\infty),
\]
while the localized defect distortion enters through the radial profiles
\[
\bar\sigma(r),\quad \chi_X(r).
\]

What is now rigorously fixed is the operator form.
What remains open is the TECT-specific input:
the actual radial profiles, the asymptotic behavior, and the grading/index computation.


\section{Final summary}

Using the radial single-defect ansatz
\[
\hat n_i=\frac{x_i}{r},
\qquad
\bar\sigma=\bar\sigma(r),
\qquad
\bar X_i{}^a
=
X_\perp(r)(\delta_i{}^a-\hat n_i\hat n^a)
+
X_\parallel(r)\hat n_i\hat n^a,
\]
we obtained the explicit defect-background coefficients
\[
K^0_{\rm def}(r)=z_0(\bar\sigma(r))\mathbf 1,
\]
\[
K^i_{\rm def}(r)
=
g_E(r)\Gamma^\perp_i
+
g_R(r)\hat n_i\Gamma_{\hat n}
+
g_O(r)J_i(\hat n),
\qquad
g_R(r)=g_E(r)+g_c(r),
\]
and
\[
M_{\rm def}(r)
=
\frac{i}{2}\left(g_R'(r)+\frac{2g_c(r)}{r}\right)\Gamma_{\hat n}
-
m_{\rm eff}(r)\Gamma^\sharp,
\]
with
\[
m_{\rm eff}(r)=m(\bar\sigma(r))-3\chi_X(r)u_X(\bar\sigma(r)).
\]

After canonical normalization, the single-defect reference operator becomes
\[
\boxed{
\mathbb H_{\rm def}
=
-\frac{i\,g_R(r)}{z_0(r)}\Gamma_{\hat n}\partial_r
-\frac{i\,g_E(r)}{z_0(r)r}\Gamma^\perp_i\nabla_i^{S^2}
-\frac{i\,g_O(r)}{z_0(r)r}J_i(\hat n)\nabla_i^{S^2}
+
W_{\rm def}(r,\hat n),
}
\]
where
\[
W_{\rm def}(r,\hat n)
=
-\frac{i\,g_R(r)}{z_0(r)}(z_0^{-1/2})'(r)\Gamma_{\hat n}
-
\frac{i}{2z_0(r)}
\left(
g_R'(r)+\frac{2g_c(r)}{r}
\right)\Gamma_{\hat n}
+
\frac{m_{\rm eff}(r)}{z_0(r)}\Gamma^\sharp.
\]

Thus the single-defect operator is now in an explicit radial form.
The three transport channels have clear microscopic meanings:
\(g_E\) is even tangential transport,
\(g_O\) is odd tangential transport,
and \(g_c\) modifies the radial channel and radial divergence term.

What remains open is no longer the operator form, but the TECT-specific constitutive profiles
\[
\bar\sigma(r),\quad X_\parallel(r),\quad X_\perp(r),
\]
their asymptotic gap behavior, and the eventual grading/index computation.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Partial-wave decomposition of the radial single-defect operator}

We now reduce the explicit radial single-defect reference operator to a one-dimensional first-order radial system.

\section{Radial form of the canonically normalized operator}

From the previous step, the canonically normalized single-defect operator has the form
\[
\mathbb H_{\rm def}
=
-\frac{i\,g_R(r)}{z_0(r)}\Gamma_{\hat n}\partial_r
-\frac{i\,g_E(r)}{z_0(r)r}\Gamma^\perp_i\nabla_i^{S^2}
-\frac{i\,g_O(r)}{z_0(r)r}J_i(\hat n)\nabla_i^{S^2}
+
W_{\rm def}(r,\hat n),
\]
with
\[
J_i(\hat n):=\epsilon_{i\ell m}\hat n_m\Gamma^\ell,
\qquad
\Gamma_{\hat n}:=\hat n_i\Gamma^i.
\]

It is convenient to define the radial coefficients
\[
\boxed{
a(r):=\frac{g_R(r)}{z_0(r)},
\qquad
b(r):=\frac{g_E(r)}{z_0(r)},
\qquad
c(r):=\frac{g_O(r)}{z_0(r)},
\qquad
\mu(r):=\frac{m_{\rm eff}(r)}{z_0(r)}.
}
\]

Also define the radial connection-like coefficient
\[
\boxed{
\omega_r(r)
:=
\frac{1}{2z_0(r)}
\left(
g_R'(r)+\frac{2g_c(r)}{r}-g_R(r)\frac{z_0'(r)}{z_0(r)}
\right).
}
\]
Then the zeroth-order term can be written as
\[
W_{\rm def}(r,\hat n)
=
-i\,\omega_r(r)\Gamma_{\hat n}
+
\mu(r)\Gamma^\sharp.
\]

Hence the operator becomes
\[
\boxed{
\mathbb H_{\rm def}
=
-i\,a(r)\Gamma_{\hat n}\partial_r
-\frac{i\,b(r)}{r}\Gamma^\perp_i\nabla_i^{S^2}
-\frac{i\,c(r)}{r}J_i(\hat n)\nabla_i^{S^2}
-i\,\omega_r(r)\Gamma_{\hat n}
+\mu(r)\Gamma^\sharp.
}
\]

\section{Angular Dirac operator on the sphere}

Define the spherical Dirac operator
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal D_{S^2}
:=
-i\,\Gamma_{\hat n}\Gamma^\perp_i\nabla_i^{S^2}.
}
\]

Then one has the identities
\[
\Gamma^\perp_i\nabla_i^{S^2}
=
i\,\Gamma_{\hat n}\mathcal D_{S^2},
\]
and, using
\[
J_i(\hat n)=i\,\Gamma_{\hat n}\Gamma^\perp_i,
\]
also
\[
J_i(\hat n)\nabla_i^{S^2}
=
-\mathcal D_{S^2}.
\]

Therefore the radial operator takes the compact form
\[
\boxed{
\mathbb H_{\rm def}
=
-i\,a(r)\Gamma_{\hat n}\partial_r
+\frac{b(r)}{r}\Gamma_{\hat n}\mathcal D_{S^2}
+\frac{i\,c(r)}{r}\mathcal D_{S^2}
-i\,\omega_r(r)\Gamma_{\hat n}
+\mu(r)\Gamma^\sharp.
}
\]

\section{Angular eigenbasis}

We now assume the standard spin-covariant spectral decomposition on \(S^2\).
Let
\[
Y_{\kappa m \varsigma}(\Omega)
\]
be a simultaneous eigenbasis satisfying
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal D_{S^2}Y_{\kappa m\varsigma}
=
\kappa\,Y_{\kappa m\varsigma},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\Gamma^\sharp Y_{\kappa m\varsigma}
=
\varsigma\,Y_{\kappa m\varsigma},
\qquad
\varsigma=\pm 1.
}
\]

Because \(\Gamma^\sharp\) anticommutes with each \(\Gamma^i\), it commutes with \(\mathcal D_{S^2}\), so the simultaneous diagonalization is consistent.
Also, since
\[
\{\Gamma_{\hat n},\mathcal D_{S^2}\}=0,
\qquad
\{\Gamma_{\hat n},\Gamma^\sharp\}=0,
\]
one has
\[
\mathcal D_{S^2}(\Gamma_{\hat n}Y_{\kappa m\varsigma})
=
-\kappa\,\Gamma_{\hat n}Y_{\kappa m\varsigma},
\]
\[
\Gamma^\sharp(\Gamma_{\hat n}Y_{\kappa m\varsigma})
=
-\varsigma\,\Gamma_{\hat n}Y_{\kappa m\varsigma}.
\]

Thus each angular sector closes on the two-dimensional span
\[
\operatorname{span}\{Y_{\kappa m\varsigma},\ \Gamma_{\hat n}Y_{\kappa m\varsigma}\}.
\]

\section{Partial-wave ansatz}

We therefore expand a stationary mode of energy \(\omega\) as
\[
\boxed{
\chi(r,\Omega)
=
\sum_{\kappa,m,\varsigma}
\Bigl[
f_{\kappa m\varsigma}(r)\,Y_{\kappa m\varsigma}(\Omega)
+
g_{\kappa m\varsigma}(r)\,\Gamma_{\hat n}Y_{\kappa m\varsigma}(\Omega)
\Bigr].
}
\]

Because the background is radial, the different \((\kappa,m,\varsigma)\) channels decouple.
So it is enough to study one fixed channel and suppress the indices:
\[
\chi(r,\Omega)=f(r)Y(\Omega)+g(r)\Gamma_{\hat n}Y(\Omega),
\]
with
\[
\mathcal D_{S^2}Y=\kappa Y,
\qquad
\Gamma^\sharp Y=\varsigma Y.
\]

\section{Radial first-order system}

Applying \(\mathbb H_{\rm def}\chi=\omega\chi\) and projecting onto the basis
\[
\{Y,\Gamma_{\hat n}Y\},
\]
one obtains the exact radial system
\[
\boxed{
\omega f
=
-i\,a(r)\,g'(r)
-i\,\omega_r(r)\,g(r)
-\frac{b(r)\kappa}{r}\,g(r)
+i\,\frac{c(r)\kappa}{r}\,f(r)
+\varsigma\,\mu(r)\,f(r),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\omega g
=
-i\,a(r)\,f'(r)
-i\,\omega_r(r)\,f(r)
+\frac{b(r)\kappa}{r}\,f(r)
-i\,\frac{c(r)\kappa}{r}\,g(r)
-\varsigma\,\mu(r)\,g(r).
}
\]

This is the desired one-dimensional first-order system.
All single-defect bound-state and zero-mode questions are now reduced to this radial ODE problem.

\section{Equivalent real form for the zero-mode sector}

For \(\omega=0\), define
\[
g(r)=i\,v(r),
\qquad
f(r)=u(r).
\]
Then the system becomes
\[
\boxed{
a(r)\,v'(r)+\omega_r(r)\,v(r)-\frac{b(r)\kappa}{r}\,i\,v(r)+\frac{c(r)\kappa}{r}\,i\,u(r)+\varsigma\,\mu(r)\,u(r)=0,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
