a(r)\,u'(r)+\omega_r(r)\,u(r)+\frac{b(r)\kappa}{r}\,u(r)+\frac{c(r)\kappa}{r}\,v(r)+\varsigma\,\mu(r)\,v(r)=0,
}
\]
or, keeping the original complex form, one may simply work with the previous pair.
The key point is that the zero-mode problem is a closed radial system with no remaining angular variables.

\section{Gauge-removal of the radial connection term}

The term \(\omega_r(r)\) has the same matrix structure as the radial derivative term.
Indeed,
\[
-i\,a(r)\Gamma_{\hat n}\partial_r - i\,\omega_r(r)\Gamma_{\hat n}
=
-i\,a(r)\Gamma_{\hat n}
\left(
\partial_r+\frac{\omega_r(r)}{a(r)}
\right).
\]

Therefore, introducing the scalar integrating factor
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I(r)
:=
\exp\left(\int^r \frac{\omega_r(s)}{a(s)}\,ds\right),
}
\]
and redefining
\[
f(r)=\mathcal I(r)^{-1}\tilde f(r),
\qquad
g(r)=\mathcal I(r)^{-1}\tilde g(r),
\]
one removes the \(\omega_r\)-term completely.
The reduced radial system becomes
\[
\boxed{
\omega \tilde f
=
-i\,a(r)\,\tilde g'
-\frac{b(r)\kappa}{r}\,\tilde g
+i\,\frac{c(r)\kappa}{r}\,\tilde f
+\varsigma\,\mu(r)\,\tilde f,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\omega \tilde g
=
-i\,a(r)\,\tilde f'
+\frac{b(r)\kappa}{r}\,\tilde f
-i\,\frac{c(r)\kappa}{r}\,\tilde g
-\varsigma\,\mu(r)\,\tilde g.
}
\]

So the genuinely dynamical coefficients are only
\[
a(r),\quad b(r),\quad c(r),\quad \mu(r).
\]

\section{Asymptotic large-\(r\) criterion}

Assume the profiles approach bulk limits
\[
a(r)\to a_\infty>0,
\qquad
b(r)\to b_\infty,
\qquad
c(r)\to c_\infty,
\qquad
\mu(r)\to \mu_\infty,
\qquad
|\mu_\infty|>0.
\]

Then the \(1/r\) angular terms vanish as \(r\to\infty\), and the zero-mode equations asymptotically reduce to
\[
-i\,a_\infty\,\tilde g'(r)+\varsigma\,\mu_\infty\,\tilde f(r)\approx 0,
\]
\[
-i\,a_\infty\,\tilde f'(r)-\varsigma\,\mu_\infty\,\tilde g(r)\approx 0.
\]

Equivalently, after one more constant phase redefinition, this yields the second-order asymptotic equation
\[
\tilde f''(r)\approx \frac{\mu_\infty^2}{a_\infty^2}\tilde f(r),
\qquad
\tilde g''(r)\approx \frac{\mu_\infty^2}{a_\infty^2}\tilde g(r).
\]

Hence the normalizable asymptotic branch behaves as
\[
\boxed{
\tilde f(r),\tilde g(r)\sim \exp\!\left(-\frac{|\mu_\infty|}{a_\infty}r\right).
}
\]

This gives the explicit radial origin of exponential localization:
the bulk gap is controlled by \(|\mu_\infty|\), while the effective radial velocity is \(a_\infty\).

\section{Near-core behavior}

Near \(r=0\), the \(1/r\) angular terms dominate.
The regularity condition is therefore controlled by the pair
\[
\frac{\kappa\,b(r)}{r},
\qquad
\frac{\kappa\,c(r)}{r}.
\]

If the profiles are smooth at the origin and
\[
a(0),b(0),c(0),\mu(0)
\]
are finite, then Frobenius analysis gives power-law behavior
\[
f(r),g(r)\sim r^\nu
\]
with exponents determined by the angular matrix
\[
\kappa
\begin{pmatrix}
i\,c(0) & -b(0)\\
+b(0) & -i\,c(0)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

Thus the actual existence of a regular zero mode is reduced to matching:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a regular near-core branch,
\item a decaying large-\(r\) branch.
\end{enumerate}

This is exactly the standard defect-bound-state shooting problem.

\section{What is now rigorously closed}

The following are now fully fixed at the operator level:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the radial single-defect operator admits a clean partial-wave decomposition;
\item each angular channel reduces to a \(2\times2\) first-order radial system;
\item the radial connection term can be gauged away by a scalar integrating factor;
\item the normalizable large-\(r\) behavior is governed by the ratio \(|\mu_\infty|/a_\infty\);
\item the existence of a single-defect light mode is now a concrete ODE boundary-value problem.
\end{enumerate}

\section{What remains open}

What remains TECT-specific is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the actual radial profiles
\[
\bar\sigma(r),\quad X_\parallel(r),\quad X_\perp(r);
\]

\item the actual constitutive functions entering
\[
a(r),\quad b(r),\quad c(r),\quad \mu(r);
\]

\item the grading/index analysis that identifies which \((\kappa,\varsigma)\) channel carries the protected mode;

\item the proof that exactly one regular decaying zero mode exists.
\end{enumerate}

So the single-defect one-mode problem has now been reduced from a PDE to a concrete radial ODE classification problem.

\section{Final summary}

The radial single-defect reference operator admits a full partial-wave decomposition.

Defining
\[
a(r)=\frac{g_R(r)}{z_0(r)},
\qquad
b(r)=\frac{g_E(r)}{z_0(r)},
\qquad
c(r)=\frac{g_O(r)}{z_0(r)},
\qquad
\mu(r)=\frac{m_{\rm eff}(r)}{z_0(r)},
\]
the canonically normalized operator can be written as
\[
\mathbb H_{\rm def}
=
-i\,a(r)\Gamma_{\hat n}\partial_r
+\frac{b(r)}{r}\Gamma_{\hat n}\mathcal D_{S^2}
+\frac{i\,c(r)}{r}\mathcal D_{S^2}
-i\,\omega_r(r)\Gamma_{\hat n}
+\mu(r)\Gamma^\sharp.
\]

For each angular channel
\[
\mathcal D_{S^2}Y_{\kappa m\varsigma}=\kappa Y_{\kappa m\varsigma},
\qquad
\Gamma^\sharp Y_{\kappa m\varsigma}=\varsigma Y_{\kappa m\varsigma},
\]
the mode ansatz
\[
\chi(r,\Omega)=f(r)Y_{\kappa m\varsigma}(\Omega)+g(r)\Gamma_{\hat n}Y_{\kappa m\varsigma}(\Omega)
\]
reduces the defect problem to a \(2\times2\) radial first-order system:
\[
\omega f
=
-i\,a(r)\,g'
-i\,\omega_r(r)\,g
-\frac{b(r)\kappa}{r}\,g
+i\,\frac{c(r)\kappa}{r}\,f
+\varsigma\,\mu(r)\,f,
\]
\[
\omega g
=
-i\,a(r)\,f'
-i\,\omega_r(r)\,f
+\frac{b(r)\kappa}{r}\,f
-i\,\frac{c(r)\kappa}{r}\,g
-\varsigma\,\mu(r)\,g.
\]

After removing the radial connection term by an integrating factor, the dynamical coefficients are only
\[
a(r),\quad b(r),\quad c(r),\quad \mu(r).
\]

As \(r\to\infty\), if
\[
a(r)\to a_\infty>0,
\qquad
\mu(r)\to \mu_\infty\neq 0,
\]
then the normalizable branch decays like
\[
\exp\!\left(-\frac{|\mu_\infty|}{a_\infty}r\right).
\]

Therefore the single-defect light-mode problem is now reduced to a concrete radial boundary-value problem:
one must determine whether there exists a regular near-core solution that matches onto the decaying large-\(r\) branch in exactly one protected channel.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Grading structure and classification of the index-carrying radial channel}

We now connect the radial single-defect ODE to the Callias/graded structure and classify which partial-wave channels can carry protected zero modes.

\section{Callias core versus the odd tangential perturbation}

From the previous step, the canonically normalized radial operator is
\[
\mathbb H_{\rm def}
=
-i\,a(r)\Gamma_{\hat n}\partial_r
+\frac{b(r)}{r}\Gamma_{\hat n}\mathcal D_{S^2}
+\frac{i\,c(r)}{r}\mathcal D_{S^2}
-i\,\omega_r(r)\Gamma_{\hat n}
+\mu(r)\Gamma^\sharp.
\]

We separate it into
\[
\boxed{
\mathbb H_{\rm def}=\mathbb H_{\rm C}+\mathbb V_O,
}
\]
where the Callias core is
\[
\boxed{
\mathbb H_{\rm C}
:=
-i\,a(r)\Gamma_{\hat n}\partial_r
+\frac{b(r)}{r}\Gamma_{\hat n}\mathcal D_{S^2}
-i\,\omega_r(r)\Gamma_{\hat n}
+\mu(r)\Gamma^\sharp,
}
\]
and the odd tangential term is
\[
\boxed{
\mathbb V_O:=\frac{i\,c(r)}{r}\mathcal D_{S^2}.
}
\]

\section{Grading operator}

Assume there exists a Hermitian involution
\[
\mathcal C=\mathcal C^\dagger,
\qquad
\mathcal C^2=\mathbf 1,
\]
such that
\[
\boxed{
\{\mathcal C,\Gamma_{\hat n}\}=0,
\qquad
\{\mathcal C,\Gamma^\sharp\}=0,
\qquad
[\mathcal C,\mathcal D_{S^2}]=0.
}
\]

Then
\[
\{\mathcal C,\mathbb H_{\rm C}\}=0,
\]
so \(\mathbb H_{\rm C}\) is the genuine graded Callias operator.
By contrast,
\[
[\mathcal C,\mathbb V_O]=0,
\]
so the \(c(r)\)-term breaks the exact grading of the full operator.

This yields the correct conceptual split:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the index is defined by the Callias core } \mathbb H_{\rm C},
}
\]
while
\[
\boxed{
\mathbb V_O
\text{ is a lower-order grading-breaking perturbation.}
}
\]

\section{Angular basis adapted to the grading}

Because
\[
[\mathcal C,\mathcal D_{S^2}]=0,
\]
we may choose angular modes
\[
Y_{\kappa m s}(\Omega)
\]
satisfying
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal D_{S^2}Y_{\kappa m s}=\kappa\,Y_{\kappa m s},
\qquad
\mathcal C\,Y_{\kappa m s}=s\,Y_{\kappa m s},
\qquad
s=\pm 1.
}
\]

Since
\[
\{\Gamma_{\hat n},\mathcal C\}=0,
\qquad
\{\Gamma_{\hat n},\mathcal D_{S^2}\}=0,
\]
one has
\[
\mathcal D_{S^2}(\Gamma_{\hat n}Y_{\kappa m s})=-\kappa\,\Gamma_{\hat n}Y_{\kappa m s},
\qquad
\mathcal C(\Gamma_{\hat n}Y_{\kappa m s})=-s\,\Gamma_{\hat n}Y_{\kappa m s}.
\]

Thus a fixed radial channel is naturally spanned by
\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{span}\{Y_{\kappa m s},\ \Gamma_{\hat n}Y_{\kappa m s}\}.
}
\]

\section{Gauge removal and chiral block form}

As already shown, the radial connection term can be removed by the scalar integrating factor
\[
\mathcal I(r)=\exp\!\left(\int^r\frac{\omega_r(s)}{a(s)}\,ds\right).
\]

After this gauge removal and the standard unitary radial measure transformation
\[
(f,g)\mapsto r(f,g),
\]
the Callias core in a fixed \((\kappa,m)\)-channel takes the chiral block form
\[
\boxed{
\mathbb H_{{\rm C},\kappa}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & Q_{\kappa,-}^{\rm core}\\
Q_{\kappa,+}^{\rm core} & 0
\end{pmatrix},
}
\]
with first-order scalar operators
\[
\boxed{
Q_{\kappa,\pm}^{\rm core}
=
\pm a(r)\frac{d}{dr}
+
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r).
}
\]

In the minimal radial constitutive ansatz, the real superpotential is
\[
\boxed{
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)
=
\mu(r)+\frac{\kappa\,b(r)}{r},
}
\]
up to the sign convention that labels the channel \(\kappa\).

\section{Kernel dimension and explicit zero-mode generators}

Since \(Q_{\kappa,\pm}^{\rm core}\) are first-order scalar ODE operators,
their kernels are at most one-dimensional:
\[
\dim\ker Q_{\kappa,\pm}^{\rm core}\le 1.
\]

Indeed, the formal zero-mode generators are
\[
\boxed{
u_{\kappa,+}(r)
=
\exp\!\left(
-\int^r \frac{W_\kappa^{\rm core}(s)}{a(s)}\,ds
\right),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
u_{\kappa,-}(r)
=
\exp\!\left(
+\int^r \frac{W_\kappa^{\rm core}(s)}{a(s)}\,ds
\right).
}
\]

Thus the channel index is
\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{ind}_\kappa
:=
\dim\ker Q_{\kappa,+}^{\rm core}
-
\dim\ker Q_{\kappa,-}^{\rm core}
\in\{-1,0,1\}.
}
\]

The contribution of a given channel is therefore completely determined by the \(L^2\)-normalizability of these two explicit generators.

\section{Effect of the \(g_O\) channel}

Now include the grading-breaking term
\[
\mathbb V_O=\frac{i\,c(r)}{r}\mathcal D_{S^2}.
\]
On a fixed \(\kappa\)-channel this becomes
\[
\boxed{
\mathbb V_{O,\kappa}
=
i\,\frac{\kappa c(r)}{r}\,\mathbf 1.
}
\]

Hence the full chiral radial operators are
\[
\boxed{
Q_{\kappa,\pm}^{\rm full}
=
\pm a(r)\frac{d}{dr}
+
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)
+
i\,\frac{\kappa c(r)}{r}.
}
\]

This is a decisive observation:
the \(g_O\)-term enters as a purely imaginary scalar addition to the superpotential.

Therefore the formal zero-mode generators become
\[
u_{\kappa,\pm}^{\rm full}(r)
=
\exp\!\left(
\mp\int^r \frac{W_\kappa^{\rm core}(s)}{a(s)}\,ds
\right)
\cdot
\exp\!\left(
\mp i\kappa\int^r \frac{c(s)}{a(s)s}\,ds
\right).
\]

The second factor is a pure phase.
Hence

\[
\boxed{
\text{the \(g_O\)-channel changes the phase of the radial zero-mode generator,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{it does not change its }L^2\text{-normalizability.}
}
\]

So the existence or nonexistence of a normalizable protected channel is controlled entirely by the real Callias core superpotential \(W_\kappa^{\rm core}\).

\section{Channel-selection criterion}

We may now state the exact channel criterion.

\paragraph{Proposition (index-carrying channel criterion).}
Fix a channel \((\kappa,m)\).
Then the corresponding protected zero-mode contribution is nonzero if and only if exactly one of the two generators
\[
u_{\kappa,+}^{\rm core},
\qquad
u_{\kappa,-}^{\rm core}
\]
belongs to the radial \(L^2\)-space.
Equivalently,
\[
\operatorname{ind}_\kappa\neq 0
\iff
\text{exactly one of }Q_{\kappa,+}^{\rm core},Q_{\kappa,-}^{\rm core}\text{ has a normalizable kernel.}
\]

\paragraph{Proof.}
Because the kernels are at most one-dimensional and the full \(g_O\)-term only adds a phase, the only possibilities are:
\[
(\dim\ker Q_{\kappa,+},\dim\ker Q_{\kappa,-})
\in
\{(0,0),(1,0),(0,1)\}.
\]
Hence
\[
\operatorname{ind}_\kappa\in\{0,\pm1\},
\]
and the index is nonzero exactly when one and only one chiral generator is \(L^2\)-normalizable.
\(\square\)

\section{Lowest-channel dominance and the one-protected-channel criterion}

In most radial Dirac/Callias problems, the angular spectrum obeys
\[
|\kappa|\ge \kappa_{\min}>0.
\]
Typically the strongest candidate for a protected mode is the lowest channel
\[
|\kappa|=\kappa_{\min},
\]
because the centrifugal contribution
\[
\frac{\kappa b(r)}{r}
\]
is smallest there.

This leads to the following conditional theorem schema.

\paragraph{Theorem (conditional one-protected-channel criterion).}
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item for every channel with \(|\kappa|>\kappa_{\min}\), neither \(u_{\kappa,+}^{\rm core}\) nor \(u_{\kappa,-}^{\rm core}\) is \(L^2\)-normalizable;

\item for exactly one lowest channel \(\kappa=\kappa_*\) (after accounting for any residual symmetry/projector reduction), exactly one of
\[
u_{\kappa_*,+}^{\rm core},
\qquad
u_{\kappa_*,-}^{\rm core}
\]
is \(L^2\)-normalizable.
\end{enumerate}

Then
\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{Ind}(\mathbb H_{\rm C})=\pm 1,
}
\]
and the single defect carries exactly one protected radial channel.

If, moreover, the relevant lowest-channel multiplicity is one, then
\[
\boxed{
\text{one defect } \leftrightarrow \text{ one protected light mode.}
}
\]

\paragraph{Comment.}
The point here is complete honesty:
the reduction to channel counting is now exact,
but the actual verification of the hypotheses depends on the concrete TECT profiles \(a(r),b(r),\mu(r)\) and on the angular multiplicity structure of the chosen bundle.

\section{Asymptotic diagnostic for the channel index}

Since
\[
u_{\kappa,\pm}^{\rm core}(r)
=
\exp\!\left(
\mp\int^r \frac{W_\kappa^{\rm core}(s)}{a(s)}\,ds
\right),
\qquad
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)=\mu(r)+\frac{\kappa b(r)}{r},
\]
the channel selection is controlled by the asymptotics of
\[
\frac{W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)}{a(r)}.
\]

At infinity, if
\[
a(r)\to a_\infty>0,
\qquad
\mu(r)\to \mu_\infty\neq 0,
\]
then
\[
\frac{W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)}{a(r)}
\to
\frac{\mu_\infty}{a_\infty},
\]
so one of the two chiral generators decays and the other grows exponentially.

Near the core, the sign and magnitude of
\[
\frac{\kappa b(r)}{a(r)r}
\]
control regularity.
Thus the protected-channel problem is precisely a matching problem between:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the near-core regular branch selected by the centrifugal/superpotential term;
\item the large-\(r\) decaying branch selected by \(\mu_\infty/a_\infty\).
\end{enumerate}

This is the exact radial meaning of the index-carrying channel criterion.

\section{What is now rigorously closed}

The following points are now fixed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the exact graded Callias core is obtained by dropping the \(g_O\)-term from the full radial operator;
\item each fixed \(\kappa\)-channel reduces to a one-dimensional chiral supercharge pair
\[
Q_{\kappa,\pm}^{\rm core}=\pm a(r)\partial_r+W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r);
\]
\item the channel index is nonzero iff exactly one chiral generator is \(L^2\)-normalizable;
\item the \(g_O\)-term contributes only a phase and therefore does not change the \(L^2\)-normalizability classification;
\item the one-defect/one-channel statement reduces to a lowest-channel uniqueness question.
\end{enumerate}

\section{What remains open}

What remains TECT-specific is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the explicit grading operator \(\mathcal C\);
\item the actual functions \(a(r),b(r),c(r),\mu(r)\);
\item the actual angular spectrum and its multiplicities;
\item the proof that exactly one lowest channel has a normalizable chiral generator.
\end{enumerate}

So the problem has now been reduced to its final concrete form:
determine the real superpotential
\[
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)=\mu(r)+\frac{\kappa b(r)}{r}
\]
for the actual TECT defect profiles and classify which channels produce \(L^2\)-normalizable zero-mode generators.

\section{Final summary}

We introduced a grading operator \(\mathcal C\) satisfying
\[
\{\mathcal C,\Gamma_{\hat n}\}=0,
\qquad
\{\mathcal C,\Gamma^\sharp\}=0,
\qquad
[\mathcal C,\mathcal D_{S^2}]=0.
\]

With this grading, the radial single-defect operator splits into:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the genuine graded Callias core
\[
\mathbb H_{\rm C}
=
-i\,a(r)\Gamma_{\hat n}\partial_r
+\frac{b(r)}{r}\Gamma_{\hat n}\mathcal D_{S^2}
-i\,\omega_r(r)\Gamma_{\hat n}
+\mu(r)\Gamma^\sharp,
\]

\item the grading-breaking odd tangential perturbation
\[
\mathbb V_O=\frac{i\,c(r)}{r}\mathcal D_{S^2}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

After gauge removal and radial reduction, each fixed \(\kappa\)-channel of the Callias core takes the chiral block form
\[
\mathbb H_{{\rm C},\kappa}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & Q_{\kappa,-}^{\rm core}\\
Q_{\kappa,+}^{\rm core} & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
Q_{\kappa,\pm}^{\rm core}
=
\pm a(r)\frac{d}{dr}
+
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r),
\]
with
\[
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)=\mu(r)+\frac{\kappa b(r)}{r}.
\]

Hence the channel index is
\[
\operatorname{ind}_\kappa
=
\dim\ker Q_{\kappa,+}^{\rm core}
-
\dim\ker Q_{\kappa,-}^{\rm core},
\]
and it is nonzero iff exactly one of the two chiral generators is \(L^2\)-normalizable.

The \(g_O\)-term only adds the purely imaginary shift
\[
i\,\frac{\kappa c(r)}{r}
\]
to the superpotential, so it changes only the phase of the zero-mode generator and not its normalizability.

Therefore the protected-channel classification is controlled entirely by the real superpotential
\[
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)=\mu(r)+\frac{\kappa b(r)}{r}.
\]

So the single-defect one-mode problem has now been reduced to its final concrete form:
determine which \(\kappa\)-channel has exactly one \(L^2\)-normalizable chiral generator.
If exactly one lowest channel does so, then one defect carries one protected light mode.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{A sufficient criterion for a unique protected lowest-\(\kappa\) channel}

We now turn the single-defect light-mode problem into an explicit sufficient criterion on the real Callias-core superpotential
\[
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)=\mu(r)+\frac{\kappa\,b(r)}{r}.
\]

\section{Callias-core channel generators}

After gauge removal and radial measure normalization, the graded core operator in a fixed partial-wave channel \(\kappa\) is
\[
\mathbb H_{{\rm C},\kappa}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & Q_{\kappa,-}^{\rm core}\\
Q_{\kappa,+}^{\rm core} & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
Q_{\kappa,\pm}^{\rm core}
=
\pm a(r)\frac{d}{dr}+W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r),
\]
with
\[
a(r)>0,
\qquad
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)=\mu(r)+\frac{\kappa b(r)}{r}.
\]

The formal zero-mode generators are
\[
u_{\kappa,+}(r)
=
\exp\!\left(
-\int^r\frac{W_\kappa^{\rm core}(s)}{a(s)}\,ds
\right),
\qquad
u_{\kappa,-}(r)
=
\exp\!\left(
+\int^r\frac{W_\kappa^{\rm core}(s)}{a(s)}\,ds
\right).
\]

Since each \(Q_{\kappa,\pm}^{\rm core}\) is first-order scalar, its kernel is at most one-dimensional.
Hence
\[
\operatorname{ind}_\kappa
=
\dim\ker Q_{\kappa,+}^{\rm core}
-
\dim\ker Q_{\kappa,-}^{\rm core}
\in\{-1,0,1\},
\]
and it is nonzero iff exactly one of \(u_{\kappa,+},u_{\kappa,-}\) is \(L^2\)-normalizable.

\section{Asymptotic large-\(r\) decay criterion}

Assume
\[
a(r)\to a_\infty>0,
\qquad
\mu(r)\to \mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
b(r)=O(1)
\qquad (r\to\infty).
\]
Then
\[
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)\to \mu_\infty>0,
\]
so
\[
u_{\kappa,+}(r)\sim
\exp\!\left(-\frac{\mu_\infty}{a_\infty}r\right),
\qquad
u_{\kappa,-}(r)\sim
\exp\!\left(+\frac{\mu_\infty}{a_\infty}r\right).
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
u_{\kappa,+}\text{ is the unique asymptotically decaying branch for every admissible }\kappa,
}
\]
while
\[
\boxed{
u_{\kappa,-}\text{ is never normalizable at infinity.}
}
\]

So the only question is whether \(u_{\kappa,+}\) is regular enough at the core.

\section{Near-core criterion}

Assume that near \(r=0\),
\[
a(r)\to a_0>0,
\qquad
b(r)\to b_0>0,
\qquad
\mu(r)=O(1).
\]
Then
\[
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)
=
\mu(r)+\frac{\kappa b(r)}{r}
=
\frac{\kappa b_0}{r}+O(1).
\]

Hence
\[
u_{\kappa,+}(r)
\sim
r^{-\kappa b_0/a_0},
\qquad
u_{\kappa,-}(r)
\sim
r^{+\kappa b_0/a_0}.
\]

After the standard unitary radial measure reduction, the radial \(L^2\)-space is \(L^2((0,\infty),dr)\).
Thus a sufficient near-core criterion is:

\[
\boxed{
u_{\kappa,+}\in L^2(0,r_0)
\quad\Leftarrow\quad
-\frac{\kappa b_0}{a_0}>-\frac12,
}
\]
that is,
\[
\boxed{
\frac{\kappa b_0}{a_0}<\frac12.
}
\]

Likewise, a sufficient exclusion criterion is
\[
\boxed{
u_{\kappa,+}\notin L^2(0,r_0)
\quad\Leftarrow\quad
\frac{\kappa b_0}{a_0}\ge \frac12.
}
\]

This already shows how channel exclusion can occur:
channels with too large positive effective centrifugal coefficient cannot support the decaying chiral generator.

\section{Monotone sign-flip criterion for a protected channel}

We now state a sharper sufficient criterion that uses the full sign structure of \(W_\kappa^{\rm core}\).

\paragraph{Assumptions.}
Let \(\mathfrak K_{\rm adm}\) be the discrete set of admissible angular channels after all bundle/grading/projector reductions.
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(a(r)\) is continuous and strictly positive on \((0,\infty)\);
\item \(\mu(r)\) is continuous, monotone increasing, and satisfies
\[
\mu(0)\le 0<\mu_\infty:=\lim_{r\to\infty}\mu(r);
\]
\item \(b(r)\) is continuous, nonnegative, and \(b(r)/r\) is monotone decreasing on \((0,\infty)\);
\item there exists a unique channel \(\kappa_*\in\mathfrak K_{\rm adm}\) such that
\[
W_{\kappa_*}^{\rm core}(r)<0
\quad\text{for }0<r<r_c,
\qquad
W_{\kappa_*}^{\rm core}(r)>0
\quad\text{for }r>R_c,
\]
for some \(0<r_c<R_c<\infty\);
\item for every \(\kappa\neq\kappa_*\) in \(\mathfrak K_{\rm adm}\), one has
\[
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)\ge \frac{\gamma_\kappa}{r}
\quad\text{for }0<r<r_c,
\qquad
\gamma_\kappa>\frac{a_0}{2},
\]
so that \(u_{\kappa,+}\notin L^2(0,r_c)\).
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{Theorem (unique protected channel by monotone sign-flip).}
Under the above assumptions, exactly one channel contributes a protected chiral zero mode:
\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{ind}_{\kappa_*}=+1,
\qquad
\operatorname{ind}_\kappa=0
\quad(\kappa\neq \kappa_*).
}
\]
Consequently,
\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{Ind}(\mathbb H_{\rm C})=+1.
}
\]

\paragraph{Proof.}
For every channel, \(u_{\kappa,-}\) is excluded by the positive asymptotic mass gap \(\mu_\infty>0\), hence
\[
u_{\kappa,-}\notin L^2(R,\infty).
\]
So only \(u_{\kappa,+}\) can possibly contribute.

For \(\kappa=\kappa_*\), the near-core negativity of \(W_{\kappa_*}^{\rm core}\) implies
\[
u_{\kappa_*,+}(r)
=
\exp\!\left(
-\int^r \frac{W_{\kappa_*}^{\rm core}(s)}{a(s)}\,ds
\right)
\]
is regular near the origin, while the asymptotic positivity implies exponential decay at infinity.
Hence \(u_{\kappa_*,+}\in L^2(0,\infty)\), so
\[
\dim\ker Q_{\kappa_*,+}^{\rm core}=1,
\qquad
\dim\ker Q_{\kappa_*,-}^{\rm core}=0.
\]
Therefore
\[
\operatorname{ind}_{\kappa_*}=1.
\]

For any \(\kappa\neq\kappa_*\), the near-core lower bound
\[
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)\ge \frac{\gamma_\kappa}{r},
\qquad
\gamma_\kappa>\frac{a_0}{2},
\]
implies
\[
u_{\kappa,+}(r)
\lesssim r^{-\gamma_\kappa/a_0},
\]
which is not \(L^2\) near \(r=0\).
So
\[
\dim\ker Q_{\kappa,+}^{\rm core}=0
\]
for all \(\kappa\neq\kappa_*\).
Since \(u_{\kappa,-}\) is already excluded at infinity, one gets
\[
\operatorname{ind}_\kappa=0
\qquad
(\kappa\neq\kappa_*).
\]
Summing over channels yields
\[
\operatorname{Ind}(\mathbb H_{\rm C})=1.
\]
\(\square\)

\section{Lowest-channel dominance as a practical corollary}

The previous theorem is abstractly clean but still depends on the admissible channel set.
In practice, one usually has an ordered channel family
\[
|\kappa_1|<|\kappa_2|<|\kappa_3|<\cdots,
\]
and \(b(r)\ge 0\) makes the centrifugal contribution larger for higher channels.

This yields the practical corollary:

\paragraph{Corollary (lowest-channel dominance).}
Suppose there exists a lowest admissible channel \(\kappa_{\min}\) such that

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(W_{\kappa_{\min}}^{\rm core}\) has the required sign-flip structure:
\[
W_{\kappa_{\min}}^{\rm core}(r)<0 \text{ near }r=0,
\qquad
W_{\kappa_{\min}}^{\rm core}(r)>0 \text{ for large }r;
\]

\item for every higher channel \(\kappa\neq \kappa_{\min}\), the centrifugal coefficient is sufficiently larger so that
\[
\frac{\kappa b_0}{a_0}\ge \frac12
\]
near the origin.
\end{enumerate}

Then only the lowest admissible channel can carry a protected zero mode.

This is the mathematically clean version of the slogan:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the protected defect mode lives in the lowest angular channel.}
}
\]

\section{Role of the odd tangential coefficient \(g_O\)}

Now restore the full operator by including
\[
\mathbb V_O=\frac{i\,c(r)}{r}\mathcal D_{S^2}.
\]
On a fixed \(\kappa\)-channel, this adds
\[
i\,\frac{\kappa c(r)}{r}
\]
to the radial superpotential.
Thus
\[
u_{\kappa,+}^{\rm full}(r)
=
u_{\kappa,+}^{\rm core}(r)
\cdot
\exp\!\left(
-i\kappa\int^r \frac{c(s)}{a(s)s}\,ds
\right).
\]

Hence:

\[
\boxed{
g_O(r)\text{ modifies the channel wavefunction by a phase only,}
}
\]
and therefore
\[
\boxed{
g_O(r)\text{ does not change which channel is }L^2\text{-normalizable.}
}
\]

So the protected-channel classification is entirely governed by the real core data
\[
a(r),\qquad b(r),\qquad \mu(r),
\]
or equivalently by the real superpotential
\[
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)=\mu(r)+\frac{\kappa b(r)}{r}.
\]

\section{What is now rigorously closed}

The following points are now fixed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the protected-channel problem reduces to the scalar superpotential
\[
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)=\mu(r)+\frac{\kappa b(r)}{r};
\]

\item the asymptotic bulk gap selects \(u_{\kappa,+}\) as the only decaying branch;

\item channel exclusion is determined by the near-core behavior of \(u_{\kappa,+}\);

\item under a unique sign-flip condition, exactly one admissible channel carries the index;

\item the odd tangential channel \(g_O\) affects only the phase and not the normalizability classification.
\end{enumerate}

\section{What remains open}

What is still TECT-specific is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the actual admissible channel set \(\mathfrak K_{\rm adm}\);
\item the actual profiles \(a(r),b(r),\mu(r)\);
\item the proof that exactly one admissible lowest channel satisfies the sign-flip criterion.
\end{enumerate}

So the one-defect/one-mode problem has now been reduced to a concrete sufficient criterion on the real radial superpotential.

\section{Final summary}

The single-defect protected-channel problem is controlled by the real Callias-core superpotential
\[
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)=\mu(r)+\frac{\kappa b(r)}{r}.
\]

For each channel,
\[
Q_{\kappa,\pm}^{\rm core}
=
\pm a(r)\frac{d}{dr}+W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r),
\]
so the formal generators are
\[
u_{\kappa,+}(r)
=
\exp\!\left(
-\int^r\frac{W_\kappa^{\rm core}(s)}{a(s)}\,ds
\right),
\qquad
u_{\kappa,-}(r)
=
\exp\!\left(
+\int^r\frac{W_\kappa^{\rm core}(s)}{a(s)}\,ds
\right).
\]

If \(\mu_\infty>0\), then only \(u_{\kappa,+}\) can decay at infinity.
Hence channel selection reduces entirely to near-core regularity of \(u_{\kappa,+}\).

Under a monotone sign-flip hypothesis --- namely, that there exists a unique admissible channel \(\kappa_*\) for which
\[
W_{\kappa_*}^{\rm core}(r)<0 \text{ near }r=0,
\qquad
W_{\kappa_*}^{\rm core}(r)>0 \text{ for large }r,
\]
while all other admissible channels have \(u_{\kappa,+}\notin L^2\) near the core --- one obtains
\[
\operatorname{ind}_{\kappa_*}=1,
\qquad
\operatorname{ind}_\kappa=0 \quad (\kappa\neq\kappa_*),
\]
and therefore
\[
\operatorname{Ind}(\mathbb H_{\rm C})=1.
\]

Moreover, the odd tangential coefficient \(g_O(r)\) only adds the phase
\[
\exp\!\left(-i\kappa\int^r \frac{c(s)}{a(s)s}\,ds\right)
\]
to the radial generator, so it does not affect normalizability and does not change the protected-channel counting.

Thus the one-defect/one-protected-mode problem has been reduced to a sufficient criterion on the real radial profiles \(a(r),b(r),\mu(r)\).

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{A profile-level sufficient criterion for the one-defect/one-mode statement}

We now combine the radial Callias-core reduction with the previously established remote-gap isolation to obtain a concrete sufficient criterion for
\[
\text{one defect } \leftrightarrow \text{ one protected light mode.}
\]

\section{Step 1: spectral isolation of the low angular slot}

Let the full single-defect fluctuation operator be decomposed into
\[
\mathbb H_{\rm full}
=
\mathbb H_{\rm low}\oplus \mathbb H_{\rm rem}
+
\text{off-diagonal couplings},
\]
where \(\mathbb H_{\rm low}\) denotes the candidate lowest angular/valley slot and \(\mathbb H_{\rm rem}\) contains all higher angular channels, wrong-internal sectors, and other remote pieces.

Assume the previously established remote-gap criterion holds uniformly:
\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{spec}(\mathbb H_{\rm rem})
\cap
(-\Delta_{\rm rem},\Delta_{\rm rem})
=
\varnothing,
\qquad
\Delta_{\rm rem}>0.
}
\]

Then any zero or near-zero protected mode must lie entirely in the low slot.
Hence the protected-mode problem reduces to the projected lowest channel.

\section{Step 2: projected lowest-channel Callias core}

Let the lowest projected channel be labeled by \(\kappa_*\).
After gauge removal and radial measure normalization, its graded Callias-core operator is
\[
\mathbb H_{{\rm C},\kappa_*}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & Q_{\kappa_*,-}^{\rm core}\\
Q_{\kappa_*,+}^{\rm core} & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
Q_{\kappa_*,\pm}^{\rm core}
=
\pm a(r)\frac{d}{dr}
+
W_*(r),
\]
where
\[
\boxed{
W_*(r):=W_{\kappa_*}^{\rm core}(r)=\mu(r)+\frac{\kappa_*\,b(r)}{r},
\qquad
a(r)>0.
}
\]

The formal zero-mode generators are
\[
u_+(r)
=
\exp\!\left(
-\int^r\frac{W_*(s)}{a(s)}\,ds
\right),
\qquad
u_-(r)
=
\exp\!\left(
+\int^r\frac{W_*(s)}{a(s)}\,ds
\right).
\]

\section{Profile inequalities}

We now impose explicit sufficient inequalities directly on \(W_*(r)\).

\paragraph{Assumption P1 (uniform positive radial velocity).}
There exists \(a_*>0\) such that
\[
a(r)\ge a_*>0
\qquad (r>0).
\]

\paragraph{Assumption P2 (core negativity with \(L^2\) margin).}
There exist \(r_0>0\) and \(\varepsilon_0>0\) such that
\[
\boxed{
W_*(r)\le -\left(\frac12+\varepsilon_0\right)\frac{a(r)}{r}
\qquad (0<r<r_0).
}
\]

\paragraph{Assumption P3 (bulk positivity).}
There exist \(R_0>r_0\) and \(m_*>0\) such that
\[
\boxed{
W_*(r)\ge m_*
\qquad (r>R_0).
}
\]

\paragraph{Assumption P4 (no competing low channels).}
For every other admissible channel \(\kappa\neq \kappa_*\) that survives the projector reduction, there exist \(r_\kappa>0\) and \(\varepsilon_\kappa>0\) such that
\[
\boxed{
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)\ge \left(\frac12+\varepsilon_\kappa\right)\frac{a(r)}{r}
\qquad (0<r<r_\kappa).
}
\]
This ensures that the decaying chiral generator in those channels is not \(L^2\)-regular near the core.

\section{Main theorem}

\paragraph{Theorem (profile-level one-defect/one-mode sufficient criterion).}
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the remote-gap isolation holds, so that only the projected lowest slot can host a zero mode;
\item the projected lowest channel \(\kappa_*\) satisfies P1--P3;
\item all competing projected channels satisfy P4.
\end{enumerate}

Then
\[
\boxed{
\dim\ker Q_{\kappa_*,+}^{\rm core}=1,
\qquad
\dim\ker Q_{\kappa_*,-}^{\rm core}=0,
}
\]
and for every \(\kappa\neq \kappa_*\),
\[
\boxed{
\dim\ker Q_{\kappa,+}^{\rm core}
=
\dim\ker Q_{\kappa,-}^{\rm core}
=
0.
}
\]
Consequently,
\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{Ind}(\mathbb H_{\rm C})=+1,
}
\]
and the defect carries exactly one protected light mode in the low slot.

\paragraph{Proof.}
From P3,
\[
u_+(r)\sim \exp\!\left(-\int^r \frac{W_*(s)}{a(s)}\,ds\right)
\]
decays exponentially for \(r>R_0\), while
\[
u_-(r)\sim \exp\!\left(+\int^r \frac{W_*(s)}{a(s)}\,ds\right)
\]
grows exponentially, so \(u_-\notin L^2(R_0,\infty)\).

From P2,
\[
-\frac{W_*(r)}{a(r)}\ge \left(\frac12+\varepsilon_0\right)\frac1r
\qquad (0<r<r_0),
\]
hence
\[
u_+(r)
=
\exp\!\left(-\int^r \frac{W_*(s)}{a(s)}\,ds\right)
\lesssim r^{1/2+\varepsilon_0},
\]
so \(u_+\in L^2(0,r_0)\).
Therefore \(u_+\in L^2(0,\infty)\), and since the kernel of a first-order scalar operator is at most one-dimensional,
\[
\dim\ker Q_{\kappa_*,+}^{\rm core}=1.
\]
Also \(\dim\ker Q_{\kappa_*,-}^{\rm core}=0\) by the large-\(r\) exclusion of \(u_-\).

Now let \(\kappa\neq\kappa_*\).
By P4,
\[
\frac{W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)}{a(r)}
\ge
\left(\frac12+\varepsilon_\kappa\right)\frac1r
\qquad (0<r<r_\kappa),
\]
so
\[
u_{\kappa,+}(r)
=
\exp\!\left(-\int^r \frac{W_\kappa^{\rm core}(s)}{a(s)}\,ds\right)
\gtrsim r^{-(1/2+\varepsilon_\kappa)},
\]
which is not \(L^2\) near \(r=0\).
Thus
\[
\dim\ker Q_{\kappa,+}^{\rm core}=0.
\]
As before, \(u_{\kappa,-}\) is excluded by the positive bulk gap.
Hence no competing channel contributes.

Therefore the total graded index is
\[
\operatorname{Ind}(\mathbb H_{\rm C})=1.
\]
Because the remote sector is uniformly gapped away from zero, this index is realized by exactly one protected low mode.
\(\square\)

\section{Monotone-profile corollary}

The previous theorem is stated directly in terms of \(W_*(r)\).
A more physical corollary is obtained from monotone profile assumptions.

\paragraph{Corollary (monotone mass profile version).}
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(a(r)\ge a_*>0\);
\item \(b(r)\ge 0\) and \(b(r)\) is bounded;
\item \(\mu(r)\) is continuous and monotone increasing;
\item there exists a unique projected channel \(\kappa_*\) such that
\[
\mu(r)+\frac{\kappa_* b(r)}{r}
\]
is negative near the core and positive for large \(r\);
\item for every other projected channel \(\kappa\neq \kappa_*\),
\[
\mu(r)+\frac{\kappa b(r)}{r}
\]
is positive near the core with the \(L^2\)-exclusion margin of P4.
\end{enumerate}

Then the conclusion of the theorem holds.

\paragraph{Comment.}
This is the operational form most likely to be checked in a concrete TECT profile calculation.
It says that the unique protected channel is the unique one whose real superpotential crosses from sufficiently negative near the core to strictly positive in the bulk.

\section{Role of the odd tangential coefficient}

Restore the grading-breaking odd tangential term
\[
\mathbb V_O=\frac{i\,c(r)}{r}\mathcal D_{S^2}.
\]
On the fixed projected channel \(\kappa_*\), this contributes
\[
i\,\frac{\kappa_* c(r)}{r}
\]
to the radial superpotential, so the full generator becomes
\[
u_+^{\rm full}(r)
=
u_+(r)\,
\exp\!\left(
-i\kappa_*\int^r \frac{c(s)}{a(s)s}\,ds
\right).
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
|u_+^{\rm full}(r)|=|u_+(r)|.
}
\]
Therefore the \(g_O\)-channel does not affect the \(L^2\)-normalizability criterion and does not alter the protected-mode counting.
It only changes the phase profile of the mode.

\section{What is now actually closed}

The one-defect/one-mode problem has now been reduced to a genuine profile inequality problem.

The following are now fixed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the remote-gap theorem removes all higher sectors from the zero-energy window;
\item the protected channel is determined entirely by the projected real superpotential
\[
W_*(r)=\mu(r)+\frac{\kappa_* b(r)}{r};
\]
\item explicit core and bulk inequalities P2--P3 are sufficient to produce one \(L^2\)-normalizable chiral generator;
\item explicit core positivity inequalities P4 exclude all competing projected channels;
\item the odd transport coefficient \(g_O\) changes only the phase, not the channel counting.
\end{enumerate}

\section{What remains TECT-specific}

What remains to be verified from the actual TECT defect solution is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the concrete projected channel \(\kappa_*\);
\item the actual radial profiles
\[
a(r),\quad b(r),\quad \mu(r);
\]
\item the validity of the profile inequalities P2--P4;
\item the actual remote-gap isolation of the higher channels in the same parameter regime.
\end{enumerate}

So the full conceptual chain is now closed:
the remaining work is a concrete profile verification problem.

\section{Final summary}

We combined the radial Callias-core reduction with the remote-gap theorem to obtain a concrete sufficient criterion for
\[
\text{one defect } \leftrightarrow \text{ one protected light mode.}
\]

Let the projected lowest channel be \(\kappa_*\), and define the real superpotential
\[
W_*(r)=\mu(r)+\frac{\kappa_* b(r)}{r}.
\]

If:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the remote sector is uniformly gapped away from zero;
\item \(a(r)\ge a_*>0\);
\item near the core,
\[
W_*(r)\le -\left(\frac12+\varepsilon_0\right)\frac{a(r)}{r};
\]
\item in the bulk,
\[
W_*(r)\ge m_*>0;
\]
\item every competing projected channel \(\kappa\neq\kappa_*\) satisfies
\[
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)\ge \left(\frac12+\varepsilon_\kappa\right)\frac{a(r)}{r}
\]
near the core,
\end{enumerate}

then exactly one chiral generator is \(L^2\)-normalizable, all competing channels are excluded, and
\[
\operatorname{Ind}(\mathbb H_{\rm C})=1.
\]

Thus the one-defect/one-mode problem has been reduced to verifying explicit inequalities for the real radial profiles \(a(r),b(r),\mu(r)\).

Moreover, the odd tangential coefficient \(g_O\) only contributes a phase and therefore does not affect the protected-channel counting.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Working radial profile ansatz and a concrete sufficient criterion for one defect / one protected mode}

We now impose a minimal working radial profile ansatz for the defect background and derive explicit sufficient inequalities on the resulting coefficients
\[
a(r),\qquad b(r),\qquad \mu(r)
\]
that guarantee exactly one protected channel.

\section{Working radial profile ansatz}

We assume a smooth radial single-defect background of the form
\[
\bar\sigma(r),\qquad
X_\perp(r),\qquad
X_\parallel(r),
\]
with the regularity conditions
\[
\bar\sigma(r)=\sigma_0+\sigma_2 r^2+O(r^4),
\]
\[
X_\perp(r)=X_0+x_{\perp,2}r^2+O(r^4),
\qquad
X_\parallel(r)=X_0+x_{\parallel,2}r^2+O(r^4),
\]
as \(r\to0\).
The equality
\[
X_\perp(0)=X_\parallel(0)=X_0
\]
is the smoothness condition required for the tensor
\[
\bar X_i{}^a
=
X_\perp(r)(\delta_i{}^a-\hat n_i\hat n^a)
+
X_\parallel(r)\hat n_i\hat n^a
\]
to be regular at the origin.

At large radius, assume exponential approach to the bulk vacuum:
\[
\bar\sigma(r)=\sigma_\infty-\Sigma_\infty e^{-m_\sigma r}+o(e^{-m_\sigma r}),
\]
\[
X_\perp(r)=X_{\perp,\infty}+A_\perp e^{-M_X r}+o(e^{-M_X r}),
\qquad
X_\parallel(r)=X_{\parallel,\infty}+A_\parallel e^{-M_X r}+o(e^{-M_X r}).
\]

In the simplest vacuum branch one has
\[
X_{\perp,\infty}=X_{\parallel,\infty}=0,
\]
but we keep the formulas general.

Define
\[
\chi_X(r):=\frac13\bigl(2X_\perp(r)+X_\parallel(r)\bigr).
\]
Then
\[
\chi_X(r)=X_0+O(r^2)
\qquad (r\to0),
\]
and
\[
\chi_X(r)\to \chi_\infty:=\frac13(2X_{\perp,\infty}+X_{\parallel,\infty})
\qquad (r\to\infty).
\]

\section{Radial constitutive coefficients}

From the previously fixed minimal constitutive choice,
\[
g_E(r)
=
v_\perp(\bar\sigma(r))
+
3\chi_X(r)\,v_E^{(X)}(\bar\sigma(r)),
\]
\[
g_c(r)
=
v_c(\bar\sigma(r))
+
3\chi_X(r)\,v_c^{(X)}(\bar\sigma(r)),
\]
\[
\mu_{\rm num}(r)
=
m(\bar\sigma(r))
-
3\chi_X(r)\,u_X(\bar\sigma(r)),
\]
and
\[
a(r)=\frac{g_R(r)}{z_0(\bar\sigma(r))},
\qquad
b(r)=\frac{g_E(r)}{z_0(\bar\sigma(r))},
\qquad
\mu(r)=\frac{\mu_{\rm num}(r)}{z_0(\bar\sigma(r))},
\]
where
\[
g_R(r)=g_E(r)+g_c(r).
\]

Thus
\[
\boxed{
a(r)
=
\frac{
v_\perp(\bar\sigma(r))+v_c(\bar\sigma(r))
+
3\chi_X(r)\bigl(v_E^{(X)}(\bar\sigma(r))+v_c^{(X)}(\bar\sigma(r))\bigr)
}{
z_0(\bar\sigma(r))
},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
b(r)
=
\frac{
v_\perp(\bar\sigma(r))
+
3\chi_X(r)\,v_E^{(X)}(\bar\sigma(r))
}{
z_0(\bar\sigma(r))
},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\mu(r)
=
\frac{
m(\bar\sigma(r))
-
3\chi_X(r)\,u_X(\bar\sigma(r))
}{
z_0(\bar\sigma(r))
}.
}
\]

\section{Core and bulk coefficients}

By smoothness of the profiles and constitutive functions, the core limits exist:
\[
\boxed{
a_0:=\lim_{r\to0}a(r),
\qquad
b_0:=\lim_{r\to0}b(r),
\qquad
\mu_0:=\lim_{r\to0}\mu(r),
}
\]
with
\[
a_0
=
\frac{
v_\perp(\sigma_0)+v_c(\sigma_0)
+
3X_0\bigl(v_E^{(X)}(\sigma_0)+v_c^{(X)}(\sigma_0)\bigr)
}{
z_0(\sigma_0)
},
\]
\[
b_0
=
\frac{
v_\perp(\sigma_0)+3X_0\,v_E^{(X)}(\sigma_0)
}{
z_0(\sigma_0)
},
\]
\[
\mu_0
=
\frac{
m(\sigma_0)-3X_0\,u_X(\sigma_0)
}{
z_0(\sigma_0)
}.
\]

Likewise, the bulk limits exist:
\[
\boxed{
a_\infty:=\lim_{r\to\infty}a(r),
\qquad
b_\infty:=\lim_{r\to\infty}b(r),
\qquad
\mu_\infty:=\lim_{r\to\infty}\mu(r),
}
\]
with
\[
a_\infty
=
\frac{
v_\perp(\sigma_\infty)+v_c(\sigma_\infty)
+
3\chi_\infty\bigl(v_E^{(X)}(\sigma_\infty)+v_c^{(X)}(\sigma_\infty)\bigr)
}{
z_0(\sigma_\infty)
},
\]
\[
b_\infty
=
\frac{
v_\perp(\sigma_\infty)+3\chi_\infty v_E^{(X)}(\sigma_\infty)
}{
z_0(\sigma_\infty)
},
\]
\[
\mu_\infty
=
\frac{
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)
}{
z_0(\sigma_\infty)
}.
\]

In the simplest vacuum branch \(\chi_\infty=0\), these reduce to
\[
a_\infty=\frac{v_\perp(\sigma_\infty)+v_c(\sigma_\infty)}{z_0(\sigma_\infty)},
\qquad
b_\infty=\frac{v_\perp(\sigma_\infty)}{z_0(\sigma_\infty)},
\qquad
\mu_\infty=\frac{m(\sigma_\infty)}{z_0(\sigma_\infty)}.
\]

\section{Near-core and bulk asymptotics of the superpotential}

For a projected angular channel \(\kappa\), the Callias-core superpotential is
\[
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)=\mu(r)+\frac{\kappa\,b(r)}{r}.
\]

Near the core,
\[
a(r)=a_0+O(r^2),
\qquad
b(r)=b_0+O(r^2),
\qquad
\mu(r)=\mu_0+O(r^2),
\]
so
\[
\boxed{
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)
=
\mu_0+\frac{\kappa b_0}{r}+O(r).
}
\]
Thus the \(1/r\) term dominates, and its sign is governed entirely by \(\kappa b_0\).

At large radius,
\[
a(r)=a_\infty+o(1),
\qquad
b(r)=b_\infty+o(1),
\qquad
\mu(r)=\mu_\infty+o(1),
\]
hence
\[
\boxed{
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)
=
\mu_\infty+\frac{\kappa b_\infty}{r}+o(1).
}
\]
Therefore
\[
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)\to \mu_\infty
\qquad (r\to\infty).
\]

\section{Profile-level sufficient inequalities}

We now formulate a directly checkable sufficient criterion.

\paragraph{Assumption S1 (positive bulk gap).}
\[
\boxed{
\mu_\infty>0.
}
\]

\paragraph{Assumption S2 (positive radial velocity).}
\[
\boxed{
a_0>0,\qquad a_\infty>0.
}
\]

\paragraph{Assumption S3 (positive core angular coefficient).}
\[
\boxed{
b_0>0.
}
\]

\paragraph{Assumption S4 (unique projected signed lowest channel).}
After the remote-gap and projector reduction, the admissible low-slot channel set contains a unique signed lowest candidate
\[
\boxed{
\kappa_*<0,
}
\]
with multiplicity one.
All competing projected channels are either excluded by the remote-gap theorem or satisfy
\[
\kappa\ge \kappa_{\rm comp}>0.
\]

\paragraph{Assumption S5 (core regularity margin for the protected channel).}
There exists \(\varepsilon_*>0\) such that
\[
\boxed{
\frac{|\kappa_*|\,b_0}{a_0}\ge \frac12+\varepsilon_*.
}
\]

\paragraph{Assumption S6 (core exclusion margin for competing channels).}
For every competing projected channel \(\kappa\neq\kappa_*\),
\[
\boxed{
\frac{\kappa\,b_0}{a_0}\ge \frac12+\varepsilon_\kappa
}
\]
for some \(\varepsilon_\kappa>0\).

\section{Main profile theorem}

\paragraph{Theorem (working one-defect/one-mode sufficient criterion).}
Assume S1--S6.
Then the projected lowest channel \(\kappa_*\) carries exactly one \(L^2\)-normalizable chiral zero-mode generator, while all competing projected channels carry none.
Consequently,
\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{Ind}(\mathbb H_{\rm C})=1,
}
\]
and the defect carries exactly one protected light mode.

\paragraph{Proof.}
Because \(\mu_\infty>0\), the large-\(r\) asymptotic generator
\[
u_{\kappa,+}(r)
=
\exp\!\left(
-\int^r \frac{W_\kappa^{\rm core}(s)}{a(s)}\,ds
\right)
\]
is the unique decaying branch for every channel, while
\[
u_{\kappa,-}(r)
=
\exp\!\left(
+\int^r \frac{W_\kappa^{\rm core}(s)}{a(s)}\,ds
\right)
\]
is never \(L^2\)-normalizable at infinity.

For the protected channel \(\kappa_*\), near the core
\[
W_{\kappa_*}^{\rm core}(r)
=
\mu_0-\frac{|\kappa_*|b_0}{r}+O(r).
\]
Since the \(1/r\) term dominates, S5 implies that for sufficiently small \(r\),
\[
W_{\kappa_*}^{\rm core}(r)
\le
-\left(\frac12+\frac{\varepsilon_*}{2}\right)\frac{a(r)}{r}.
\]
Thus the decaying branch behaves like
\[
u_{\kappa_*,+}(r)\lesssim r^{1/2+\varepsilon_*/2},
\]
and is \(L^2\)-regular near the origin.
Combined with large-\(r\) decay, this gives
\[
\dim\ker Q_{\kappa_*,+}^{\rm core}=1,
\qquad
\dim\ker Q_{\kappa_*,-}^{\rm core}=0.
\]

For a competing channel \(\kappa\neq\kappa_*\), S6 implies that near the core
\[
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)
\ge
\left(\frac12+\frac{\varepsilon_\kappa}{2}\right)\frac{a(r)}{r},
\]
so
\[
u_{\kappa,+}(r)\gtrsim r^{-(1/2+\varepsilon_\kappa/2)},
\]
which is not \(L^2\)-regular at the origin.
Since \(u_{\kappa,-}\) is already excluded at infinity, no competing channel contributes.

Hence exactly one projected channel contributes one protected chiral generator, and
\[
\operatorname{Ind}(\mathbb H_{\rm C})=1.
\]
\(\square\)

\section{Practical monotone-profile corollary}

The theorem above can be rewritten in a more physical form.

\paragraph{Corollary (monotone working-profile version).}
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(\bar\sigma(r)\) is monotone increasing from \(\sigma_0\) to \(\sigma_\infty\);
\item \(X_\perp(r)\) and \(X_\parallel(r)\) are monotone decreasing from \(X_0\) to their bulk limits;
\item \(z_0(\sigma)>0\), \(v_\perp(\sigma)>0\), and \(v_\perp(\sigma)+v_c(\sigma)>0\);
\item the constitutive combination \(m(\sigma)-3\chi_X u_X(\sigma)\) tends to a strictly positive bulk value;
\item the projected low-slot contains a unique signed lowest channel \(\kappa_*<0\).
\end{enumerate}

If, in addition, the core ratios satisfy
\[
\frac{|\kappa_*|\,b_0}{a_0}>\frac12,
\qquad
\frac{\kappa\,b_0}{a_0}>\frac12
\quad
\text{for all projected competitors }\kappa>0,
\]
then the defect carries exactly one protected light mode.

\paragraph{Comment.}
This is the form most useful for an actual TECT profile check.
Everything is reduced to the core constants
\[
a_0,\qquad b_0,
\]
the bulk mass parameter
\[
\mu_\infty,
\]
and the projected channel structure.

\section{Role of the odd tangential profile \(g_O(r)\)}

The odd tangential profile enters the full radial generator as a phase factor only:
\[
u_{\kappa,+}^{\rm full}(r)
=
u_{\kappa,+}^{\rm core}(r)
\exp\!\left(
-i\kappa\int^r \frac{c(s)}{a(s)s}\,ds
\right).
\]
Therefore
\[
\boxed{
|u_{\kappa,+}^{\rm full}(r)|=|u_{\kappa,+}^{\rm core}(r)|.
}
\]
So \(g_O(r)\) does not alter the protected-channel counting.
It only changes the phase profile of the wavefunction.

\section{What is now actually reduced to explicit verification}

The one-defect/one-mode statement is now reduced to verifying the following concrete TECT data:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the core constants \(a_0,b_0\);
\item the bulk gap \(\mu_\infty>0\);
\item the projected admissible low-slot channel structure;
\item the remote-gap isolation of all higher sectors.
\end{enumerate}

These are now profile-check problems rather than structural unknowns.

\section{Final summary}

Using the working radial defect ansatz
\[
\bar\sigma(r),\qquad X_\perp(r),\qquad X_\parallel(r),
\]
the Callias-core coefficients are
\[
a(r)=\frac{g_R(r)}{z_0(\bar\sigma(r))},
\qquad
b(r)=\frac{g_E(r)}{z_0(\bar\sigma(r))},
\qquad
\mu(r)=\frac{m(\bar\sigma(r))-3\chi_X(r)u_X(\bar\sigma(r))}{z_0(\bar\sigma(r))},
\]
with
\[
\chi_X(r)=\frac13\bigl(2X_\perp(r)+X_\parallel(r)\bigr).
\]

Their core and bulk limits are
\[
a_0,\quad b_0,\quad \mu_0,
\qquad
a_\infty,\quad b_\infty,\quad \mu_\infty.
\]

For the projected lowest channel \(\kappa_*\), the real superpotential is
\[
W_*(r)=\mu(r)+\frac{\kappa_* b(r)}{r}.
\]

A sufficient one-defect/one-mode criterion is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(\mu_\infty>0\) (bulk gap);
\item \(a_0>0\) and \(b_0>0\);
\item after projector reduction there is a unique signed lowest channel \(\kappa_*<0\) of multiplicity one;
\item
\[
\frac{|\kappa_*|\,b_0}{a_0}>\frac12;
\]
\item every competing projected channel satisfies
\[
\frac{\kappa\,b_0}{a_0}>\frac12.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Under these conditions, exactly one chiral generator is \(L^2\)-normalizable, all competing channels are excluded, and
\[
\operatorname{Ind}(\mathbb H_{\rm C})=1.
\]

Thus the one-defect/one-mode problem has been reduced to explicit verification of the core coefficients, the bulk gap, the projected channel structure, and the remote-gap isolation.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Final unified chain: remote-gap isolation + Bloch extraction + radial one-mode criterion}

We now combine the three previously separate modules into a single working sufficient criterion for
\[
\text{one defect } \leftrightarrow \text{ one protected light mode.}
\]

The three modules are:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the remote-gap isolation theorem;
\item the Bloch/valley/Class II coefficient extraction of \((g_c,g_E,g_O)\);
\item the radial Callias-core one-channel criterion.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Microscopic transport triplet and its two projections}

From the locked BCC/Class II coefficient extraction, the reduced valley transport coefficients are defined by
\[
\lambda_\parallel=C_c\,g_c,
\qquad
\alpha=C_E\,g_E,
\qquad
\beta=C_O\,g_O,
\]
with
\[
g_c=\frac{\lambda_\parallel}{C_c},
\qquad
g_E=\frac{\alpha}{C_E},
\qquad
g_O=\frac{\beta}{C_O}.
\]

These are the valley-projected transport coefficients.

From the radial single-defect constitutive ansatz, the corresponding core transport coefficients are
\[
g_E^{\rm core}:=g_E^{\rm eff}(0),
\qquad
g_c^{\rm core}:=g_c^{\rm eff}(0),
\qquad
g_O^{\rm core}:=g_O^{\rm eff}(0),
\]
and the bulk mass coefficient is
\[
\mu_\infty
=
\lim_{r\to\infty}
\frac{
m(\bar\sigma(r))-3\chi_X(r)u_X(\bar\sigma(r))
}{
z_0(\bar\sigma(r))
}.
\]

To connect the two descriptions, we introduce the minimal local-to-valley matching hypothesis:

\paragraph{Matching hypothesis.}
There exist positive constants
\[
\xi_E>0,\qquad \xi_c>0,\qquad \xi_O>0
\]
such that
\[
\boxed{
g_E^{\rm core}=\xi_E\,g_E,
\qquad
g_c^{\rm core}=\xi_c\,g_c,
\qquad
g_O^{\rm core}=\xi_O\,g_O.
}
\]

In the strict local-core matching approximation one has simply
\[
\xi_E=\xi_c=\xi_O=1,
\]
but the theorem below does not require this stronger specialization.

\section{Core/bulk coefficients entering the radial criterion}

Recall that the radial Callias-core coefficients are
\[
a(r)=\frac{g_R(r)}{z_0(r)},
\qquad
b(r)=\frac{g_E(r)}{z_0(r)},
\qquad
\mu(r)=\frac{m_{\rm eff}(r)}{z_0(r)},
\qquad
g_R(r)=g_E(r)+g_c(r).
\]

At the core,
\[
a_0=\frac{g_E^{\rm core}+g_c^{\rm core}}{z_{0,0}},
\qquad
b_0=\frac{g_E^{\rm core}}{z_{0,0}},
\qquad
c_0=\frac{g_O^{\rm core}}{z_{0,0}},
\]
where
\[
z_{0,0}:=z_0(\sigma_0)>0.
\]

Under the matching hypothesis, this becomes
\[
\boxed{
a_0=\frac{\xi_E g_E+\xi_c g_c}{z_{0,0}},
\qquad
b_0=\frac{\xi_E g_E}{z_{0,0}},
\qquad
c_0=\frac{\xi_O g_O}{z_{0,0}}.
}
\]

At infinity,
\[
\boxed{
\mu_\infty
=
\frac{
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)
}{
z_0(\sigma_\infty)
}.
}
\]
In the simplest vacuum branch \(\chi_\infty=0\),
\[
\boxed{
\mu_\infty=\frac{m(\sigma_\infty)}{z_0(\sigma_\infty)}.
}
\]

\section{Remote-gap isolation and reduction to the lowest projected channel}

Let \(\mathbb H_{\rm full}\) be the full single-defect fluctuation operator decomposed into
\[
\mathbb H_{\rm full}
=
\mathbb H_{\rm low}\oplus \mathbb H_{\rm rem}
+\text{off-diagonal couplings}.
\]

Assume the previously established full remote-gap condition:
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\]
Then the remote-gap theorem implies
\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{spec}(\mathbb H_{\rm rem})
\cap
(-\Delta_{\rm rem},\Delta_{\rm rem})
=
\varnothing
}
\]
for some \(\Delta_{\rm rem}>0\).
Therefore any protected zero or near-zero mode must lie in the projected low slot.

We assume that after this low-slot projection there remains a unique signed lowest admissible channel
\[
\boxed{
\kappa_*<0
}
\]
of multiplicity one.

\section{Radial one-mode inequalities in terms of }(g_c,g_E,g_O)

For the lowest projected channel, the real Callias-core superpotential is
\[
W_*(r)=\mu(r)+\frac{\kappa_* b(r)}{r}.
\]
The protected-channel criterion obtained earlier requires:

\begin{enumerate}
\item bulk positivity:
\[
\mu_\infty>0;
\]

\item positive radial velocity:
\[
a_0>0;
\]

\item positive core angular coefficient:
\[
b_0>0;
\]

\item lowest-channel core regularity:
\[
\frac{|\kappa_*|\,b_0}{a_0}>\frac12;
\]

\item competitor exclusion:
for every surviving projected competitor \(\kappa\neq \kappa_*\),
\[
\frac{\kappa\,b_0}{a_0}>\frac12.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Substituting the matching formulas for \(a_0,b_0\), these become

\[
\boxed{
\xi_E g_E+\xi_c g_c>0,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\xi_E g_E>0,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\mu_\infty>0,
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
2|\kappa_*|\,\xi_E g_E
>
\xi_E g_E+\xi_c g_c.
}
\]

Similarly, every projected competitor \(\kappa\neq \kappa_*\) is excluded if
\[
\boxed{
2\kappa\,\xi_E g_E
>
\xi_E g_E+\xi_c g_c.
}
\]

Thus the radial one-mode criterion has been translated entirely into inequalities on the extracted transport coefficients together with the bulk mass parameter.

\section{Main unified theorem}

\paragraph{Theorem (final working one-defect/one-mode sufficient criterion).}
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the full remote-gap condition holds:
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho};
\]

\item after remote-gap reduction and low-slot projection, there is a unique signed lowest admissible channel \(\kappa_*<0\) of multiplicity one;

\item the extracted Bloch/valley coefficients \((g_c,g_E,g_O)\) satisfy the matching hypothesis with positive constants \((\xi_c,\xi_E,\xi_O)\);

\item the bulk mass parameter satisfies
\[
\mu_\infty>0;
\]

\item the core transport coefficients satisfy
\[
\xi_E g_E+\xi_c g_c>0,
\qquad
\xi_E g_E>0,
\]
and
\[
2|\kappa_*|\,\xi_E g_E
>
\xi_E g_E+\xi_c g_c;
\]

\item every competing projected channel \(\kappa\neq\kappa_*\) satisfies
\[
2\kappa\,\xi_E g_E
>
\xi_E g_E+\xi_c g_c.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Then the full defect operator carries exactly one protected light mode:
\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{Ind}(\mathbb H_{\rm C})=1,
}
\]
and therefore
\[
\boxed{
\text{one defect } \leftrightarrow \text{ one protected light mode.}
}
\]

\paragraph{Proof.}
By the remote-gap theorem, all remote sectors are uniformly excluded from the zero-energy window, so the protected-mode problem reduces to the low projected slot.

In that slot, the radial Callias-core criterion applies with
\[
a_0=\frac{\xi_E g_E+\xi_c g_c}{z_{0,0}},
\qquad
b_0=\frac{\xi_E g_E}{z_{0,0}},
\]
and \(z_{0,0}>0\).
Hence the assumptions
\[
\xi_E g_E+\xi_c g_c>0,
\qquad
\xi_E g_E>0
\]
imply
\[
a_0>0,
\qquad
b_0>0.
\]

The lowest-channel inequality
\[
2|\kappa_*|\,\xi_E g_E>\xi_E g_E+\xi_c g_c
\]
is equivalent to
\[
\frac{|\kappa_*|\,b_0}{a_0}>\frac12,
\]
so the decaying chiral generator in the \(\kappa_*\)-channel is \(L^2\)-regular at the core.

The bulk positivity \(\mu_\infty>0\) guarantees that the same generator decays at infinity, while the opposite chiral generator is excluded.

For every competitor \(\kappa\neq\kappa_*\), the inequality
\[
2\kappa\,\xi_E g_E>\xi_E g_E+\xi_c g_c
\]
is equivalent to
\[
\frac{\kappa\,b_0}{a_0}>\frac12,
\]
which excludes the decaying generator at the core.

Thus exactly one projected channel contributes one normalizable chiral generator.
Since the remote sectors are spectrally isolated, the total defect index is
\[
\operatorname{Ind}(\mathbb H_{\rm C})=1.
\]
Therefore the defect carries exactly one protected light mode.
\(\square\)

\section{Role of the odd transport coefficient}

The coefficient \(g_O\) remains physically relevant in the full operator, but it does not enter the protected-mode counting.
Indeed, under the matching hypothesis,
\[
c_0=\frac{\xi_O g_O}{z_{0,0}},
\]
and the odd tangential term contributes only the channel-dependent phase
\[
\exp\!\left(
-i\kappa\int^r \frac{c(s)}{a(s)s}\,ds
\right)
\]
to the radial generator.
Thus
\[
\boxed{
g_O\text{ affects the phase profile of the mode, but not the }L^2\text{-normalizability criterion.}
}
\]

\section{Operational interpretation}

The theorem shows that the entire one-defect/one-mode problem is reduced to checking the following explicit data:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the remote-gap inequality
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho};
\]

\item the low-slot channel structure and uniqueness of the signed lowest channel \(\kappa_*\);

\item the signs and sizes of the extracted transport coefficients \(g_E,g_c\);

\item the bulk mass gap sign \(\mu_\infty>0\).
\end{enumerate}

In particular, the decisive low-core inequality is
\[
\boxed{
2|\kappa_*|\,\xi_E g_E>\xi_E g_E+\xi_c g_c.
}
\]
This is the concrete bridge between the Bloch/Class II transport extraction and the radial one-mode criterion.

\section{What is now actually closed}

The conceptual chain is now complete:

\[
\boxed{
\text{remote-gap theorem}
\Longrightarrow
\text{low-slot isolation}
\Longrightarrow
\text{radial projected channel problem}
\Longrightarrow
\text{one-defect/one-mode criterion in terms of }(g_c,g_E,\mu_\infty).
}
\]

What remains is no longer structural.
It is the actual verification of the inequalities and matching constants for the concrete TECT working branch.

\section{Final summary}

We unified the three previously separate modules:

\[
\text{remote-gap isolation},
\qquad
\text{Bloch/valley extraction of }(g_c,g_E,g_O),
\qquad
\text{radial Callias-core one-mode criterion.}
\]

The defect-core coefficients are
\[
a_0=\frac{\xi_E g_E+\xi_c g_c}{z_{0,0}},
\qquad
b_0=\frac{\xi_E g_E}{z_{0,0}},
\qquad
c_0=\frac{\xi_O g_O}{z_{0,0}},
\]
while the bulk mass parameter is
\[
\mu_\infty
=
\frac{
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)
}{
z_0(\sigma_\infty)
}.
\]

If:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the remote-gap condition
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
\]
holds;

\item the low-slot projection leaves a unique signed lowest channel \(\kappa_*<0\) of multiplicity one;

\item \(\mu_\infty>0\);

\item
\[
\xi_E g_E+\xi_c g_c>0,
\qquad
\xi_E g_E>0,
\]
and
\[
2|\kappa_*|\,\xi_E g_E>\xi_E g_E+\xi_c g_c;
\]

\item every competing projected channel satisfies
\[
2\kappa\,\xi_E g_E>\xi_E g_E+\xi_c g_c;
\]
\end{enumerate}

then
\[
\operatorname{Ind}(\mathbb H_{\rm C})=1,
\]
and therefore one defect carries exactly one protected light mode.

Moreover, \(g_O\) affects only the phase of the radial generator and does not alter the protected-mode counting.

Thus the remaining work is purely explicit verification:
evaluate the extracted coefficients and check the inequalities in the concrete TECT working branch.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Benchmark dictionary linking Bloch/Class II extraction to the radial one-mode criterion}

We now construct the practical benchmark dictionary that connects:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the Bloch/valley/Class II extracted coefficients
\[
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta),
\]

\item the radial Callias-core coefficients
\[
(a_0,b_0,c_0,\mu_\infty),
\]

\item the final one-defect/one-protected-mode sufficient criterion.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Exact valley extraction layer}

On the low valley doublet, the transport coefficients are extracted by
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3M_\parallel),
\qquad
\alpha=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_1M_1+\sigma_2M_2),
\qquad
\beta=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_2M_1-\sigma_1M_2).
\]

By definition of the overlap constants,
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=C_c\,g_c,
\qquad
\alpha=C_E\,g_E,
\qquad
\beta=C_O\,g_O,
}
\]
hence
\[
\boxed{
g_c=\frac{\lambda_\parallel}{C_c},
\qquad
g_E=\frac{\alpha}{C_E},
\qquad
g_O=\frac{\beta}{C_O}.
}
\]

This part is exact once \(C_c,C_E,C_O\) are fixed by the chosen Bloch/overlap convention.

\section{Exact radial core layer}

From the radial constitutive reduction, the core coefficients are
\[
a_0=\frac{g_E^{\rm core}+g_c^{\rm core}}{z_{0,0}},
\qquad
b_0=\frac{g_E^{\rm core}}{z_{0,0}},
\qquad
c_0=\frac{g_O^{\rm core}}{z_{0,0}},
\]
where
\[
z_{0,0}:=z_0(\sigma_0)>0.
\]

The bulk mass parameter is
\[
\boxed{
\mu_\infty
=
\frac{
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)
}{
z_0(\sigma_\infty)
}.
}
\]
In the simplest vacuum branch \(\chi_\infty=0\),
\[
\boxed{
\mu_\infty=\frac{m(\sigma_\infty)}{z_0(\sigma_\infty)}.
}
\]

\section{Matching hypothesis between valley and core transport data}

To connect the valley-extracted coefficients with the defect-core coefficients, introduce the matching constants
\[
\boxed{
g_E^{\rm core}=\xi_E\,g_E,
\qquad
g_c^{\rm core}=\xi_c\,g_c,
\qquad
g_O^{\rm core}=\xi_O\,g_O,
}
\]
with
\[
\xi_E>0,\qquad \xi_c>0,\qquad \xi_O>0.
\]

These constants encode the difference between the core-local projection and the valley/Bloch projection.
They are not yet a theorem of the branch; they are the remaining matching data to be computed explicitly.

Under this hypothesis,
\[
\boxed{
a_0
=
\frac{1}{z_{0,0}}
\left(
\xi_E\frac{\alpha}{C_E}
+
\xi_c\frac{\lambda_\parallel}{C_c}
\right),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
b_0
=
\frac{\xi_E}{z_{0,0}}\frac{\alpha}{C_E},
\qquad
c_0
=
\frac{\xi_O}{z_{0,0}}\frac{\beta}{C_O}.
}
\]

\section{Dimensionless benchmark ratios}

Define the two dimensionless ratios
\[
\boxed{
R_c
:=
\frac{\xi_c C_E}{\xi_E C_c}\,
\frac{\lambda_\parallel}{\alpha},
}
\qquad
\boxed{
R_O
:=
\frac{\xi_O C_E}{\xi_E C_O}\,
\frac{\beta}{\alpha},
}
\]
whenever \(\alpha\neq 0\).

Then the core coefficients simplify to
\[
\boxed{
a_0=b_0(1+R_c),
\qquad
c_0=b_0 R_O.
}
\]

Equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
\frac{a_0}{b_0}=1+R_c,
\qquad
\frac{c_0}{b_0}=R_O.
}
\]

This is the cleanest practical dictionary.
The parameter \(R_c\) controls the relative strength of the radial/longitudinal channel compared with the even tangential channel, while \(R_O\) controls the odd/torsion-like phase channel.

\section{Radial one-mode criterion in dictionary form}

For the projected lowest channel \(\kappa_*\), the real Callias-core superpotential is
\[
W_*(r)=\mu(r)+\frac{\kappa_* b(r)}{r}.
\]

The previously derived sufficient criterion requires:

\begin{enumerate}
\item remote-gap isolation:
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho};
\]

\item a unique signed lowest projected channel \(\kappa_*<0\) of multiplicity one;

\item bulk positivity:
\[
\mu_\infty>0;
\]

\item positive core transport coefficients:
\[
a_0>0,\qquad b_0>0;
\]

\item lowest-channel regularity:
\[
\frac{|\kappa_*|\,b_0}{a_0}>\frac12;
\]

\item competitor exclusion:
for all projected competitors \(\kappa\neq\kappa_*\),
\[
\frac{\kappa\,b_0}{a_0}>\frac12.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Using
\[
a_0=b_0(1+R_c),
\]
this becomes

\[
\boxed{
\mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
b_0>0,
\qquad
1+R_c>0,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
2|\kappa_*|>1+R_c,
}
\]
and for every competitor,
\[
\boxed{
2\kappa>1+R_c.
}
\]

Since
\[
b_0=\frac{\xi_E}{z_{0,0}}\frac{\alpha}{C_E},
\]
the sign condition \(b_0>0\) is equivalent to
\[
\boxed{
\frac{\xi_E}{C_E}\alpha>0.
}
\]
Under the standard convention \(C_E>0\) and \(\xi_E>0\), this reduces simply to
\[
\boxed{
\alpha>0.
}
\]

Thus the one-mode criterion is controlled entirely by

\[
\boxed{
\mu_\infty,\qquad \alpha,\qquad R_c,\qquad \kappa_*.
}
\]

\section{Most practical lowest-channel specialization}

The practically most relevant case is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the projected lowest signed channel is
\[
\boxed{
\kappa_*=-1;
}
\]

\item all other surviving projected competitors satisfy
\[
\kappa\ge 1.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Then the inequalities reduce to
\[
\boxed{
-1<R_c<1,
}
\]
together with
\[
\boxed{
\alpha>0,
\qquad
\mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\]

Indeed:
\[
1+R_c>0 \iff R_c>-1,
\]
and
\[
2|\kappa_*|>1+R_c
\quad\text{with}\quad |\kappa_*|=1
\iff
2>1+R_c
\iff
R_c<1.
\]

Hence the simplest operational criterion is precisely
\[
\boxed{
-1<R_c<1,\qquad \alpha>0,\qquad \mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\]

\section{Role of \(\beta\) and \(R_O\)}

The odd transport coefficient enters through
\[
R_O=\frac{\xi_O C_E}{\xi_E C_O}\frac{\beta}{\alpha},
\]
but, as shown previously, it contributes only a phase to the radial zero-mode generator.
Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
R_O\ \text{does not enter the protected-channel counting inequalities.}
}
\]

It is still physically meaningful, because it controls the phase/torsion-like structure of the wavefunction and will matter for finer transport and chirality diagnostics, but not for the one-mode index count itself.

\section{Exact versus conditional parts of the dictionary}

It is important to distinguish the exact parts from the still-conditional parts.

\paragraph{Exact.}
The following are exact within the working formalism:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the extraction of \((\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)\) from the projected Pauli traces;
\item the definitions
\[
g_c=\lambda_\parallel/C_c,\quad
g_E=\alpha/C_E,\quad
g_O=\beta/C_O;
\]
\item the core formulas
\[
a_0=\frac{g_E^{\rm core}+g_c^{\rm core}}{z_{0,0}},
\qquad
b_0=\frac{g_E^{\rm core}}{z_{0,0}},
\qquad
c_0=\frac{g_O^{\rm core}}{z_{0,0}};
\]
\item the radial one-mode inequalities once \(a_0,b_0,\mu_\infty,\kappa_*\) are known.
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{Conditional / branch-specific.}
The following remain to be verified in the actual branch:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the matching constants \(\xi_E,\xi_c,\xi_O\);
\item the unique signed lowest projected channel \(\kappa_*<0\);
\item the remote-gap inequality in the same parameter regime;
\item the sign of \(\mu_\infty\).
\end{enumerate}

Thus the dictionary is structurally complete, but still requires explicit branch evaluation of a small number of matching and spectral data.

\section{Final working theorem}

\paragraph{Theorem (practical working one-defect/one-mode criterion).}
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the remote-gap inequality holds:
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho};
\]

\item the projected low slot contains a unique signed lowest channel \(\kappa_*<0\) of multiplicity one;

\item the matching hypothesis with positive \(\xi_E,\xi_c,\xi_O\) holds;

\item \(\mu_\infty>0\);

\item
\[
\frac{\xi_E}{C_E}\alpha>0,
\qquad
1+R_c>0,
\qquad
2|\kappa_*|>1+R_c;
\]

\item every competing projected channel satisfies
\[
2\kappa>1+R_c.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Then
\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{Ind}(\mathbb H_{\rm C})=1,
}
\]
and therefore
\[
\boxed{
\text{one defect } \leftrightarrow \text{ one protected light mode.}
}
\]

In the practically important case
\[
\kappa_*=-1,\qquad \kappa_{\rm comp}\ge 1,
\]
this reduces to the compact criterion
\[
\boxed{
-1<R_c<1,\qquad \alpha>0,\qquad \mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\]

\section{Final summary}

We constructed the practical benchmark dictionary connecting the Bloch/Class II coefficients
\[
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)
\]
to the radial one-mode coefficients
\[
(a_0,b_0,c_0,\mu_\infty).
\]

The exact valley extraction is
\[
\lambda_\parallel=C_c g_c,\qquad
\alpha=C_E g_E,\qquad
\beta=C_O g_O.
\]

The exact core formulas are
\[
a_0=\frac{g_E^{\rm core}+g_c^{\rm core}}{z_{0,0}},
\qquad
b_0=\frac{g_E^{\rm core}}{z_{0,0}},
\qquad
c_0=\frac{g_O^{\rm core}}{z_{0,0}}.
\]

Under the matching hypothesis
\[
g_E^{\rm core}=\xi_E g_E,\qquad
g_c^{\rm core}=\xi_c g_c,\qquad
g_O^{\rm core}=\xi_O g_O,
\]
this becomes
\[
a_0
=
\frac{1}{z_{0,0}}
\left(
\xi_E\frac{\alpha}{C_E}
+
\xi_c\frac{\lambda_\parallel}{C_c}
\right),
\qquad
b_0
=
\frac{\xi_E}{z_{0,0}}\frac{\alpha}{C_E},
\qquad
c_0
=
\frac{\xi_O}{z_{0,0}}\frac{\beta}{C_O}.
\]

Defining
\[
R_c:=\frac{\xi_c C_E}{\xi_E C_c}\frac{\lambda_\parallel}{\alpha},
\qquad
R_O:=\frac{\xi_O C_E}{\xi_E C_O}\frac{\beta}{\alpha},
\]
one gets
\[
a_0=b_0(1+R_c),
\qquad
c_0=b_0 R_O.
\]

Hence the one-mode criterion is controlled by
\[
\mu_\infty,\qquad \alpha,\qquad R_c,\qquad \kappa_*,
\]
while \(R_O\) affects only the phase profile and not the protected-mode counting.

In the practically most relevant case
\[
\kappa_*=-1,\qquad \kappa_{\rm comp}\ge 1,
\]
the working sufficient criterion reduces to
\[
\boxed{
-1<R_c<1,\qquad \alpha>0,\qquad \mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\]

This is the cleanest operational form of the full chain:
remote-gap isolation, Bloch/Class II transport extraction, and radial one-defect/one-mode protection are now expressed in a single set of inequalities.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Practical calculation checklist for the refined locked + Class II working branch}

We now convert the final unified theorem into an explicit calculation protocol.
The goal is to determine the data
\[
C_c,\ C_E,\ C_O,\qquad
\xi_c,\ \xi_E,\ \xi_O,\qquad
\kappa_*,\qquad
\mu_\infty,
\]
and then verify the working sufficient criterion for
\[
\text{one defect } \leftrightarrow \text{ one protected light mode.}
\]

\section{Step 0: fix conventions once and for all}

Before any extraction, one must fix:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the normalization of the low-valley Pauli basis \(\{\sigma_1,\sigma_2,\sigma_3\}\);
\item the normalization of the radial core basis and the core coefficient convention \(z_{0,0}>0\);
\item the sign convention for the lowest signed projected channel \(\kappa_*\);
\item the overlap normalization convention used to define \(C_c,C_E,C_O\).
\end{enumerate}

Without these conventions, sign comparisons between Bloch-extracted and radial coefficients are ambiguous.
Once the convention is fixed, all quantities below are unambiguously defined.

\section{Step 1: remote-gap validation}

Compute the explicit benchmark lower bound
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}
\]
and the full residual mixing budget
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
\]

Then verify
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\]

If this inequality fails, the low slot is not spectrally isolated, and the one-mode criterion cannot yet be applied.
If it holds, then all higher angular/remote sectors are uniformly excluded from the zero-energy window.

This is the mandatory first gate.

\section{Step 2: low-valley extraction of }(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)

On the locked BCC/Class II branch, compute:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the Bloch fiber operator \(H_{\rm eff}(k)\);
\item the shell projection \(H_{\rm shell}(p)\);
\item the exact low-valley Riesz projector
\[
P_*=\frac{1}{2\pi i}\oint_\Gamma (z-H_{\rm shell}(0))^{-1}dz;
\]
\item the transport matrices
\[
M_i=P_*\left.\partial_{k_i}H_{\rm eff}(k)\right|_{k=k_*}P_*.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Then, in the adapted defect frame \((\hat n,e_1,e_2)\), define
\[
M_\parallel=\hat n_i M_i,
\qquad
M_1=e_{1i}M_i,
\qquad
M_2=e_{2i}M_i.
\]

Assuming the locked Pauli selection rule has been established, extract
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3M_\parallel),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\alpha=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_1M_1+\sigma_2M_2),
\qquad
\beta=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_2M_1-\sigma_1M_2).
}
\]

This produces the Bloch/valley transport triplet.

\section{Step 3: determination of }C_c,C_E,C_O

The overlap constants
\[
C_c,\qquad C_E,\qquad C_O
\]
must be fixed in the same convention as the valley extraction.

The cleanest practical protocol is the calibration protocol:

\paragraph{Calibration run C.}
Impose a constitutive deformation such that, in the low-energy transport sector, only the \(c\)-type channel is switched on with unit normalization, while the \(E\)- and \(O\)-type channels are off.
Then compute the extracted \(\lambda_\parallel\).
Set
\[
\boxed{
C_c:=\lambda_\parallel^{(c\text{-unit})}.
}
\]

\paragraph{Calibration run E.}
Impose a constitutive deformation such that only the even tangential channel is switched on with unit normalization.
Then compute the extracted \(\alpha\).
Set
\[
\boxed{
C_E:=\alpha^{(E\text{-unit})}.
}
\]

\paragraph{Calibration run O.}
Impose a constitutive deformation such that only the odd tangential channel is switched on with unit normalization.
Then compute the extracted \(\beta\).
Set
\[
\boxed{
C_O:=\beta^{(O\text{-unit})}.
}
\]

This protocol is exact within the chosen normalization convention.
After it is completed, define
\[
\boxed{
g_c=\frac{\lambda_\parallel}{C_c},
\qquad
g_E=\frac{\alpha}{C_E},
\qquad
g_O=\frac{\beta}{C_O}.
}
\]

\section{Step 4: determination of }a_0,b_0,c_0,\mu_\infty\text{ from the radial constitutive profile}

From the radial constitutive reduction,
\[
a_0=\frac{g_E^{\rm core}+g_c^{\rm core}}{z_{0,0}},
\qquad
b_0=\frac{g_E^{\rm core}}{z_{0,0}},
\qquad
c_0=\frac{g_O^{\rm core}}{z_{0,0}}.
\]

Also,
\[
\boxed{
\mu_\infty
=
\frac{
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)
}{
z_0(\sigma_\infty)
}.
}
\]

So one must compute:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the core value \(\sigma_0=\bar\sigma(0)\);
\item the core mediator contraction \(\chi_X(0)\);
\item the bulk values \(\sigma_\infty,\chi_\infty\);
\item the constitutive functions \(z_0,m,u_X\) evaluated at these core/bulk values.
\end{enumerate}

This produces the radial core/bulk data
\[
a_0,\qquad b_0,\qquad c_0,\qquad \mu_\infty.
\]

\section{Step 5: determination of }\xi_E,\xi_c,\xi_O

The matching constants are defined by
\[
g_E^{\rm core}=\xi_E g_E,
\qquad
g_c^{\rm core}=\xi_c g_c,
\qquad
g_O^{\rm core}=\xi_O g_O.
\]

The clean practical protocol is again calibration-based.

\paragraph{Core/valley matching run E.}
Use the same \(E\)-unit calibration as in Step 3, compute both:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the valley-extracted \(g_E\);
\item the radial core coefficient \(g_E^{\rm core}\).
\end{enumerate}

Then set
\[
\boxed{
\xi_E:=\frac{g_E^{\rm core}}{g_E}.
}
\]

Similarly,
\[
\boxed{
\xi_c:=\frac{g_c^{\rm core}}{g_c},
\qquad
\xi_O:=\frac{g_O^{\rm core}}{g_O}.
}
\]

This is the cleanest way to determine the matching constants without making any uncontrolled identification between local-core data and Bloch-projected data.

\section{Step 6: determination of the projected lowest signed channel }\kappa_*

Now determine the projected admissible angular channel set after:

\begin{enumerate}
\item remote-gap elimination of higher sectors;
\item internal/projector restriction to the low slot;
\item grading-compatible angular decomposition.
\end{enumerate}

Operationally, one computes the spectrum and multiplicities of the projected angular operator
\[
\mathcal D_{S^2}^{\rm proj}
\]
in the low slot and records the surviving signed channels
\[
\mathfrak K_{\rm adm}^{\rm low}.
\]

Then identify whether there exists a unique signed lowest channel
\[
\boxed{
\kappa_*<0
}
\]
of multiplicity one.

If such a unique channel does not exist, the compact one-mode criterion cannot yet be applied.
This is the second mandatory gate.

\section{Step 7: construct the benchmark ratios}

Once the previous steps are completed, define
\[
\boxed{
R_c
:=
\frac{\xi_c C_E}{\xi_E C_c}\frac{\lambda_\parallel}{\alpha},
\qquad
R_O
:=
\frac{\xi_O C_E}{\xi_E C_O}\frac{\beta}{\alpha},
}
\]
provided \(\alpha\neq 0\).

Then
\[
\boxed{
a_0=b_0(1+R_c),
\qquad
c_0=b_0 R_O.
}
\]

Thus the decisive radial one-mode inequalities can be written entirely in terms of
\[
R_c,\qquad \alpha,\qquad \mu_\infty,\qquad \kappa_*.
\]

\section{Step 8: final inequality check}

The final working sufficient criterion is:

\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\mu_\infty>0,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\frac{\xi_E}{C_E}\alpha>0,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
1+R_c>0,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
2|\kappa_*|>1+R_c,
}
\]
and for every projected competitor \(\kappa\neq\kappa_*\),
\[
\boxed{
2\kappa>1+R_c.
}
\]

In the practically most relevant case
\[
\kappa_*=-1,
\qquad
\kappa_{\rm comp}\ge 1,
\]
this reduces to
\[
\boxed{
-1<R_c<1,
\qquad
\alpha>0,
\qquad
\mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho},
}
\]
assuming the standard sign convention \(C_E>0,\ \xi_E>0\).

\section{Optional Step 9: direct radial shooting validation}

Even after the sufficient inequalities are verified, the most convincing final diagnostic is a direct radial ODE check in the projected lowest channel.

Using
\[
Q_{\kappa_*,\pm}^{\rm core}
=
\pm a(r)\frac{d}{dr}
+
W_{\kappa_*}^{\rm core}(r),
\qquad
W_{\kappa_*}^{\rm core}(r)=\mu(r)+\frac{\kappa_* b(r)}{r},
\]
one may numerically integrate the decaying generator and verify directly that:

\begin{enumerate}
\item it is \(L^2\)-regular at the core;
\item the opposite chiral generator is excluded;
\item no competing channel admits a normalizable branch.
\end{enumerate}

This does not replace the theorem, but it gives a strong numerical confirmation of the same conclusion.

\section{Exact versus conditional outputs of the protocol}

After the full checklist is completed, the outputs separate as follows.

\paragraph{Exact within the working branch.}
\begin{enumerate}
\item \(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta\);
\item \(C_c,C_E,C_O\) once the calibration convention is fixed;
\item \(g_c,g_E,g_O\);
\item \(a_0,b_0,c_0,\mu_\infty\);
\item \(R_c,R_O\).
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{Still branch-verified rather than abstractly guaranteed.}
\begin{enumerate}
\item \(\xi_c,\xi_E,\xi_O\);
\item the uniqueness and sign of \(\kappa_*\);
\item the positivity of \(\mu_\infty\);
\item the remote-gap inequality in the same parameter regime.
\end{enumerate}

Thus the remaining problem is no longer conceptual.
It is a finite explicit verification problem on the chosen working branch.

\section{Final summary}

The actual working calculation protocol is now fixed.

One must compute, in this order:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the remote-gap inequality
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho};
\]

\item the low-valley transport coefficients
\[
\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta;
\]

\item the overlap constants \(C_c,C_E,C_O\) by unit-channel calibration runs;

\item the radial core/bulk coefficients
\[
a_0,\ b_0,\ c_0,\ \mu_\infty;
\]

\item the matching constants
\[
\xi_c,\ \xi_E,\ \xi_O
\]
by core/valley calibration runs;

\item the projected signed lowest channel \(\kappa_*\);

\item the benchmark ratios
\[
R_c=\frac{\xi_c C_E}{\xi_E C_c}\frac{\lambda_\parallel}{\alpha},
\qquad
R_O=\frac{\xi_O C_E}{\xi_E C_O}\frac{\beta}{\alpha}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Then the final practical sufficient criterion is:

\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho},
\qquad
\mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
\frac{\xi_E}{C_E}\alpha>0,
\qquad
1+R_c>0,
\qquad
2|\kappa_*|>1+R_c,
\]
together with competitor exclusion
\[
2\kappa>1+R_c
\quad
(\kappa\neq\kappa_*).
\]

In the most practical case
\[
\kappa_*=-1,\qquad \kappa_{\rm comp}\ge 1,
\]
this reduces to
\[
\boxed{
-1<R_c<1,\qquad \alpha>0,\qquad \mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\]

Therefore the one-defect/one-mode problem has been reduced to a concrete finite checklist of computations on the refined locked + Class II working branch.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Audit table for the refined locked + Class II working branch}

\section{Purpose of the audit}

The current goal is not to introduce new abstract structure, but to classify every ingredient of the working one-defect/one-mode chain into exactly one of the following three statuses:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{Already available}: structurally derived or already established in the current working branch;
\item \textbf{Needs explicit computation}: not conceptually open, but still requires concrete evaluation from the branch data or code;
\item \textbf{Still an assumption / matching hypothesis}: not yet derived inside the branch, and must be treated honestly as an assumption until verified.
\end{enumerate}

The chain being audited is
\[
\boxed{
\text{remote-gap isolation}
\Longrightarrow
\text{low-slot projection}
\Longrightarrow
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)
\Longrightarrow
(g_c,g_E,g_O)
\Longrightarrow
(a_0,b_0,c_0,\mu_\infty)
\Longrightarrow
\text{radial one-mode criterion}.
}
\]

\section{I. Already available}

The following ingredients are already available in the current formalism.

\subsection{A. Reduced-operator and Schur-complement skeleton}

\begin{enumerate}
\item The light/heavy reduction
\[
\mathcal Y_{\rm eff}=L-KH^{-1}K^\dagger
\]
is already established.
