\item The explicit specialization to the refined locked + Class II working branch is already established:
\[
\mathcal L_{\rm mic}
=
\mathcal L_\Psi^{\rm ref}
+\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+\alpha_X X_i^aJ_i^a
+\beta_X X_i^aK_i^a.
\]

\item The quadratic heavy elimination is already structurally fixed:
\[
H_{\rm eff}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)-H_{\Psi X}(k)H_{XX}(k)^{-1}H_{X\Psi}(k).
\]

\item In the pure auxiliary working truncation,
\[
H_{XX}(k)=M_X^2\mathbf 1_X
\]
is already part of the explicit branch structure.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{B. Valley/Bloch extraction layer}

\begin{enumerate}
\item The exact projected transport matrices
\[
M_i=P_*\left.\partial_{k_i}H_{\rm eff}(k)\right|_{k=k_*}P_*
\]
are already formally fixed.

\item The low-valley coefficient extraction formulas are already fixed:
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3M_\parallel),
\]
\[
\alpha=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_1M_1+\sigma_2M_2),
\qquad
\beta=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_2M_1-\sigma_1M_2).
\]

\item The exact dictionary
\[
\lambda_\parallel=C_c g_c,\qquad
\alpha=C_E g_E,\qquad
\beta=C_O g_O
\]
is already fixed as the correct normalization layer, even though the constants \(C_c,C_E,C_O\) themselves are not yet numerically evaluated.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{C. Radial constitutive and one-mode layer}

\begin{enumerate}
\item The minimal constitutive ansatz for the working microscopic multiplet
\[
(P^A,\Psi,X_i^a)
\]
is already fixed.

\item The defect-core coefficient definitions are already fixed:
\[
a_0=\frac{g_E^{\rm core}+g_c^{\rm core}}{z_{0,0}},
\qquad
b_0=\frac{g_E^{\rm core}}{z_{0,0}},
\qquad
c_0=\frac{g_O^{\rm core}}{z_{0,0}}.
\]

\item The bulk mass parameter is already fixed by definition:
\[
\mu_\infty
=
\frac{
m(\sigma_\infty)-3\chi_\infty u_X(\sigma_\infty)
}{
z_0(\sigma_\infty)
}.
\]

\item The radial Callias-core superpotential is already fixed:
\[
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)=\mu(r)+\frac{\kappa b(r)}{r}.
\]

\item The sufficient one-mode criterion is already structurally fixed:
\[
\mu_\infty>0,\qquad
a_0>0,\qquad
b_0>0,\qquad
\frac{|\kappa_*|b_0}{a_0}>\frac12,
\]
with competitor exclusion for all other projected channels.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{D. Remote-gap theorem layer}

\begin{enumerate}
\item The full remote-gap sufficient criterion is already fixed:
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
\]

\item The clean self-adjoint operator form and the corresponding perturbative spectral-isolation proof are already in place.

\item The block-budget and finite-truncation Gershgorin variants are already structurally closed as support theorems.
\end{enumerate}

\section{II. Needs explicit computation}

The following items are not conceptually open; they simply still require explicit branch evaluation.

\subsection{A. Explicit evaluation of the Bloch-side constants}

\begin{enumerate}
\item The overlap constants
\[
C_c,\qquad C_E,\qquad C_O
\]
still need to be computed by the calibration protocol.

\item Concretely, this requires the three unit-channel calibration runs:
\[
(c\text{-unit}),\qquad (E\text{-unit}),\qquad (O\text{-unit}).
\]

\item After those runs,
\[
g_c=\frac{\lambda_\parallel}{C_c},
\qquad
g_E=\frac{\alpha}{C_E},
\qquad
g_O=\frac{\beta}{C_O}
\]
will become explicit numerical/analytic outputs.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{B. Explicit evaluation of the matching constants}

\begin{enumerate}
\item The matching constants
\[
\xi_c,\qquad \xi_E,\qquad \xi_O
\]
still need to be computed.

\item This requires paired core/valley calibration:
for each unit-channel run, compute both the valley-extracted coefficient and the radial core coefficient.

\item Then set
\[
\xi_E=\frac{g_E^{\rm core}}{g_E},
\qquad
\xi_c=\frac{g_c^{\rm core}}{g_c},
\qquad
\xi_O=\frac{g_O^{\rm core}}{g_O}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{C. Explicit low-slot spectral projection}

\begin{enumerate}
\item The exact valley projector
\[
P_*=\frac{1}{2\pi i}\oint_\Gamma (z-H_{\rm shell}(0))^{-1}dz
\]
is structurally fixed, but still needs explicit evaluation in the current branch.

\item The projected angular/channel set
\[
\mathfrak K_{\rm adm}^{\rm low}
\]
still needs to be explicitly computed after remote-gap reduction and low-slot projection.

\item In particular, the signed lowest channel \(\kappa_*\) must still be read off from the actual projected operator.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{D. Explicit core/bulk profile evaluation}

\begin{enumerate}
\item The background profiles
\[
\bar\sigma(r),\qquad
X_\perp(r),\qquad
X_\parallel(r)
\]
still need to be supplied explicitly, numerically or analytically, in the working branch.

\item From them one must compute
\[
\sigma_0,\qquad
X_0,\qquad
\sigma_\infty,\qquad
\chi_\infty.
\]

\item Then one can explicitly evaluate
\[
a_0,\qquad
b_0,\qquad
c_0,\qquad
\mu_\infty.
\]
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{E. Final benchmark ratios}

Once the previous layers are computed, the benchmark ratios
\[
R_c
=
\frac{\xi_c C_E}{\xi_E C_c}\frac{\lambda_\parallel}{\alpha},
\qquad
R_O
=
\frac{\xi_O C_E}{\xi_E C_O}\frac{\beta}{\alpha}
\]
still need to be explicitly evaluated.

Then the practically relevant criterion
\[
-1<R_c<1,\qquad
\alpha>0,\qquad
\mu_\infty>0,\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
\]
can be directly checked.
\end{enumerate}

\section{III. Still assumptions / branch-specific hypotheses}

The following items are not yet derived and must still be treated honestly as assumptions or matching hypotheses.

\subsection{A. Matching hypothesis itself}

At present, the relations
\[
g_E^{\rm core}=\xi_E g_E,
\qquad
g_c^{\rm core}=\xi_c g_c,
\qquad
g_O^{\rm core}=\xi_O g_O
\]
are still a matching hypothesis until the calibration runs are actually completed.

So the existence of positive finite matching constants
\[
\xi_E,\ \xi_c,\ \xi_O
\]
is still a branch-specific assumption, not yet a theorem.

\subsection{B. Unique signed lowest projected channel}

The statement
\[
\boxed{
\text{there exists a unique signed lowest projected channel }\kappa_*<0\text{ of multiplicity one}
}
\]
is still an assumption until the projected channel spectrum is explicitly computed.

This is one of the most important remaining branch-specific checks.

\subsection{C. Actual positivity of the bulk mass gap}

The inequality
\[
\mu_\infty>0
\]
is still a condition to be checked from the actual constitutive functions and asymptotic branch.
At present it is structurally well-defined, but not yet verified in the concrete working branch.

\subsection{D. Simultaneous parameter regime overlap}

Even if each separate condition is individually plausible, it is still an assumption that all of the following can hold in the same parameter regime:

\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho},
\qquad
\mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
-1<R_c<1,
\qquad
\kappa_*<0\ \text{unique}.
\]

The existence of a common regime is not yet proven; it must be checked explicitly.

\section{IV. Minimal decision tree}

The whole working program now reduces to the following decision tree.

\paragraph{Gate 1.}
Check
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
\]
If false, the low slot is not isolated and the one-mode criterion cannot be applied.

\paragraph{Gate 2.}
Compute the projected admissible channel set and determine whether there exists a unique signed lowest \(\kappa_*<0\).
If false, the compact one-mode criterion is not yet available.

\paragraph{Gate 3.}
Compute
\[
\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta,\qquad
C_c,C_E,C_O,\qquad
\xi_c,\xi_E,\xi_O.
\]
Then construct
\[
R_c,\qquad R_O.
\]

\paragraph{Gate 4.}
Compute
\[
\mu_\infty.
\]
If \(\mu_\infty\le 0\), the bulk gap does not support the protected-mode criterion.

\paragraph{Gate 5.}
Check
\[
\frac{\xi_E}{C_E}\alpha>0,
\qquad
1+R_c>0,
\qquad
2|\kappa_*|>1+R_c,
\]
and all competitor inequalities.

If all gates pass, then
\[
\operatorname{Ind}(\mathbb H_{\rm C})=1
\]
follows by the working theorem.

\section{V. Current honest status}

The current honest status is therefore:

\begin{enumerate}
\item The structural chain is already built.
\item The support theorems are largely complete.
\item The remaining work is finite and explicit.
\item The remaining bottleneck is no longer conceptual, but computational/verification-based.
\end{enumerate}

In particular, the main unfinished tasks are exactly:

\[
\boxed{
C_c,C_E,C_O,
\qquad
\xi_c,\xi_E,\xi_O,
\qquad
\kappa_*,
\qquad
\mu_\infty,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}-\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\]

Once these are evaluated, the working one-defect/one-mode criterion becomes a direct numerical/analytic verification problem.

\section{Final summary}

The audit divides the remaining ingredients into three classes.

\paragraph{Already available.}
The following are already structurally established:
\[
\mathcal Y_{\rm eff}=L-KH^{-1}K^\dagger,
\]
the refined locked + Class II branch,
the remote-gap theorem,
the valley extraction formulas for \((\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)\),
the radial constitutive formulas for \((a_0,b_0,c_0,\mu_\infty)\),
and the abstract one-mode sufficient criterion.

\paragraph{Needs explicit computation.}
The following still need concrete evaluation:
\[
C_c,\ C_E,\ C_O,\qquad
\xi_c,\ \xi_E,\ \xi_O,\qquad
\kappa_*,\qquad
\mu_\infty,\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}},\ \eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
\]

\paragraph{Still assumptions.}
Until explicitly verified in the working branch, the following remain assumptions:
the existence of positive matching constants,
the uniqueness of the signed lowest projected channel,
the positivity of \(\mu_\infty\),
and the existence of a common parameter regime where all inequalities hold simultaneously.

Therefore the main program is no longer conceptually open.
It has become a finite explicit verification problem on the refined locked + Class II working branch.

\section{Priority Computation I: explicit evaluation protocol for the remote-gap gate}

The first mandatory gate in the working one-defect/one-mode program is the remote-gap isolation inequality
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\]
If this fails, the low slot is not spectrally isolated, and none of the later channel-counting arguments can be safely applied.
So this gate must be evaluated first.

\section{Step 1: fix the low-slot window and the momentum radius \(\rho\)}

Choose the reference low slot (the candidate Dirac/valley slot) and fix a momentum radius
\[
0<\rho\le \rho_{\max}
\]
small enough that the low-slot expansion remains valid.
All estimates below are then carried out uniformly for
\[
|p|\le \rho.
\]

The output of this step is a concrete candidate interval
\[
0<\rho\le \rho_*,
\]
inside which both the low-slot expansion and the remote benchmark formulas are trusted.

\section{Step 2: compute the benchmark lower bounds for each remote sector}

Let the full remote benchmark operator be block-diagonal across the remote sectors:
\[
D_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)
=
D_{\mathrm{vol}}(p)
\oplus
D_{\mathrm{high}}(p)
\oplus
D_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}(p)
\oplus
D_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(p)
\oplus
\cdots.
\]

For each sector, compute an explicit lower bound on the spectral distance from zero:
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho}
\le
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(0,\operatorname{spec}(D_{\mathrm{vol}}(p))\bigr),
\]
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{high},\rho}
\le
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(0,\operatorname{spec}(D_{\mathrm{high}}(p))\bigr),
\]
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int},\rho}
\le
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(0,\operatorname{spec}(D_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}(p))\bigr),
\]
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\le
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(0,\operatorname{spec}(D_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}(p))\bigr).
\]

Then define
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}
:=
\min\Bigl\{
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho},
\Delta_{\mathrm{high},\rho},
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int},\rho},
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)},
\ldots
\Bigr\}.
}
\]

This is the benchmark side of the gate.

\paragraph{Working-branch placeholders.}
In the current working branch, the intended sectorwise lower bounds are of the schematic form
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho}\sim 4K-|r_*|,
\]
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{high},\rho}\sim \sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\]
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int},\rho}
\sim
q_*^2\left|(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}\right|,
\]
together with the previously established non-enriched lower bound.
These expressions must be inserted only after their positivity regime is explicitly checked.

\section{Step 3: compute the residual remote mixing budget}

Write the full remote remainder as
\[
R_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)
=
R_{\mathrm{rem}}^{\mathrm{offdiag}}(p)
+
R_{\mathrm{rem}}^{\mathrm{tail}}(p)
+
R_{\mathrm{rem}}^{\mathrm{diag\ corr}}(p).
\]

Define
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_{\mathrm{rem}}(p)\|.
\]

To bound this explicitly, split it into:

\subsection{(a) finite sectorwise off-diagonal budget}

For the truncated remote sector
\[
\mathcal H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}},
\]
define pairwise off-diagonal budgets
\[
\eta_{ab,\rho}
=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_{ab}(p)\|.
\]

Then
\[
\boxed{
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
\le
\sum_{a\neq b}\eta_{ab,\rho}.
}
\]

\subsection{(b) tail-coupling / power-counting budget}

Using the previously established tail theorem, bound the tail part by
\[
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
\le
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}
K_a\,\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}
\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a},
\qquad
r_a\ge 1.
}
\]

\subsection{(c) bounded diagonal correction budget}

If diagonal benchmark corrections are present, define
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_{\mathrm{rem}}^{\mathrm{diag\ corr}}(p)\|.
\]

Then a clean total bound is
\[
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
\le
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\]

This is the residual side of the gate.

\section{Step 4: define the gate margin}

Define the remote-gap margin
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak M_{\mathrm{rem}}(\rho)
:=
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}-\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\]

Then the pass/fail criterion is simply:
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak M_{\mathrm{rem}}(\rho)>0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\text{remote-gap gate passes at radius }\rho.
}
\]

The optimal practical strategy is to search for a window
\[
0<\rho\le \rho_*
\]
such that
\[
\mathfrak M_{\mathrm{rem}}(\rho)>0
\]
uniformly on that window.

\section{Step 5: optional sharper truncated check by Gershgorin}

For the finite truncated remote matrix \(H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(p)\), define
\[
\mathcal R_m(p):=\sum_{n\neq m}\bigl|(H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(p))_{mn}\bigr|,
\]
and
\[
\Delta_{G,\rho}
:=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\min_m
\Bigl(
|(H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(p))_{mm}|-\mathcal R_m(p)
\Bigr).
\]

If
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{G,\rho}>0,
}
\]
then the truncated remote matrix is already spectrally isolated from zero.
This does not replace the full operator-norm gate, but it is often a useful sharper diagnostic when the remote matrix is sparse.

\section{Step 6: output classification of the remote-gap gate}

The remote-gap audit should output exactly one of the following statuses:

\paragraph{Status A: passed.}
There exists a working window \(0<\rho\le \rho_*\) such that
\[
\mathfrak M_{\mathrm{rem}}(\rho)>0.
\]
Then the low slot is spectrally isolated and the one-mode program may proceed.

\paragraph{Status B: inconclusive.}
The available lower/upper bounds are too crude to decide the sign of \(\mathfrak M_{\mathrm{rem}}(\rho)\).
Then sharper benchmark estimates or sharper residual budgets are needed.

\paragraph{Status C: failed.}
The best available estimate gives
\[
\mathfrak M_{\mathrm{rem}}(\rho)\le 0
\]
throughout the candidate window.
Then the current branch does not yet isolate the low slot and the later protected-mode counting cannot be trusted.

\section{Priority list of actual quantities to compute next inside Gate 1}

To make Gate 1 executable in the current working branch, the next concrete computations should be ordered as follows:

\begin{enumerate}
\item compute or confirm explicit positive formulas for
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho},\ 
\Delta_{\mathrm{high},\rho},\ 
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int},\rho},\ 
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)};
\]

\item compute the pairwise budgets
\[
\eta_{ab,\rho}
\]
for the truncated remote off-diagonal blocks;

\item compute the tail constants
\[
K_a,\ \widetilde K_a,\ r_a,\ \sigma_a;
\]

\item compute or bound \(\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}\);

\item assemble
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}
\quad\text{and}\quad
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho};
\]

\item inspect the sign of
\[
\mathfrak M_{\mathrm{rem}}(\rho).
\]
\end{enumerate}

Only after this gate is passed is it efficient to move on to
\[
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)
\to
(C_c,C_E,C_O)
\to
\kappa_*
\to
\mu_\infty
\to
(\xi_c,\xi_E,\xi_O).
\]

\section{Conclusion of the first-priority protocol}

The first-priority computational target is therefore not a new theorem but the explicit evaluation of
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak M_{\mathrm{rem}}(\rho)
=
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}-\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\]

Once this quantity is shown to be positive on a nontrivial \(\rho\)-window, the rest of the one-defect/one-mode chain becomes operationally meaningful.

\section{Final summary}

The first mandatory gate of the working program is the remote-gap margin
\[
\mathfrak M_{\mathrm{rem}}(\rho)
=
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}-\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
\]

To evaluate it, one must:

\begin{enumerate}
\item compute the sectorwise benchmark lower bounds and define
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}
=
\min\{\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho},\Delta_{\mathrm{high},\rho},
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int},\rho},
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)},\ldots\};
\]

\item compute the residual mixing budget
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}
\le
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
+\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
+\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho},
\]
with
\[
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
\le
\sum_{a\neq b}\eta_{ab,\rho},
\qquad
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
\le
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}K_a\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a};
\]

\item inspect the sign of
\[
\mathfrak M_{\mathrm{rem}}(\rho).
\]
\end{enumerate}

The gate passes iff
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak M_{\mathrm{rem}}(\rho)>0
}
\]
on a nontrivial working window \(0<\rho\le \rho_*\).

This is the highest-priority explicit computation, because if it fails, the later one-mode channel analysis is not yet trustworthy.

\section{Honest current status of the microscopic PDE}

At the present stage, the full microscopic TECT condensate PDE is not yet uniquely derived from first principles.
The current explicit model
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi,P]
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^aJ_i^a[\Psi,P]
+
\beta_X X_i^aK_i^a[P,\Psi]
}
\label{eq:working_mic_ansatz_clean}
\end{equation}
should therefore be described as the strongest explicit \emph{working microscopic ansatz}, not yet as the final complete TECT action.

What is already structurally fixed is the reduced infrared Dirac-type form.
The final finite arbiter of whether the current working branch is dynamically sufficient is the Bloch-frame calibration:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(C_E,C_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:final_bloch_calibration_clean}
\end{equation}
If this calibration succeeds, the current branch is dynamically sufficient inside this explicit setting.
If it fails, then the current \(L_{\mathrm{mic}}\) is structurally incomplete and the true complete microscopic TECT action must contain additional UV structure.

\section{Corrected transverse microscopic audit}

The transverse microscopic audit must be stated carefully.

\subsection{Naive local \(JK\) does not suffice}

In the minimal shell-adapted form, the \(J\)-sector is axial,
\[
J\sim j\,\Sigma_3,
\]
while the \(K\)-sector is transverse,
\[
K\sim k_E\Sigma_1+k_O\Sigma_2.
\]
Then the simplest local real Hermitian \(JK\) bilinear reduces to
\[
\Sigma_3(k_E\Sigma_1+k_O\Sigma_2)+(k_E\Sigma_1+k_O\Sigma_2)\Sigma_3
=
k_E\{\Sigma_3,\Sigma_1\}+k_O\{\Sigma_3,\Sigma_2\}=0.
\]
Therefore:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the naive local real Hermitian }JK\text{ bilinear vanishes.}
}
\label{eq:naive_JK_zero_clean}
\end{equation}

So the statement
\[
JK\text{ automatically produces }c_E,c_O
\]
is too strong and should not be used.

\subsection{Actual transverse frontier}

The genuinely load-bearing transverse audit is the shell-derivative audit
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{JK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0},
\qquad
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{KK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0}.
}
\label{eq:derivative_shell_frontier_clean}
\end{equation}
These derivative-generated shell tensors can avoid the simple Pauli anticommutation obstruction and generate nonzero transverse witnesses.

In the explicit folded-Bragg Class II branch, this derivative bookkeeping compresses to the Fourier-overlap problem
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\sum_A\sum_{Q+Q'=G_*}
\widehat J_i^A(Q)\widehat K_{i,\alpha}^A(Q').
}
\label{eq:Talpha_ClassII_clean}
\end{equation}
In the minimal first-shell-dominant reduction, the final transverse yes/no test is reduced to two explicit overlaps:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{G_*}(C_1\cdot G_*)\neq 0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}(C_2\cdot G_*)\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:two_overlap_test_clean}
\end{equation}
If these hold, then
\[
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0)
\]
is realized in the explicit Class II branch.

\section{How to keep the TD/DT result without overclaiming}

The previously written TD/DT section can still be used, but only with the correct status label.

\subsection{Branch-level transverse summary}

Within the current explicit branch, the mixed shell--defect blocks \(TD\) and \(DT\) may be summarized as
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_\perp(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[
(A_E+B_E)E^\mu_a\Sigma_a
+
(A_O+B_O)J^\mu_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr].
\label{eq:TDDT_summary_clean}
\end{equation}
Define
\[
C_E:=A_E+B_E,
\qquad
C_O:=A_O+B_O.
\]
Under the previously fixed projector normalization conventions, the reduced transverse coefficients are summarized by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_0^{(1)}=\frac12 C_E=\frac12(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
o_0^{(1)}=\frac12 C_O=\frac12(A_O+B_O).
}
\label{eq:e0o0_clean}
\end{equation}
Using
\[
\alpha=I_\theta e_0^{(1)},
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta o_0^{(1)},
\qquad
I_\theta=-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
\]
one obtains
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\theta_0\kappa(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\theta_0\kappa(A_O+B_O).
}
\label{eq:alpha_beta_TDDT_clean}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Correct status label.}
Equation \eqref{eq:alpha_beta_TDDT_clean} should be described as:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the branch-level reduced transverse summary within the current explicit LO/Class II realization.}
}
\label{eq:branch_level_status_clean}
\end{equation}
It should \emph{not} be described as the final unconditional microscopic closure of the full TECT PDE.

\section{Unified honest endpoint}

Putting everything together, the strongest honest current statement is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{The reduced Dirac-type PDE form is structurally fixed.}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{The current }L_{\mathrm{mic}}\text{ is the strongest explicit working microscopic branch.}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{The transverse sector is not decided by a naive local }JK\text{ term, but by the derivative-resolved shell audit of }JK\text{ and/or }KK.
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Inside the current explicit branch, the TD/DT transverse summary may be used as a reduced branch-level coefficient summary.}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{The final microscopic frontier remains the explicit Bloch calibration of }
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta),
\text{ equivalently }(C_\parallel,C_E,C_O).
}
\end{equation}

\section{Practical consequence for the manuscript}

Therefore the manuscript should distinguish three levels clearly:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{Algebraically closed:} the reduced anisotropic Dirac-type PDE and Clifford embedding;
\item \textbf{Explicitly realized in the current branch:} the branch-level transverse coefficient summary from TD/DT and the Class II shell-projection framework;
\item \textbf{Still open microscopically:} the final unconditional evaluation of the Bloch-frame overlaps and the full-action coefficient extraction.
\end{enumerate}

This wording is both strong and honest.

\section{Final summary}

The attached material sharpens the honest logical status of the current program.

First, the current microscopic model
\[
L_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi,P]
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^aJ_i^a[\Psi,P]
+
\beta_X X_i^aK_i^a[P,\Psi]
\]
should be described as the strongest explicit working microscopic ansatz, not yet as the final complete TECT action.

Second, the reduced anisotropic Dirac-type PDE form is already structurally fixed, and the final finite arbiter of the current branch is the Bloch calibration
\[
C_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(C_E,C_O)\neq (0,0).
\]

Third, the transverse microscopic frontier is not the naive local \(JK\) bilinear, which vanishes by Pauli anticommutation, but the derivative-resolved shell audit
\[
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{JK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0},
\qquad
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{KK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0}.
\]

Fourth, within the current explicit LO/Class II branch, the TD/DT block formulas may still be used as a branch-level reduced summary:
\[
e_0^{(1)}=\frac12(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
o_0^{(1)}=\frac12(A_O+B_O),
\]
\[
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\theta_0\kappa(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\theta_0\kappa(A_O+B_O).
\]

Thus the correct final wording is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the reduced PDE is structurally fixed,}
\quad
\text{the current branch is an explicit working realization,}
\quad
\text{and the final microscopic frontier is the explicit Bloch calibration.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Current working benchmark proposition for Gate 1}

We now fix the benchmark side of the remote-gap gate in the notation of the current refined locked + Class II working branch.

\section{Goal}

The first mandatory gate is the remote-gap inequality
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho}.
}
\]
If this fails, the low slot is not spectrally isolated, and the later protected-channel counting is not yet trustworthy.
So the first nonredundant task is to fix a clean working formula for
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}.
\]

\section{Sectorwise benchmark inputs}

In the current working truncation, the remote benchmark is built from four sectorwise lower bounds.

\subsection{1. Higher-shell benchmark}

Let
\[
\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}
=
\inf_{Q\in\mathcal Q_{\mathrm{high}}}
\bigl||Q|^2-q_*^2\bigr|>0,
\]
and assume the shell energy is of the form
\[
\Lambda(Q)=r_*+K(|Q|^2-q_*^2)^2,
\qquad
K>0.
\]
Then
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{high},\rho}^{(0)}
\ge
K\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}^2-|r_*|.
\]
For the current BCC reciprocal arithmetic,
\[
\delta_{\mathrm{shell}}=2,
\]
hence
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{high},\rho}^{(0)}
\ge
4K-|r_*|.
}
\]

\subsection{2. Volumetric benchmark}

For the heavy volumetric sector, the current working branch uses a positive lower bound of the form
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho}^{(0)}
=
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2}.
}
\]
This is the current refined heavy-locking benchmark.
If one prefers a coarser but simpler benchmark, one may replace it by a positive lower bound such as
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho}^{(0)}\ge c_{\mathrm{vol}}M_\sigma,
\qquad
c_{\mathrm{vol}}>0,
\]
provided that this alternative lower bound has already been justified in the chosen truncation.

\subsection{3. Wrong-internal benchmark}

At the shell point \(G_*\), the wrong-internal splitting is
\[
E_L-E_*
=
q_*^2
\left[
(\lambda+\mu)
+
\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right].
\]
Therefore the corresponding benchmark is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int},\rho}^{(0)}
=
q_*^2
\left|
(\lambda+\mu)
+
\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|.
}
\]
Under a bounded perturbation
\[
H=H_0+\delta H,
\qquad
\|Q\delta H Q\|\le \varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}},
\]
the gap is stable:
\[
m_{\mathrm{int}}
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int},\rho}^{(0)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{int}}.
\]

\subsection{4. Same-shell non-enriched benchmark}

Let
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\]
denote the same-shell non-enriched lower bound produced by the finite truncated eigenvalue computation, and let
\[
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\]
be its truncation/error budget.
Then the usable benchmark entry is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}.
}
\]

\section{Current working master benchmark}

Combining the four sectorwise lower bounds, define
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
:=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\Biggr\}.
}
\]
Equivalently, if the coarser volumetric benchmark is used, replace the second entry by \(c_{\mathrm{vol}}M_\sigma\).

\section{Gate-1 proposition}

\paragraph{Proposition (current working benchmark gate).}
Assume the remote remainder satisfies
\[
\eta_{R,\rho}
=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_R(p)\|.
\]
If
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho},
}
\]
then the remote sector has a positive uniform spectral gap:
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_\rho
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0.
}
\]

\paragraph{Proof.}
By construction,
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
\le
\delta_{0,\rho}
:=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(0,\operatorname{spec}(D_R(p))\bigr).
\]
Therefore
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\Longrightarrow
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}.
\]
The uniform remote-gap criterion then gives
\[
\Delta_\rho=\delta_{0,\rho}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0.
\]
Hence the low slot is spectrally isolated from the remote sector.
\(\square\)

\section{Honest current status of Gate 1}

The current benchmark side is now compressed to a very small remaining frontier.

\paragraph{Already explicit or nearly explicit.}
The following are already available in usable working form:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the higher-shell benchmark
\[
4K-|r_*|;
\]

\item the wrong-internal benchmark
\[
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|;
\]

\item the heavy volumetric benchmark in the current refined heavy-locking working form
\[
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{Still genuinely unresolved.}
The only genuinely model-specific unresolved benchmark entry is
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)},
\]
together with the residual remote-mixing norm
\[
\eta_{R,\rho}.
\]

Thus Gate 1 is now reduced to exactly:
\[
\boxed{
\text{one finite same-shell non-enriched eigenvalue computation}
\quad+\quad
\text{one remote-mixing norm bound.}
}
\]

\section{Operational conclusion}

Therefore the next explicit computation inside Gate 1 should not be a new theorem.
It should be:

\begin{enumerate}
\item compute
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)};
\]

\item compute or bound
\[
\eta_{R,\rho};
\]

\item assemble
\[
\mathfrak M_{\mathrm{rem}}(\rho)
=
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}-\eta_{R,\rho};
\]

\item determine whether \(\mathfrak M_{\mathrm{rem}}(\rho)>0\) on a nontrivial \(\rho\)-window.
\end{enumerate}

Only after this gate is passed is it maximally efficient to continue to
\[
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)\to(C_c,C_E,C_O)\to\kappa_*\to\mu_\infty.
\]

\section{Final summary}

The correct priority is to push Gate 1 rather than further polish the TD/DT section.

The current working remote benchmark is
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\Biggr\}.
\]

If
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho},
\]
then
\[
\Delta_\rho
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0,
\]
so the low slot is spectrally isolated.

At the current stage, the higher-shell and wrong-internal entries are already explicit, and the volumetric entry is available in a usable working form.
The only genuinely unresolved benchmark-side item is the same-shell non-enriched lower bound, together with the residual remote-mixing norm.

Therefore the real remaining Gate-1 frontier is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{one finite same-shell non-enriched eigenvalue computation}
\quad+\quad
\text{one remote-mixing norm bound.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Finite truncated eigenvalue formulation of the same-shell non-enriched benchmark}

We now isolate the last unresolved benchmark entry in Gate 1, namely the same-shell non-enriched lower bound
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}.
\]

\section{1. Same-shell decomposition}

Let
\[
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
=
\Pi_{S_*}\,H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k_*+p)\,\Pi_{S_*},
\qquad |p|\le \rho,
\]
be the shell-projected effective operator near the folded Bragg point.

Assume the shell space admits the orthogonal decomposition
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{S_*}
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}},
}
\]
where:

\begin{itemize}
\item \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{enr}}\) is the enriched low slot (the candidate Dirac/valley slot),
\item \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}\) is the orthogonal complement inside the same shell.
\end{itemize}

Let
\[
P_{\mathrm{enr}}
\]
be the orthogonal projector onto \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{enr}}\), and define
\[
\boxed{
Q_{\mathrm{non}}:=\Pi_{S_*}-P_{\mathrm{enr}}.
}
\]

Then the exact same-shell non-enriched operator is
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{non}}(p)
:=
Q_{\mathrm{non}}\,H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)\,Q_{\mathrm{non}}.
}
\]

\section{2. Exact benchmark quantity}

The exact same-shell non-enriched benchmark gap is
\[
\boxed{
\delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}
:=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(0,\operatorname{spec}(H_{\mathrm{non}}(p))\bigr).
}
\]

This is the exact quantity that must be inserted into the full remote benchmark minimum.
However, it is generally not directly computable in closed form.
So we replace it by a finite truncation plus an explicit error budget.

\section{3. Finite truncation}

Choose a finite-dimensional trial subspace
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non}}^{(N)}
\subset
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}},
\qquad
\dim \mathcal H_{\mathrm{non}}^{(N)}=N,
\]
with orthogonal projector
\[
Q_{\mathrm{non}}^{(N)}.
\]

Define the finite truncated operator
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{non}}^{(N)}(p)
:=
Q_{\mathrm{non}}^{(N)}\,H_{\mathrm{non}}(p)\,Q_{\mathrm{non}}^{(N)}.
}
\]

Equivalently, after choosing an orthonormal basis of \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non}}^{(N)}\), one obtains an \(N\times N\) Hermitian matrix
\[
\mathbf H_{\mathrm{non}}^{(N)}(p).
\]

Define the finite benchmark
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
:=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(0,\operatorname{spec}(H_{\mathrm{non}}^{(N)}(p))\bigr).
}
\]

This is the quantity obtained by the actual finite eigenvalue computation.

\section{4. Truncation error budget}

Define the truncation remainder by
\[
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}
\left\|
H_{\mathrm{non}}(p)
-
\iota_N H_{\mathrm{non}}^{(N)}(p)\iota_N^*
\right\|,
}
\]
where
\[
\iota_N:\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non}}^{(N)}\hookrightarrow \mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\]
is the canonical inclusion.

In practice, one may bound \(\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}\) by:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a tail norm estimate from omitted harmonic modes;
\item an operator-norm estimate from neglected off-shell couplings;
\item a numerical residual estimate if the truncated basis is obtained variationally.
\end{enumerate}

The important point is only that \(\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}\) be an explicit uniform bound for \(|p|\le \rho\).

\section{5. Benchmark proposition}

\paragraph{Proposition (finite same-shell non-enriched benchmark).}
Assume \(H_{\mathrm{non}}(p)\) is self-adjoint for every \(|p|\le \rho\), and let
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)},
\qquad
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\]
be defined as above.
Then
\[
\boxed{
\delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}.
}
\]

\paragraph{Proof.}
For each fixed \(|p|\le \rho\), the self-adjoint perturbation inequality gives
\[
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(0,\operatorname{spec}(H_{\mathrm{non}}(p))\bigr)
\ge
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(0,\operatorname{spec}(H_{\mathrm{non}}^{(N)}(p))\bigr)
-
\left\|
H_{\mathrm{non}}(p)-\iota_N H_{\mathrm{non}}^{(N)}(p)\iota_N^*
\right\|.
\]
Taking the infimum over \(|p|\le \rho\) yields
\[
\delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}.
\]
\(\square\)

\section{6. Usable benchmark entry}

Therefore the usable same-shell non-enriched benchmark entry is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}.
}
\]

This is exactly the object that enters the current working master benchmark:
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\Biggr\}.
}
\]

\section{7. Computational realization}

The actual finite computation now reduces to the following explicit task:

\begin{enumerate}
\item choose the truncated same-shell non-enriched basis \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non}}^{(N)}\);
\item compute the Hermitian matrix \(\mathbf H_{\mathrm{non}}^{(N)}(p)\);
\item compute its smallest absolute eigenvalue uniformly for \(|p|\le \rho\):
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\min_j |\lambda_j^{(N)}(p)|;
\]
\item compute or bound the truncation error
\[
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)};
\]
\item form
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

This is the single remaining benchmark-side finite eigenvalue problem in Gate 1.

\section{8. Honest current status}

Within the current working branch, the higher-shell, volumetric, and wrong-internal benchmark entries already exist in usable explicit form.
Therefore the benchmark-side frontier has now been reduced to exactly one unresolved finite computation:
\[
\boxed{
\text{evaluate }
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}.
}
\]

Once this is done, the benchmark side of Gate 1 is complete, and the only remaining Gate-1 task is the residual norm budget \(\eta_{R,\rho}\).

\section{Final summary}

The unresolved benchmark entry in Gate 1 is the same-shell non-enriched gap.

Let
\[
H_{\mathrm{non}}(p)=Q_{\mathrm{non}}H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)Q_{\mathrm{non}}
\]
be the exact same-shell non-enriched operator, and let
\[
H_{\mathrm{non}}^{(N)}(p)
\]
be its finite truncation on an \(N\)-dimensional trial space.

Define
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
=
\inf_{|p|\le \rho}
\operatorname{dist}\!\bigl(0,\operatorname{spec}(H_{\mathrm{non}}^{(N)}(p))\bigr),
\]
and
\[
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}
\left\|
H_{\mathrm{non}}(p)-\iota_N H_{\mathrm{non}}^{(N)}(p)\iota_N^*
\right\|.
\]

Then the exact benchmark is bounded below by
\[
\delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}.
\]

Therefore the usable same-shell non-enriched benchmark entry is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}.
}
\]

This is the only unresolved benchmark-side finite eigenvalue computation still needed to complete the benchmark part of Gate 1.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Clean decomposition of the residual remote budget in Gate 1}

We now fix the residual side of Gate 1 in the notation of the current refined locked + Class II working branch.

\section{1. Goal}

The first mandatory gate is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho},
}
\]
where
\[
\eta_{R,\rho}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_R(p)\|.
\]

The benchmark side has already been reduced to
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\Biggr\}.
\]

So it remains to fix a clean and explicit decomposition of \(\eta_{R,\rho}\).

\section{2. Full residual decomposition}

Write the full remote operator as
\[
H_R(p)=D_R(p)+R_R(p),
\qquad |p|\le \rho,
\]
where \(D_R(p)\) is the benchmark remote operator and \(R_R(p)\) is the full residual remote remainder.

We decompose the remainder into three pieces:
\[
\boxed{
R_R(p)
=
R_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(p)
+
R_R^{\mathrm{tail}}(p)
+
R_R^{\mathrm{diag}}(p).
}
\]

Here:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(R_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(p)\) is the off-diagonal remainder inside the finite truncated remote sector;
\item \(R_R^{\mathrm{tail}}(p)\) contains all couplings to omitted tail sectors and all induced tail-mediated corrections;
\item \(R_R^{\mathrm{diag}}(p)\) contains the bounded difference between the exact diagonal/reference part and the simplified benchmark diagonal used in \(\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}\).
\end{enumerate}

Define the corresponding budgets
\[
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(p)\|,
\]
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_R^{\mathrm{tail}}(p)\|,
\]
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_R^{\mathrm{diag}}(p)\|.
\]

Then by the triangle inequality,
\[
\boxed{
\eta_{R,\rho}
\le
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\]

\section{3. Finite truncated remote budget}

In the finite truncated remote sector, let
\[
\mathcal H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}.
\]

Write the truncated off-diagonal remainder as
\[
R_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & R_{\mathrm{vol,high}} & R_{\mathrm{vol,non}} & R_{\mathrm{vol,wrong}}\\
R_{\mathrm{high,vol}} & 0 & R_{\mathrm{high,non}} & R_{\mathrm{high,wrong}}\\
R_{\mathrm{non,vol}} & R_{\mathrm{non,high}} & 0 & R_{\mathrm{non,wrong}}\\
R_{\mathrm{wrong,vol}} & R_{\mathrm{wrong,high}} & R_{\mathrm{wrong,non}} & 0
\end{pmatrix}(p).
\]

Define the pairwise budgets
\[
\eta_{ab,\rho}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_{ab}(p)\|.
\]

Then
\[
\boxed{
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
\le
\sum_{a\neq b}\eta_{ab,\rho}.
}
\]

Explicitly,
\[
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
\le
\eta_{\mathrm{vol,high},\rho}
+\eta_{\mathrm{vol,non},\rho}
+\eta_{\mathrm{vol,wrong},\rho}
+\eta_{\mathrm{high,vol},\rho}
+\eta_{\mathrm{high,non},\rho}
+\eta_{\mathrm{high,wrong},\rho}
+\eta_{\mathrm{non,vol},\rho}
+\eta_{\mathrm{non,high},\rho}
+\eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho}
+\eta_{\mathrm{wrong,vol},\rho}
+\eta_{\mathrm{wrong,high},\rho}
+\eta_{\mathrm{wrong,non},\rho}.
\]

If self-adjointness gives
\[
R_{ab}(p)=R_{ba}(p)^\dagger,
\]
then the symmetric budgets satisfy
\[
\eta_{ab,\rho}=\eta_{ba,\rho},
\]
and the previous bound may be rewritten more economically as
\[
\boxed{
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
\le
2\Bigl(
\eta_{\mathrm{vol,high},\rho}
+\eta_{\mathrm{vol,non},\rho}
+\eta_{\mathrm{vol,wrong},\rho}
+\eta_{\mathrm{high,non},\rho}
+\eta_{\mathrm{high,wrong},\rho}
+\eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho}
\Bigr).
}
\]

This is still crude, but it is rigorous and directly computable.

\section{4. Tail budget}

Let \(R_R^{\mathrm{tail}}(p)\) denote all couplings involving omitted harmonics, omitted heavy auxiliaries, and tail-mediated effective corrections.
By the previously established power-counting/tail theorem, one may assume a bound of the form
\[
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
\le
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}
K_a\,\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}
\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a},
\qquad
r_a\ge 1.
}
\]

This expresses two structural facts:

\begin{enumerate}
\item every tail correction vanishes at least as \(O(\rho)\) near the low crossing;
\item heavy-mediated tails carry additional inverse-mass suppression.
\end{enumerate}

In the current branch, this budget includes in particular:

\begin{enumerate}
\item omitted same-shell harmonics outside the chosen \(N\)-dimensional non-enriched truncation;
\item omitted higher-shell harmonics coupled through residual off-shell transport;
\item omitted heavy-locking or mediator-induced tail corrections beyond the retained quadratic working truncation.
\end{enumerate}

\section{5. Diagonal correction budget}

The benchmark operator \(D_R(p)\) is not necessarily the exact diagonal block of the full operator; it is a simplified lower-bound model.
Hence define the diagonal correction
\[
R_R^{\mathrm{diag}}(p)
:=
D_R^{\mathrm{exact}}(p)-D_R^{\mathrm{bench}}(p),
\]
where \(D_R^{\mathrm{bench}}(p)\) is the diagonal/reference operator whose spectrum is bounded below by \(\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}\).

Its uniform budget is
\[
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_R^{\mathrm{diag}}(p)\|.
}
\]

Typical contributions to \(\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}\) in the current working branch are:

\begin{enumerate}
\item bounded deviations of the actual volumetric branch from the coarse benchmark
\[
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2};
\]

\item bounded deviations of the actual wrong-internal splitting from the simple shell-point estimate
\[
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|;
\]

\item residual bounded corrections to the same-shell non-enriched benchmark not already absorbed into
\[
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

If the benchmark entries are taken directly from exact diagonal sectors, then one may set
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}=0.
\]
Otherwise, \(\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}\) must be kept explicitly.

\section{6. Master residual proposition}

\paragraph{Proposition (current working residual budget).}
For the current refined locked + Class II working branch,
\[
\boxed{
\eta_{R,\rho}
\le
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho},
}
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
\le
\sum_{a\neq b}\eta_{ab,\rho},
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
\le
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}
K_a\,\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}
\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a}.
}
\]

Therefore the Gate-1 margin obeys
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak M_{\mathrm{rem}}(\rho)
:=
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}-\eta_{R,\rho}
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
-
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
-
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
-
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\]

So a sufficient practical gate condition is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
>
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\]

\paragraph{Proof.}
This is immediate from the decomposition
\[
R_R=R_R^{\mathrm{tr}}+R_R^{\mathrm{tail}}+R_R^{\mathrm{diag}}
\]
and the triangle inequality.
\(\square\)

\section{7. Gate-1 closure statement}

Combining the benchmark proposition from the previous step with the present residual proposition, the full Gate-1 pass criterion becomes
\[
\boxed{
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\Biggr\}
>
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\]

If this holds on a nontrivial interval \(0<\rho\le \rho_*\), then
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_\rho>0
}
\]
and the low slot is uniformly isolated from the remote sector.

\section{8. Honest current status}

At this point, Gate 1 is reduced to exactly two explicit finite tasks:

\begin{enumerate}
\item compute
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)};
\]

\item compute or bound
\[
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}},
\qquad
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho},
\qquad
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Everything else in Gate 1 is already structurally organized.

Therefore the unresolved Gate-1 frontier is no longer conceptual.
It is the explicit evaluation of a finite non-enriched benchmark together with an explicit residual norm budget.

\section{Final summary}

The residual side of Gate 1 is cleanly decomposed as
\[
R_R(p)=R_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(p)+R_R^{\mathrm{tail}}(p)+R_R^{\mathrm{diag}}(p),
\]
so that
\[
\eta_{R,\rho}
\le
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
\]

The finite truncated budget is
\[
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
\le
\sum_{a\neq b}\eta_{ab,\rho},
\qquad
\eta_{ab,\rho}
=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_{ab}(p)\|.
\]

The tail budget is bounded by power counting:
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
\le
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}}
K_a\,\rho^{r_a}
+
\sum_{a\in\mathcal A_{\mathrm{act}}^{(H)}}
\frac{\widetilde K_a}{M_a^{\sigma_a}}\rho^{r_a},
\qquad
r_a\ge 1.
\]

The diagonal correction budget is
\[
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}
=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_R^{\mathrm{diag}}(p)\|.
\]

Hence a sufficient Gate-1 condition is
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
>
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
\]

Combining this with the previous benchmark result, the remaining unresolved Gate-1 tasks are exactly:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the finite same-shell non-enriched computation
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)};
\]

\item the explicit evaluation of
\[
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}},
\qquad
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho},
\qquad
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Thus Gate 1 is now fully reduced to a finite benchmark computation plus a finite residual-norm computation.

\section{Pairwise audit table for the truncated remote budget}

We now resolve the truncated remote norm budget
\[
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
\]
into explicit pairwise source terms in the notation of the current refined locked + Class II working branch.

\section{1. Projectors and unique pair set}

Let
\[
Q_{\mathrm{vol}},\qquad
Q_{\mathrm{high}},\qquad
Q_{\mathrm{non}},\qquad
Q_{\mathrm{wrong}}
\]
denote the orthogonal projectors onto
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}},\qquad
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}},\qquad
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}},\qquad
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}},
\]
respectively, inside the finite truncated remote sector.

For \(a\neq b\), define the pairwise off-diagonal blocks
\[
R_{ab}(p):=Q_a\,H_R^{\mathrm{tr}}(p)\,Q_b,
\qquad
\eta_{ab,\rho}:=\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_{ab}(p)\|.
\]

By self-adjointness,
\[
R_{ab}(p)=R_{ba}(p)^\dagger,
\qquad
\eta_{ab,\rho}=\eta_{ba,\rho}.
\]
Hence it suffices to track the six unordered pairs
\[
(\mathrm{vol,high}),\ 
(\mathrm{vol,non}),\ 
(\mathrm{vol,wrong}),\ 
(\mathrm{high,non}),\ 
(\mathrm{high,wrong}),\ 
(\mathrm{non,wrong}).
\]

The truncated remote budget obeys
\[
\boxed{
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
\le
2\Bigl(
\eta_{\mathrm{vol,high},\rho}
+\eta_{\mathrm{vol,non},\rho}
+\eta_{\mathrm{vol,wrong},\rho}
+\eta_{\mathrm{high,non},\rho}
+\eta_{\mathrm{high,wrong},\rho}
+\eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho}
\Bigr).
}
\]

\section{2. Universal direct/heavy decomposition for each pair}

Write the effective operator as
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)=H_{\mathrm{dir}}(k)+\Delta_X(k),
\]
where
\[
\Delta_X(k)
=
-
H_{\Psi X}(k)H_{XX}(k)^{-1}H_{X\Psi}(k).
\]

In the auxiliary Class II working truncation,
\[
H_{XX}(k)=M_X^2\mathbf 1_X,
\qquad
H_{\Psi X}(k)=\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k).
\]
Therefore
\[
\Delta_X(k)
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\bigl(\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k)\bigr)
\bigl(\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k)\bigr)^\dagger.
\]

For each pair \(a\neq b\), define the direct budget
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal D_{ab,\rho}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}
\left\|
Q_a\,H_{\mathrm{dir}}(k_*+p)\,Q_b
\right\|.
}
\]

Define the heavy-mediated channel budgets
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal M_{ab,\rho}^{JJ}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}
\left\|
Q_a\,\mathcal J\mathcal J^\dagger\,Q_b
\right\|,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal M_{ab,\rho}^{JK}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}
\left\|
Q_a\,(\mathcal J\mathcal K^\dagger+\mathcal K\mathcal J^\dagger)\,Q_b
\right\|,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal M_{ab,\rho}^{KK}
:=
\sup_{|p|\le \rho}
\left\|
Q_a\,\mathcal K\mathcal K^\dagger\,Q_b
\right\|.
}
\]

Then every pairwise budget satisfies the exact current-branch bound
\[
\boxed{
\eta_{ab,\rho}
\le
\mathcal D_{ab,\rho}
+
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\mathcal M_{ab,\rho}^{JJ}
+
\frac{|\alpha_X\beta_X|}{M_X^2}\mathcal M_{ab,\rho}^{JK}
+
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\mathcal M_{ab,\rho}^{KK}.
}
\]

This is the master pairwise audit formula.

\section{3. Pairwise source table}

We now identify the source content of each pair.

\subsection{(i) Volumetric--higher-shell pair}

\[
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{vol,high},\rho}
\le
\mathcal D_{\mathrm{vol,high},\rho}
+
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\mathcal M_{\mathrm{vol,high},\rho}^{JJ}
+
\frac{|\alpha_X\beta_X|}{M_X^2}\mathcal M_{\mathrm{vol,high},\rho}^{JK}
+
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\mathcal M_{\mathrm{vol,high},\rho}^{KK}.
}
\]

\paragraph{Direct source.}
\(\mathcal D_{\mathrm{vol,high},\rho}\) comes from direct volumetric--inter-shell transport mixing inside \(H_{\mathrm{dir}}\), i.e. shell-number-changing couplings between the heavy volumetric block and higher-shell harmonics.

\paragraph{Heavy-mediated source.}
The three \(\mathcal M_{\mathrm{vol,high},\rho}^{UV}\) terms come from Class II mediation with one leg in the volumetric sector and the other in the higher-shell sector.

\subsection{(ii) Volumetric--same-shell non-enriched pair}

\[
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{vol,non},\rho}
\le
\mathcal D_{\mathrm{vol,non},\rho}
+
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\mathcal M_{\mathrm{vol,non},\rho}^{JJ}
+
\frac{|\alpha_X\beta_X|}{M_X^2}\mathcal M_{\mathrm{vol,non},\rho}^{JK}
+
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\mathcal M_{\mathrm{vol,non},\rho}^{KK}.
}
\]

\paragraph{Direct source.}
\(\mathcal D_{\mathrm{vol,non},\rho}\) comes from the direct coupling between the volumetric branch and the same-shell non-enriched harmonics.

\paragraph{Heavy-mediated source.}
The \(\mathcal M_{\mathrm{vol,non},\rho}^{UV}\) terms come from mediator exchange with one leg on the volumetric sector and the other on the same-shell non-enriched sector.

\subsection{(iii) Volumetric--wrong-internal pair}

\[
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{vol,wrong},\rho}
\le
\mathcal D_{\mathrm{vol,wrong},\rho}
+
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\mathcal M_{\mathrm{vol,wrong},\rho}^{JJ}
+
\frac{|\alpha_X\beta_X|}{M_X^2}\mathcal M_{\mathrm{vol,wrong},\rho}^{JK}
+
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\mathcal M_{\mathrm{vol,wrong},\rho}^{KK}.
}
\]

\paragraph{Direct source.}
\(\mathcal D_{\mathrm{vol,wrong},\rho}\) comes from direct volumetric coupling to the wrong-internal branch.

\paragraph{Heavy-mediated source.}
The \(\mathcal M_{\mathrm{vol,wrong},\rho}^{UV}\) terms come from mediated exchange between the volumetric and wrong-internal sectors.

\subsection{(iv) Higher-shell--same-shell non-enriched pair}

\[
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{high,non},\rho}
\le
\mathcal D_{\mathrm{high,non},\rho}
+
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\mathcal M_{\mathrm{high,non},\rho}^{JJ}
+
\frac{|\alpha_X\beta_X|}{M_X^2}\mathcal M_{\mathrm{high,non},\rho}^{JK}
+
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\mathcal M_{\mathrm{high,non},\rho}^{KK}.
}
\]

\paragraph{Direct source.}
\(\mathcal D_{\mathrm{high,non},\rho}\) is the direct inter-shell transport coupling between higher-shell modes and same-shell non-enriched modes.

\paragraph{Heavy-mediated source.}
The \(\mathcal M_{\mathrm{high,non},\rho}^{UV}\) terms come from mediator exchange between these two shell sectors.

\subsection{(v) Higher-shell--wrong-internal pair}

\[
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{high,wrong},\rho}

\mathcal D_{\mathrm{high,wrong},\rho}
+
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\mathcal M_{\mathrm{high,wrong},\rho}^{JJ}

\frac{|\alpha_X\beta_X|}{M_X^2}\mathcal M_{\mathrm{high,wrong},\rho}^{JK}

\paragraph{Direct source.}
\(\mathcal D_{\mathrm{high,wrong},\rho}\) comes from direct shell-changing internal misalignment couplings.

\paragraph{Heavy-mediated source.}
The \(\mathcal M_{\mathrm{high,wrong},\rho}^{UV}\) terms come from Class II-mediated transport with one leg in the higher-shell branch and one leg in the wrong-internal branch.

\subsection{(vi) Same-shell non-enriched--wrong-internal pair}

\eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho}

\mathcal D_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho}

\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\mathcal M_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho}^{JJ}

+

}
\]

\paragraph{Direct source.}
\(\mathcal D_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho}\) is the direct same-shell internal mixing between the non-enriched branch and the wrong-internal branch.

\paragraph{Heavy-mediated source.}
The \(\mathcal M_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho}^{UV}\) terms are the corresponding Class II-mediated internal/off-diagonal transport couplings.

\section{4. Compact six-pair master bound}

Combining all six unique pairs, we obtain

\boxed{
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
\le

(\mathrm{high,wrong}),
(\mathrm{non,wrong})

This is the explicit pairwise audit formula for the truncated remote budget.

\section{5. Gate-1 master margin in fully expanded pairwise form}

\section{Final summary}

The truncated remote budget is fully resolved into six unordered sector pairs:
\[
(\mathrm{vol,high}),
(\mathrm{vol,non}),
(\mathrm{vol,wrong}),

where:

\item \(\mathcal M_{ab,\rho}^{JJ}\), \(\mathcal M_{ab,\rho}^{JK}\), \(\mathcal M_{ab,\rho}^{KK}\) are the three heavy-mediated Class II budgets.

Therefore

\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}

+

\right].

Combining this with the tail and diagonal budgets, the full Gate-1 sufficient condition becomes

\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
>
2\sum_{(ab)\in\mathfrak P_6}
\left[
\mathcal D_{ab,\rho}
+
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\mathcal M_{ab,\rho}^{JJ}
+

+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
\]

Thus Gate 1 has now been reduced to a finite six-pair source audit plus tail/diagonal remainder bounds.

\section{Direct non--wrong mixing}

The direct mixing operator is
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{dir}}^{\mathrm{non,wrong}}
=
Q_{\mathrm{non}} V^\mu_\perp \partial_\mu Q_{\mathrm{wrong}}.
}
\]

Using the TD/DT result,
\[
V^\mu_\perp
=
\theta'(\xi)
\left[
C_E E^\mu_a \Sigma_a
+
C_O J^\mu_a \Sigma_a
\right],
\]
we obtain
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{dir}}^{\mathrm{non,wrong}}
=
\theta'(\xi)
\left[
C_E\, Q_{\mathrm{non}}(E^\mu_a \Sigma_a)Q_{\mathrm{wrong}}
+
C_O\, Q_{\mathrm{non}}(J^\mu_a \Sigma_a)Q_{\mathrm{wrong}}
\right]\partial_\mu.
}
\]

\section{Heavy-mediated non--wrong mixing}

The mediated contribution is
\[
\boxed{
Q_{\mathrm{non}}\Delta_X Q_{\mathrm{wrong}}
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
Q_{\mathrm{non}}
(\alpha_X \mathcal J + \beta_X \mathcal K)
(\alpha_X \mathcal J + \beta_X \mathcal K)^\dagger
Q_{\mathrm{wrong}}.
}
\]

Expanding,
\[
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\Bigl[
\alpha_X^2 Q_{\mathrm{non}}\mathcal J\mathcal J^\dagger Q_{\mathrm{wrong}}
+
\alpha_X\beta_X Q_{\mathrm{non}}(\mathcal J\mathcal K^\dagger+\mathcal K\mathcal J^\dagger)Q_{\mathrm{wrong}}
+
\beta_X^2 Q_{\mathrm{non}}\mathcal K\mathcal K^\dagger Q_{\mathrm{wrong}}
\Bigr].
\]

\section{Final bound for non--wrong mixing}

Combining the direct and mediated contributions, we obtain
\[
\boxed{
\eta_{\mathrm{non,wrong},\rho}
\le
\kappa\,\rho\,(|C_E|+|C_O|)
+
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\left(
\alpha_X^2 + |\alpha_X\beta_X| + \beta_X^2
\right).
}
\]

\section{Final Gate-1 condition (fully explicit)}

A sufficient condition for Gate 1 is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
>
2\left[
\kappa\,\rho\,(|C_E|+|C_O|)
+
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\left(
\alpha_X^2 + |\alpha_X\beta_X| + \beta_X^2
\right)
\right]
+
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho}.
}
\]

\section{Actual next target: extract the enriched shell Dirac carrier}

The current most useful direction is not further polishing of the TD/DT summary or further expansion of the remote-gap bookkeeping.
According to the current notes, the actual completion criterion is finite and concrete:
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
\to
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
\to
P_*K_iP_*
\to
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
}
\]

Therefore the next nonredundant task is to construct the enriched shell carrier explicitly.

\section{1. Shell-projected operator}

Let
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)-H_{\Psi X}(k)H_{XX}(k)^{-1}H_{X\Psi}(k)
\]
be the current refined locked + Class II effective Bloch operator.

Choose the resonant shell \(S_*\) around the folded Bragg point \(k_*=G_*/2\), and define
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}(p)
:=
P_{S_*}^{(N)}\,H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k_*+p)\,P_{S_*}^{(N)},
\qquad |p|\le \rho.
}
\]
Here \(P_{S_*}^{(N)}\) is a finite shell truncation retaining the enriched harmonics needed for the low Dirac carrier.

\section{2. Enriched shell decomposition}

The shell space is decomposed as
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}
=
\mathcal H_D^{(N)}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)},
}
\]
where

\begin{itemize}
\item \(\mathcal H_D^{(N)}\) is the enriched \(4\)-dimensional Dirac carrier candidate,
\item \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}\) is the same-shell complement.
\end{itemize}

This is exactly the practical route stated in the notes: construct \(H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}(p)\), identify the enriched \(4\)-dimensional Dirac carrier, then treat the complement as the same-shell non-enriched slot. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

Let
\[
P_D^{(N)}
\]
be the orthogonal projector onto \(\mathcal H_D^{(N)}\), and
\[
Q_{\mathrm{non}}^{(N)}:=P_{S_*}^{(N)}-P_D^{(N)}.
\]

\section{3. The shell-core Hamiltonian}

Define the enriched shell-core block
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(p)
:=
P_D^{(N)}\,H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}(p)\,P_D^{(N)}.
}
\]

By the current shell-Dirac notes, the correct canonical target form is
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{\mathrm{can}}(p)
=
E_*(p)\mathbf 1_4
+
m\,\tau^1\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
v_\parallel p_\parallel\,\tau^3\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
\tau^1\otimes\bigl(p_1W^1+p_2W^2\bigr)
+
O(|p|^2).
}
\]
The shell block becomes a massless Dirac principal symbol if and only if:
\[
\boxed{m=0,}
\]
\[
\boxed{v_\parallel\neq 0,}
\]
\[
\boxed{
W^1,\ W^2\ \text{are traceless Hermitian, nonzero, and linearly independent.}
}
\]
After internal basis reduction this becomes
\[
\boxed{
W^1=\nu_1 s^1,\qquad
W^2=\nu_2 s^2,\qquad
\nu_1\nu_2\neq 0.
}
\]
These are exactly the shell-level Dirac carrier conditions isolated in the notes. 

\section{4. Why this is the real frontier}

The notes are explicit that the remaining open step is not another abstract witness theorem, but the finite enriched Bloch calculation:
\[
\boxed{
\text{construct }H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k),\ H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p),\ P_*K_iP_*,\ \text{and extract }(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
}
\]
Moreover, the same-shell non-enriched slot is already reduced to one concrete finite matrix plus one perturbative radius estimate. 

Therefore the real next theorem target is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{construct }H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(p)\text{ explicitly and show that it satisfies }m=0,\ v_\parallel\neq0,\ W^1,W^2\text{ full-rank.}
}
\]

\section{5. Finite computation protocol}

The actual finite computation is now:

\begin{enumerate}
\item construct \(H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)\) from the refined locked + Class II branch;
\item choose the near-resonant harmonic set \(S_*\);
\item build \(H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}(p)\);
\item identify the enriched \(4\)-dimensional candidate carrier \(\mathcal H_D^{(N)}\);
\item compute
\[
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(0)
\]
and check whether the constant mass term \(m\) vanishes;
\item compute
\[
K_i^{(N)}:=\partial_{p_i}H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(0);
\]
\item decompose the linear symbol into
\[
v_\parallel,\qquad W^1,\qquad W^2;
\]
\item verify
\[
v_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
W^1,W^2\ \text{Pauli-full-rank}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

After that, one no longer reproves the general Dirac theorem.
One simply reads off
\[
\lambda_\parallel,\qquad \alpha,\qquad \beta
\]
from the three Pauli projections.

\section{6. Repositioning Gate 1 correctly}

Gate 1 should now be viewed as a support condition:
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\Longrightarrow
\text{the enriched shell carrier is spectrally isolated from the remote sector.}
}
\]
It is necessary, but it is not the actual last frontier.
The actual frontier is the explicit calculation of the enriched shell-core symbol itself.

\section{7. Honest current status}

The correct current status is therefore:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the reduced anisotropic Dirac architecture is already known abstractly;
\item the refined locked + Class II branch is the correct current microscopic branch;
\item the same-shell non-enriched problem is already reduced to a finite Hermitian matrix benchmark;
\item the genuinely remaining central task is to compute the enriched shell-core block and extract
\[
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
\]
\end{enumerate}

So the program should now push the enriched shell carrier directly.

\section{Final summary}

The most useful next step is not further TD/DT polishing and not further expansion of Gate 1 bookkeeping.

The actual completion criterion, according to the current notes, is the finite enriched Bloch calculation
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
\to
H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}(p)
\to
\mathcal H_D^{(N)}
\to
P_*K_iP_*
\to
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
\]

The enriched shell core must be put into the canonical form
\[
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{\mathrm{can}}(p)
=
E_*(p)\mathbf 1_4
+
m\,\tau^1\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
v_\parallel p_\parallel\,\tau^3\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
\tau^1\otimes(p_1W^1+p_2W^2)
+
O(|p|^2),
\]
and the actual Dirac carrier conditions are
\[
m=0,\qquad
v_\parallel\neq 0,\qquad
W^1,\ W^2\ \text{traceless Hermitian and linearly independent.}
\]

Gate 1 remains necessary, but only as a support theorem guaranteeing that the enriched shell carrier is spectrally isolated.
The real frontier is the explicit evaluation of the enriched shell-core block and the extraction of the three coefficients
\[
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
\]

\section{PROJECT: TECT --- Master Contents for Continuation (Enriched Shell Dirac Carrier Stage)}

\section{Current Main Goal}

The current main goal is no longer to polish support theorems in isolation.
The actual frontier is now:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{construct the enriched shell Dirac carrier explicitly and extract }
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)
\text{ from the refined locked + Class II branch.}
}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, the main completion chain is

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
\;\longrightarrow\;
H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}(p)
\;\longrightarrow\;
\mathcal H_D^{(N)}
\;\longrightarrow\;
P_*K_iP_*
\;\longrightarrow\;
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
}
\end{equation}

This is the current nonredundant target.

\section{What is structurally already fixed}

\section{Working microscopic branch}

The current strongest explicit microscopic working branch is

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi,P]
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^aJ_i^a[\Psi,P]
+
\beta_X X_i^aK_i^a[P,\Psi].
}
\end{equation}

This is \emph{not} yet claimed to be the final complete TECT microscopic action.
It is the strongest explicit working microscopic ansatz currently available.

\section{Light/heavy reduction}

The exact reduced operator skeleton is already fixed:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal Y_{\rm eff}=L-KH^{-1}K^\dagger.
}
\end{equation}

In the Bloch/Class II realization this becomes

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)-H_{\Psi X}(k)H_{XX}(k)^{-1}H_{X\Psi}(k),
}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\Psi X}(k)=\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k).
}
\end{equation}

In the auxiliary heavy Class II truncation,

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{XX}(k)=M_X^2\mathbf 1_X.
}
\end{equation}

Therefore

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_X(k)
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\bigl(\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k)\bigr)
\bigl(\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k)\bigr)^\dagger.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Shell projection and valley extraction}

The shell-projected operator is

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
=
\Pi_{S_*}\,H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k_*+p)\,\Pi_{S_*}.
}
\end{equation}

The low-valley projector is defined spectrally as

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_*=\frac{1}{2\pi i}\oint_\Gamma (z-H_{\mathrm{shell}}(0))^{-1}\,dz.
}
\end{equation}

The projected transport matrices are

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_i
=
P_*
\left.\partial_{k_i}H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)\right|_{k=k_*}
P_*.
}
\end{equation}

In the adapted defect frame \((\hat n,e_1,e_2)\),

\begin{equation}
M_\parallel=\hat n_iM_i,\qquad
M_1=e_{1i}M_i,\qquad
M_2=e_{2i}M_i.
\end{equation}

Under the locked Pauli selection rule,

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_\parallel=\lambda_\parallel\sigma_3,
\qquad
M_1=\alpha\sigma_1+\beta\sigma_2,
\qquad
M_2=\alpha\sigma_2-\beta\sigma_1.
}
\end{equation}

Hence the extracted reduced coefficients are

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3M_\parallel),
}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_1M_1+\sigma_2M_2),
\qquad
\beta=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_2M_1-\sigma_1M_2).
}
\end{equation}

\section{Exact overlap normalization layer}

The Bloch/transport overlap constants are defined by

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=C_c\,g_c,
\qquad
\alpha=C_E\,g_E,
\qquad
\beta=C_O\,g_O.
}
\end{equation}

So

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c=\frac{\lambda_\parallel}{C_c},
\qquad
g_E=\frac{\alpha}{C_E},
\qquad
g_O=\frac{\beta}{C_O}.
}
\end{equation}

This normalization layer is exact once \(C_c,C_E,C_O\) are calibrated.

\section{Current honest status of the transverse sector}

The reduced anisotropic Dirac-type PDE form is already structurally fixed, but the microscopic transverse frontier must be stated honestly.

A naive local real Hermitian \(JK\) bilinear vanishes because

\begin{equation}
\{\Sigma_3,\Sigma_1\}=\{\Sigma_3,\Sigma_2\}=0.
\end{equation}

Therefore the genuine microscopic transverse frontier is the derivative-resolved shell audit:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{JK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0},
\qquad
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{KK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0}.
}
\end{equation}

However, within the current explicit LO/Class II realization, the TD/DT sector may still be used as a branch-level reduced summary:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_0^{(1)}=\frac12(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
o_0^{(1)}=\frac12(A_O+B_O),
}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\theta_0\kappa(A_E+B_E),
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{32}\theta_0\kappa(A_O+B_O).
}
\end{equation}

This TD/DT formula should be described only as a \emph{branch-level reduced transverse summary}, not yet as the unconditional final microscopic closure of the full TECT PDE.

\section{Single-defect constitutive/radial reduction}

A minimal working constitutive ansatz compatible with the locked BCC background has already been fixed.

The minimal microscopic multiplet is

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(P^A,\Psi,X_i^a).
}
\end{equation}

The defect-background first-order coefficients are

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K^0_{\rm def}(x)=z_0(\bar\sigma(x))\mathbf 1,
}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K^i_{\rm def}(x)
=
g_E^{\rm eff}(x)\Gamma^i
+
g_O^{\rm eff}(x)\epsilon_{i\ell m}\hat n_m\Gamma^\ell
+
g_c^{\rm eff}(x)\hat n_i\Gamma_{\hat n},
}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_E^{\rm eff}=v_\perp+3\chi_Xv_E^{(X)},
\qquad
g_O^{\rm eff}=3\chi_Xv_O^{(X)},
\qquad
g_c^{\rm eff}=v_c+3\chi_Xv_c^{(X)}.
}
\end{equation}

The effective mass profile is

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_{\rm eff}(x)=m(\bar\sigma(x))-3\chi_X(x)u_X(\bar\sigma(x)).
}
\end{equation}

After radial defect specialization, the canonically normalized single-defect operator becomes

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbb H_{\rm def}
=
-\frac{i\,g_R(r)}{z_0(r)}\Gamma_{\hat n}\partial_r
-\frac{i\,g_E(r)}{z_0(r)r}\Gamma_i^\perp\nabla_i^{S^2}
-\frac{i\,g_O(r)}{z_0(r)r}J_i(\hat n)\nabla_i^{S^2}
+
W_{\rm def}(r,\hat n),
}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
g_R(r)=g_E(r)+g_c(r).
\end{equation}

\section{Callias core and one-defect/one-mode criterion}

The graded Callias core is

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbb H_{\rm C}
=
-i\,a(r)\Gamma_{\hat n}\partial_r
+\frac{b(r)}{r}\Gamma_{\hat n}\mathcal D_{S^2}
-i\,\omega_r(r)\Gamma_{\hat n}
+\mu(r)\Gamma^\sharp,
}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a(r)=\frac{g_R(r)}{z_0(r)},
\qquad
b(r)=\frac{g_E(r)}{z_0(r)},
\qquad
\mu(r)=\frac{m_{\rm eff}(r)}{z_0(r)}.
}
\end{equation}

For each angular channel \(\kappa\), the real superpotential is

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W_\kappa^{\rm core}(r)=\mu(r)+\frac{\kappa\,b(r)}{r}.
}
\end{equation}

The protected-channel counting is controlled entirely by this real superpotential.
The odd tangential coefficient \(g_O\) changes only the phase of the radial generator and does not affect \(L^2\)-normalizability.

A working sufficient criterion for one defect / one protected mode is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mu_\infty>0,
\qquad
a_0>0,
\qquad
b_0>0,
\qquad
\frac{|\kappa_*|b_0}{a_0}>\frac12,
}
\end{equation}
together with competitor exclusion for all other projected channels.

\section{Remote-gap theorem and its correct role}

The full remote-gap sufficient criterion is

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho}.
}
\end{equation}

The current working benchmark side is

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}-\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\Biggr\}.
}
\end{equation}

The same-shell non-enriched entry has been reduced to a finite Hermitian eigenvalue problem:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}
\ge
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}.
}
\end{equation}

The residual side has been cleanly decomposed as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{R,\rho}
\le
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho},
}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
\le
2\sum_{(ab)\in\mathfrak P_6}
\left[
\mathcal D_{ab,\rho}
+
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\mathcal M_{ab,\rho}^{JJ}
+
\frac{|\alpha_X\beta_X|}{M_X^2}\mathcal M_{ab,\rho}^{JK}
+
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\mathcal M_{ab,\rho}^{KK}
\right].
}
\end{equation}

Gate 1 is necessary, but it is now correctly understood as a \emph{support theorem}:
it guarantees that the enriched low slot is spectrally isolated from the remote sector.
It is no longer the main frontier.

\section{What is actually finished}

The following are already structurally closed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the light/heavy Schur-complement reduction;
\item the refined locked + Class II working microscopic branch;
\item the shell projection and valley projector formalism;
\item the Pauli extraction formulas for \((\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)\);
\item the minimal constitutive/radial reduction;
\item the Callias-core one-channel criterion;
\item the remote-gap theorem and its benchmark/residual decomposition;
\item the reduction of the same-shell non-enriched benchmark to a finite Hermitian matrix problem.
\end{enumerate}

\section{What is still not finished}

The actual unfinished frontier is now very specific:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{explicitly construct the enriched shell core }H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(p)
\text{ and verify that it is a massless Dirac carrier.}
}
\end{equation}

This means:

\begin{enumerate}
\item build \(H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}(p)\);
\item identify the enriched \(4\)-dimensional Dirac carrier candidate \(\mathcal H_D^{(N)}\);
\item compute
\[
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(p):=P_D^{(N)}H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}(p)P_D^{(N)};
\]
\item extract the constant mass term \(m\);
\item compute the linear symbol coefficients \(v_\parallel,W^1,W^2\).
\end{enumerate}

The canonical target form is

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{\mathrm{can}}(p)
=
E_*(p)\mathbf 1_4
+
m\,\tau^1\otimes\mathbf 1_2
+
v_\parallel p_\parallel\,\tau^3\otimes\mathbf 1_2
+
\tau^1\otimes(p_1W^1+p_2W^2)
+
O(|p|^2).
}
\end{equation}

The explicit Dirac-carrier conditions are

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m=0,
\qquad
v_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
W^1,\ W^2\ \text{traceless Hermitian, nonzero, and linearly independent.}
}
\end{equation}

After that, the actual extracted coefficients \((\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)\) are simply read off from the Pauli projections.

The following are still branch-specific and not yet fully verified:

all hold together.
\end{enumerate}

The current main frontier is no longer support-theorem polishing.
It is the explicit enriched shell Dirac-carrier extraction:
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
\to
H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}(p)
